## Metabolic

# Exercise Accelerates Wound Healing and Decreases Local Inflammation in Old Mice

Todd Keylock², Jeffrey Woods, FACSM², Matt Wallig', Luisa DiPietro². 1University of Illinois, Urbana, IL. University of Illinois, Chicago, IL.

PURPOSE: The purpose of this study was to determine the effect of exercise on wound healing and inflammation in young and old Balb/cBy] mice. Our hypothesis was that exercise would decrease levels of inflammation in wound tissue, allowing healing to occur faster.

METHODS: Young (three months) and old (18-months) female Balb/cBy] mice were assigned to either exercise (Ex) or sedentary control (CON) group. EX mice were run on a motorized treadmill at a moderate intensity (approximately 70% of their V02 max; at 18m/min for young mice and 12 m/min for old mice) for 30 minutes a day for three days before wounding and five days afterwards. All mice were given 4 full thickness dermal wounds using a 3.5mm punch biopsy needle and wounds were photographed for 10 days to measure rate of wound healing, Changes in wound size were analvzed by repeated measure analysis of variance for group and interaction effects and independent t-tests for differences by day. After allowing the mice to heal, they were wounded again in different locations and wounds with surrounding tissue were harvested at one, three, or five days after wounding. Harvested wounds were made into homogenates and analyzed with the Bio-Plex cytokine assay for interleukin-1 (IL-1β), interleukin-6 (IL-6), keratinocyte chemoattractant (KC), monocyte chemorattractant protein-1 (MCp-1), and tumor necrosis factor alpha (TNF-a). Differences in cytokines between groups were analyzed by 2-way ANOVA.

RESULTS: No differences in wound size were found as a result of exercise in young mice (F(2,21) = 0.31; p = .736). However, exercise significantly decreased wound size in old mice when compared to sedentary control mice (F(1,38) = 6.33, p = .016). When expressed in terms of percent of original size, the length of time it took for wounds to contract by 20% was 2.5 days faster in EX than in CON, 1.5 days faster to contract by 40%, and 1.8 days faster to contract by 60%. Levels of some proinflammatory cytokines in wound tissue of exercised mice were significantly lower than control mice, including Mcp-1 (F(1,30) = 7.00 p=.013), TNF-a (F(1,30) = 12.93, p=.001) and KC (F(1,30) = 9.51, p=.004). No differences were found in IL-1β or IL-6.

CONCLusIoN: These data suggest that exercise accelerates the wound healing process in o mice, which is delayed, but not young mice, which display quick healing. In this study, exercise-associated decreases in levels of some inflammatory cytokines in wound tissue are associated with faster healing.

36

## Metabolic

# Calcineurin is a Positive Regulator of Muscle Fatty Acid Oxidation

Paul J. Schaeffer. Miami University, Oxford, OH.

Calcineurin (Cn) is a calcium, calmodulin dependent protein phosphatase implicated ir skeletal muscle and cardiac growth and metabolism programs. Calcineurin is activated by sustained elevation of intracellular calcium concentration, such as is seen in working muscle. Calcineurin has also been implicated in the fast-to-slow skeletal muscle fiber-type shift, typified by expression of slow type contractile proteins. To learn more about the metabolic targets of Cn in muscle, we investigated its actions in cardiac and skeletal muscle myocytes and in the hearts of mice in vivo. Adenoviral-mediated expression of constitutively active Cn (Cn\*) induced expression of peroxisome proliferator-activated receptor y co-activator 1a (PGC-1a), a transcriptional coactivator involved in the control of multiple cellular energy metabolic pathways. Transcriptional profiling studies demonstrated that Cn actives expression of numerous fatty acid oxidation (FAO) enzymes genes as well as the nuclear receptor, peroxisome proliferator-activated receptor a (PPARa). Increased PPARa gene expression provides one mechanism whereby cellular fatty acid utilizatior genes are selectively activated by Cn. Transfection experiments demonstrated that Cn directly activates the mouse PPARa gene promoter. Cn was also shown to directly activate a known PPARa target, muscle carnitine palmitoyltransferase I (M-CPT I), providing a second mechanism by which Cn activates genes of cellular fatty acid utilization. To assess the in vivo role of Cn in a loss-of-function model, cardiac specific Cnb1 (the regulatory subunit of Cn) null mice were generated (csCnb1/-). Expression of PGC-1a, PPARa and a target gene involved in mitochondrial fatty acid oxidation, medium chain acyl-CoA dehydrogenase, was significantly lower (\~30%) in csCnb1/ mice. Mitochondria were isolated from the hearts of csCnb1?" mice, incubated with media containing either pyruvate or palmitoyl-carnitine and respiration was determined. Mitochondria from csCnb1-7- mice showed a significant defect in state 3 respiration using palmitoyl-carnitine as substrate, but no difference from controls when respiring on pyruvate, consistent with our earlier observation of reduced expression of PGC-1a, PPARa and FAO enzyme genes. In contrast, expression of mitochondrial electron transport system genes were maintained in the hearts of the csCnb1'/- mice. These results indicate that Cn plays a key role in regulating muscle fatty acid oxidation and identifies pathway specific control of metabolic targets.

37

# Mechanical Ventilation-Induced Alterations in Diaphragmatic Akt Signalling and FOxo Activation

Keith C. DeRuisseau, Joseph M. McClung, Darin J. Falk, Melissa A. Whidden, Scott K. Powers, FACSM. University of Florida, Gainesville, FL.

PURPosE: Mechanical ventilation (MV) unloads the diaphragm and results in the rapid onset of diaphraqmatic oxidative stress, contractile dysfunction, proteolysis, and myofiber atrophy. We tested the hypothesis that prolonged MV would alter diaphragmatic protein kinase B (Akt) signalling to the forkhead box (FoxO) family of transcription factors METHoDs: To test this postulate, Sprague-Dawley rats were randomly assigned to one of three experimental groups: control, 6-hour MV, and 18-hour MV.

REsULTS: 18-hours of MV decreased diaphragmatic Type I, Type IIa, and Type IIx/IIb myofiber cross sectional areas. Prolonged MV (18hr) decreased cytosolic Akt activity (- 37%) in the diaphragm and coincided with increased activation of 4E-BP1 and decreased activation of p70s6kinase protein. Further, phosphorylation of diaphragmatic cytosolic FOXO1 decreased 25% and 30% with 6- and 18-hours of MV, respectively. Finally, nuclear FOXO1 protein abundance increased 30-40% with 6- and 18-hours of MV and coincided with increased FOxO1 transcriptional activation at both time-points, coNcLusIoNs: Collectively. these data are consistent with the concept that Mv-induced Akt-FOxC signallinq contributes to MV-induced diaphraqmatic myofiber atrophy. This work was supported by National Institutes of Health (R01 HL072789)

# Caspase-3 Regulation of Diaphragmatic Myonuclear Apoptosis during prolonged Mechanical Ventilation

Joseph M. McClung, Keith C. DeRuisseau, Andreas N. Kavazis, Darin J. Falk, Melissa A. Whidden, Scott K. Powers, FACSM, University of Florida. Gainesville, FL. Email: jmcclung@hhp.ufl.edu

PURPosE: Unloading the diaphraqm via mechanical ventilation (MV) results in a rapid decrease in mvonuclear content and diaphragmatic myofiber atrophy, We tested the hypothesis that caspase-3 activation is a critical component of the MV-induced myonuclear loss.

METHoDs: To test this postulate, Sprague-Dawley rats were randomly assigned to one of five experimental groups: control, 6-hour MV, 12-hour MV, 6-hour MV with a highly specific caspase-3 inhibitor (DEVD-CHO), and 12-hour MV with DEVD-CHO.

REsuLTs: Decreases in myonuclear content and increases in the number of terminal deoxynucleotidyl transferase (TdT)-mediated dUTP nick-end labeling (TUNEL) positive nuclei were observed in diaphragm muscle fibers following 6- and 12-hours of MV. DEVD-CHO administration attenuated the decrease in both myonuclear content and the increase in TUNEL positive myonuclei at both 6- and 12-hours of My, In addition, decreases in both Type I and Type IIa diaphragm myofiber cross sectional areas with 12-hours of MV were attenuated by DEVD-CHO administration.

coNcLustoNs: Collectively, these data support the hypothesis that caspase-3 activation is a critical component of myonuclear loss occurring during rapid MV induced myofiber atrophy.

This work was supported by National Institutes of Health (R01 HL072789).

## Metabolic

# Nitric Oxide Influences AMPK Activity and the Induction of GLUT4 mRNA in Skeletal Muscle

Vitor A. Lira, Ouinlyn A. Soltow, Jenna L. Betters. Jodi H. Long, David S. Criswell, FACSM University of Florida, Gainesville, FL Email: lirav@ufl.edu

BAckGRouND: The uprequlation of GLUT4 expression is an important exercise-induced adaptation leading to improved glucose disposal in skeletal muscle. We have observed that nitric oxide synthase (NOS) inhibition (non-isoform-selective or nNOS-selective) attenuates the induction of GLUT4 mRNA mediated by AICAR (5-aminoimidazole-4-carboxamide riboside, 1mM) in L6 myotubes. Therefore, we sought to test whether AICAR-induced AMPK activity (i.e. phosphorylation of the AMPK substrate, Acetyl CoA Carboxylase, p-ACC) in L6 myotubes is dependent upon endogenous NOS activity, and if exogenous NO is sufficient to induce p-ACC. Secondly. we examined whether nNOS inhibition would prevent AICARinduced upregulation of GLUT4 mRNA in rat skeletal muscle in vivo. METHoDS: L6 myotubes were treated for 1h with AICAR (1mM), L-NAME (N(G)-L-nitro-arginine methyl ester,100μM and 500 μM), AICAR + L-NAME, or the NO donor, SNAP (1μM and 10μM) Separately, sixteen female Sprague-Dawley rats (10 mo old) were injected IP with: saline (control), AICAR (0.5mg/g body weight), TRIM (1-(2-trifluoromethyl-phenyl)-imidazole, 50 mg/g body weight), or AICAR+TRIM, and the plantaris muscles harvested after 12h.

RESULTS: AICAR increased p-ACC by 2-fold (P<0.O5), while co-treatment with L-NAME prevented this effect. Additionally, SNAP (10uM) increased p-ACC by 50% (P<0.05). However, the effect of L-NAME and SNAP on p-AMPK was variable and not statistically significant. In vivo, GLUT4 mRNA in the plantaris muscle was increased \~80%, 12h after AICAR injection (P<0.01), while TRIM co-treatment inhibited this effect by \~50%. CoNCLusIoN: These results suggest that NO influences AMPK activity. Further, nNOS activity is required for the full effect of AICAR on GLUT4 mRNA in vivo. Funded by AHA Grant #05301 96N.

## Metabolic

# Passive Loading, a "Stretch" for Exercise-Induced Glucose Transport

Melissa A. Smith, Jennifer S. Moylan, Michael B. Reid. University of Kentucky, Lexington, KY. Email: masmit8@uky.edu

Contraction stimulates insulin-independent glucose transport by skeletal muscle. There are a multitude of contraction-induced changes in muscle that trigger increased glucose transport. Among these are increased production of reactive oxygen species (ROS) anc phosphorylation of p38 mitogen-activated protein kinase (MAPk) and AMP-activated protein kinase (AMpk). This study tested the hypothesis that passive oading, i.e., stretch. stimulates glucose transport in murine skeletal muscle. Our model proposes that stretchinduced glucose transport is mediated by ROS and phosphorylated p38 and AMPK. We measure oxidant activity by use of 2',7' dichlorofluorescein. AMpK and p38 phosphorylation were measured by immunoblotting with a phospho-specific antibody (Cell Signaling). Glucose transport was measured by uptake of deoxy-D[1,2-3H]glucose. We demonstrate that stretching murine extensor digitorum longus (EDL) 90 to 110% optimal length increases oxidant activity (150% control, p < 0.01). We show that stretching EDL 90 to 120% optimal length for one hour increases p38 and AMPk phosphorylation (250% and 164% control, p < 0.05). Preliminary data show that stretching EDL 90 to 120% optimal length for one hour increases glucose transport (220% control, p = 0.08; N=6). These data support passive loading as an alternative mechanism for insulin-independent glucose transport that produces changes in muscle parallel to those produced by contraction. Supported by DK 066232.

## Metabolic

## Predictors of Change in Insulin Sensitivity

Kim M. Huffman², Gregory P. Samsa², Cris A. Slentz, FACsM², Brian D. Duscha², Johanna L. Johnson², Brian Annex², Joseph A. Houmard, FACSM³, William E. Kraus, FACSM2 1Veterans Affairs Medical Center; Duke University Medical Center, Durham, NC. 2Duke University Medical Center, Durham, NC. 3East Carolina University, Greenville, NC. Email: huffm007@mc.duke.edu

PuRPosE: Insulin resistance is the central feature of the metabolic syndrome and type 2 diabetes mellitus, Aerobic exercise training can improve insulin resistance. Our objective was to determine predictors of change in insulin sensitivity with exercise training to obtain insights into the mechanisms of improved insulin action.

METHoDs: Insulin sensitivity was determined from a frequently sampled intravenous glucose tolerance test in 206 sedentary, overweight to mildly obese, dyslipidemic individuals that were randomized to six months of inactivity or exercise training.

REsuLTs: Using multiple linear regression analysis, we found that gender, use of hormone replacement therapy (HRT), subcutaneous adiposity change, weight change, plasma triglyceride concentration change, fitness (relative peak VO2) change, and capillary density (number of endothelial cells per skeletal muscle fiber) change combined to explain 18% of the variance in the change in insulin sensitivity (p<0.o05). In this model, gender and HRT were independent predictors (p<0.05 for each). When gender interactions were evaluated, the predictive capacity of the model increased from 18% to 32% (p<0.0002). In this model, gender, HRT, triglyceride change, gender x triglyceride change, gender x subcutaneous adiposity change, and gender x capillary density change were each independent predictors of change in insulin sensitivity (p<0.05 for predictors, p<0.10 for interaction terms). For women but not men, change in insulin sensitivity related to changes in plasma triglycerides and capillary density. In contrast, for men but not women, change in insulin sensitivity correlated with subcutaneous adiposity change. We verified these results with separate modeling for women and men. For women, we found that 40% of the variance in change in insulin sensitivity was accounted for by HRT use, triglyceride change and capillary density change. For men, subcutaneous adiposity change explained 10% of the variance in change in insulin sensitivity.

coNcLusIoNs: We have observed significant gender specificity in predictors for change in insulin sensitivity. These results imply that exercise training imposes improvements in insulin sensitivity mechanisms that are unique for women and men.

42

## Metabolic

# The Influence of Exhaustive Exercise and Glycogen Repletion on PGC-1alpha mRNA and Protein Expression

Anila S. Mathai, Arend Bonen, Carley R. Benton, D. L. Robinson, Terry E. Graham. University of Guelph, Guelph, ON, Canada. Email: anila.mathai@gmail.com

Altered substrate availability and muscle glycogen concentration may mediate exerciseinduced gene transcription in skeletal muscle during and following exercise. To determine the influence of prolonged exercise and rapid glycogen repletion on regulation of peroxisome proliferator-activated receptor-gamma co-activator-1alpha (PGC-1a), a nuclear co-activator involved in coordinating metabolic gene expression and mitochondria biogenesis, 7 male subjects (23 + 1.3 y, V02max 48.4 + 0.8 mL kg-1 min-1) completed 2 trials consisting of exhaustive cycling exercise (\~2h) at 65% VO2max followed by ingestion of either a high- (HC) or low-carbohydrate (LC) diet for the ensuing 52 h recovery period. Biopsies were taken at rest, exhaustion, and at 2-, 24-, and 52-h of recovery. Glycogen content remained depressed throughout recovery in LC (P<0.05), while returning to resting levels by 24 h of recovery in HC. Exercise induced a 6.2-fold increase in PGC-1a mRNA (P<0.05) that returned to resting levels within 24 h of recovery. There was also a 23% increase in PGC-1a protein (P<0.05) at the end of exercise, and it remained elevated for at least 24 h (P<0.05). While there was no direct treatment effect with HC vs. LC for PGC-1a mRNA, there were trends (P=0.11 and 0.06 in exercise and recovery, respectively) between the changes in glycogen and PGC-1a protein. PGC-1a protein content is increased by a single bout of exercise and its up-regulation may be associated with changes ir muscle glycogen stores.

# The Influence of the Adiponectin Gene Polymorphism SNP(276) on Adiponectin in Response to Exercise Training

Hu Huang1, Kaoruko Tada Iida1, Haruka Murakami², Yoko Saito², Takeshi Otsuki1, Motoyuki Iemitsu1, Seiji Maeda1, Hirohito Sone², Shinya Kuno1, Ryuichi Ajisaka1. University of Tsukuba, Tsukuba city, Japan. 2Ochanomizu university, Tokyo city, Japan. Email: koukohh@med.taiiku.tsukuba.ac.jp

PuRPosE: Adiponectin is an adipocytokine that is involved in insulin sensitivity. The adiponectin gene contains a single nucleotide polymorphism (SNP) at position 276(G/T) The GG genotype of SNP276(G/T) is associated with lower plasma adiponectin levels and a higher insulin resistance index. Therefore, we examined the influence of SNP276(G/T) on the plasma level of adiponectin in response to exercise training

METHoDS: Thirty healthy Japanese (M12/F18; 56 to 79 years old) performed both resistance and endurance training, 5 times a week for 6 months. The rate of work per kg of weight at double-product break-point (DPBP) was measured and Blood samples were obtained before and after the experiment. Plasma concentrations of adiponectin, HbA1c insulin, glucose, total-, high-density lipoprotein (HDL-), and low-density lipoprotein (LDL-) cholesterol, and triglyceride were measured. Genotypes of SNP276 were specified. Student's t test for paired values and unpaired values was used.

REsuLTs: After the 6-month training period, the rate of work per kg of weight at DPBP and the plasma HDL-cholesterol level were significantly improved (P<0.05), while no change was observed in the total plasma adiponectin level. However, the plasma adiponectin level in those with the GT+TT genotype had significantly increased (P<0.05) Additionally, the degree of the decrease in the HOMA-R level was significantly greater in the subjects with the GT+TT genotype than those with the GG genotype (p<0.05)

coNcLUsIoNs: Our results suggest that subjects with the genotype GT+TT at SNP276(G/T) have a greater adiponectin-related response to exercise training than those with the GG genotype.

## Metabolic

# Effects of Diathermy on Hsp70 Content in Human Skeletal Muscle

Philip Gallagher, Scott Richmond, Chad Touchberry, Tung Le, Phill Vardiman, David Carr University of Kansas, Lawrence, KS. Email: philku@ku.edu

Heat shock proteins are cytoprotective and have recently been shown to be involved in the repair process of myofibrils. Purpose: Thus, the purpose of this investigation was to determine whether short wave diathermy can increase heat shock protein 70 (Hsp70) content in skeletal muscle. Methods: Eight subjects (6 females and 2 males, 18-35 yrs) received a muscle biopsy from the v. lateralis of one leg and then underwent 20-minutes of short wave diathermy followed by 20 minutes of hot pack heating on the other leg Twenty-four hours following the diathermy session, another muscle biopsy was performed on the treated leg. Muscle samples were analyzed for Hsp70 content using western immunoblotting techniques. Images of the blots were obtained and analyzed using an Alpha Innotech imaging system. A paired t-Test was used to examine there were differences in Hsp70 content between the treated and untreated legs. Significance was set at P<0.05. Results: Twenty four hours following the diathermy treatment Hsp70 content was on average 92% higher compared to the untreated lea (P<0.05). All but one subject (-10%) had a higher level of Hsp70 in the treated leg. Conclusion: This is the first study to report the effects of diathermy on heat shock protein content in humans. These results indicate that short wave diathermy is an effective modality to induce Hsp70 in skeleta muscle.

Research supported, in part, by a University of Kansas General Research Fund grant (P. Gallagher), and a McNair Scholarship (T. Le)

## Metabolic

# The Effect of Voluntary Wheel Running on Muscle Mass, Mitochondrial Function and Oxidative Damage in Sod1-/- mice

Michael S. Lustgarten, Young C. Jang, Wook Song, Yuhong Liu, Anson Pierce, Eric deWaal, Asish Chaudhuri, Wenbo Oi Holly Van Remmen UTHSCSA. San Antonio, TX Email: uthscsaml@aol.com

An absence in a major antioxidant enzyme CuZnSOD (SoD1) leads to age-related muscle loss. Exercise training has been demonstrated to induce beneficial changes in both muscle mass and function. The aim of the present study was to examine the potential protective effect of long-term voluntary wheel running (VwR) on muscle mass, mitochondrial function (including ROS and ATP production, RCR), and, on oxidative damage markers (cytosolic protein carbonyls and tissue F2-isoprostanes) in old Sod1-/- mice (20 months of age). At three months of age, mice were randomly divided into four different aroups: WT and Sod1 (sedentary), and, WT and Sod1 (VwR), for a period of 15 months. Sod1" mice ran approximately 30% less than WT mice on a daily average. VWR induced positive changes in muscle mass in all three muscles studied (soleus, tibialis anterior and gastrocnemius) for both Sod1" and WT. When normalized to body weight (muscle mass/body weight), VWR increased the ratio for all three muscles, in both WT and Sod1/ mice. Mitochondrial ROS production was increased in untrained Sod1'/ when compared to WT, either during State 1 (no exogenously added substrate) or when using Complex I or II specific substrates (glutamate/malate or succinate + rotenone, respectively). However, in response to long term VWR mitochondrial ROS production was reduced in State1 and glutamate/malate supported respiration (but not with succinate + rotenone) for the Sod1" mice. These changes would suggest a beneficial effect on mitochondrial function. but ATp production rates and RCR (State 3/State4) were measured to be unchanged. VWR had no effect on oxidative damage to protein as measured by the levels of cytosolic protein carbonyls in WT animals, but resulted in an increase in this parameter in muscle from the Sod1' mice. Oxidative damage to lipids, as measured by the levels of F2-isoprostanes, was increased in muscle from Sod mice when compared to WT, regardless if trained or sedentary. VWR did not induce further increases in F2-isoprostane levels in any of the measured groups Collectively, these data suggest that although VWR reduced ROS production by Sod17- mitochondria, elevated levels of oxidative damage may play a role in the discovered limitation in voluntary wheel running.

Supported by NIH P01 AG20591 (H.V.R.), MDA Grant MDA3879 (H.V.R.), and ACSM(TeXas) SRDA to YCJ

## Metabolic

# Isolated Mitochondrial Palmitate Oxidation is not Impaired with Obesity

Graham P. Holloway², A. Brianne Thrush², George J.F. Heigenhauser, FACSM², Narendra N Tandon², Jorge Calles-Escandon, Jan F.C. Glatz², Joost J.F.P. Luiken5, David J. Dyck Arend Bonen², Lawrence L. Spriet, FACSM}, 2University of Guelph, Guelph, ON, Canada. McMaster University, Hamilton, ON, Canada. 3Otsuka Maryland Medicinal Laboratories, Rockville, MD. 4Forest University School of Medicine and Baptist Medical Center, Winston-Salem, NC. 5Maastricht University, Maastricht, The Netherlands. Email: ghollowa@uoguelph.ca

PuRPosE: Numerous studies have suggested that obesity is associated with skeletal muscle mitochondrial dysregulation, reducing the capacity to oxidize fatty acids and ultimately shifting the fate of fatty acids to favor storage, Elevations in the content of intramuscular triacylglycerides (IMTG), and the associated increases in diacylglycerides (DAG) and ceramides, have been associated with an attenuation in insulin siqnaling, and subsequently been shown to be strong predictors of insulin resistance. While previous research has focused on the ability of whole muscle to oxidize fatty acids, the purpose of the present study was to ascertain the ability of skeletal muscle mitochondria isolated from obese subjects to oxidize fatty acids.

METHods: Rectus abdominus muscle was sampled from nine lean (age; 47±3 yrs, mass; 59.7±2.0 kg, BMI; 23.3±0.7 kg/m²) and nine obese (age; 45±3 yrs, mass; 99.2±6.8 kg, BMI; 37.6±2.2 kg/m²) women. A portion of muscle was homogenized and used to determine maximal citrate synthase (CS) and β-hydroxyacyl-CoA dehydrogenase (β-HAD) activities. The majority of the muscle was then used to isolated viable mitochondria, and to determine palmitate oxidation rates and fatty acid transport protein contents through Western analysis.

RESULTS: Obesity decreased (P<0.05) CS and β-HAD activity by 34% and 17%, respectively. CS siqnificantly correlated with BMI (r=-0.53), however B-HAD did not (r=. 0.31). Palmitate oxidation did not differ between lean and obese individuals (59±4 vs 69±9, nmol/mg protein/hour), nor did the content of mitochondrial fatty acid translocase (FAT)/CD36 (100±16 vs 120±17, arbitrary units) or fatty acid binding protein (FABP) (100±17 vs. 93±8, arbitrary units). However, regardless of BMI classification, palmitate oxidation significantly (P<0.01) correlated with FAT/CD36 content (r=0.67), but did not with FABP content (r=0.42). CoNCLuSIoNS: It is concluded that reductions in fatty acid oxidation that have been reported with obesity result from decreases in mitochondria volume, and not from an inability of remaining mitochondria to oxidize fatty acids. This research was supported by NSERC and CIHR.

# Investigation of the role of AMPK in Mitochondrial Biogenesis of Skeletal Muscle

Megan E. Osler, Pablo Garcia-Roves, Juleen R. Zierath. Karolinska Institutet, Stockholm, Sweden. Email: megan.osler@ki.se

Activation of 5'-AMp-activated kinase (AMPk) has been suggested to contribute to the requlation of insulin-independent qlucose transport in skeletal muscle in response to exercise/contraction or factors that induce metabolic stress. Microarray data comparing the white gastrocnemius muscle of AMPKy3 mouse models (y3subunit mutant transgenic and y3 knock-out) show opposite changes of expression of genes essential to mitochondrial biogenesis, including many PGC-1a-regulated genes (JBC 281(11):7244-52, 2006). Thus, we hypothesize that AMPk signaling acts through mitochondrial genes to mediate an increase in insulin sensitivity, making AMPk a good therapeutic target for Type 2 diabetes To unravel how AMPk exerts its beneficial effects on skeletal muscle metabolism, we have designed experimental protocols to address the connection between AMPk and mitochondrial biogenesis. To this end, we will utilize skeletal muscle specific mutant or wild-type AMPKy3 transgenic mice and AMPKy3 knockout mice and analyze mitochondria behavior following several distinct metabolic manipulations. To assess the contribution of AMPKy3 alterations to PGC-1a activation and mitochondrial biogenesis, we will measure potential changes in mitochondrial biogenesis in skeletal muscle of AMPky3 transgenic (mutant and wild-type) and knockout mice before, and following the exposure of animals to high fat feeding (to induce insulin-resistance) and chronic exercise (treadmill running). Following each of these studies, an analysis of mitochondrial histology will be performed using confocal and electron microscopy. Preliminary results suggest that no fiber type change has occurred due to genetic manipulation of AMpk and the multifaceted mitochondrial analysis is underway. Finally, depletion of PGC-1a, a key player in mitochondrial biogenesis, in vivo by electroporation of PGC-1a shRNA into AMPK mouse models will probe the connection of AMPK to mitochondrial activity. Understanding the relationship between AMPk and mitochondrial biogenesis will undoubtedly clarify the importance of AMPK in beneficial exercise-induced metabolic changes and potentially revea additional therapeutic targets for the pharmacological treatment of Type 2 diabetes.

# An Initial Phase of Phosphocreatine Recovery after Exercise with Flow Occlusion can be Explained by Glycogenolysis

Ronald Meyer1, Jill M. Slade², Theodore F. Towse², Jennifer Olive². 1Michigan State University, East Lansing, MI. 2University of Louisville, Louisville, KY.

PURPosE: Classic studies (e.g., Sahlin, et al, Scand. J. Clin. Lab Invest. 39:551, 1979) suggested that phosphocreatine (PCr) resynthesis in human muscle after exercise is entirely dependent on oxidative metabolism. These results reinforce the view that glycogenolytic flux is strongly dependent on feedforward activation by calcium or other signals associated with contractile activity. In contrast, recent modeling studies (e.g., Lambeth and Kushmerick, Ann. Biomed. Eng. 30:808, 2002) suggest that the observed dependence of glycogenolysis on contractile activity is explained by strong coupling of the pathway to ATPase rate via classic feedback mechanisms. According to this modeling, glycogenolytically-driven PCr recovery ought to be observed under some conditions.

METHoDs:In this study, PCr resynthesis after 1 min of repetitive isometric ankle dorsiflexion exercise was measured in anterior tibial muscle of human subjects (n=4) by 31P-NMR spectroscopy (51.7 MHz, TR 3s) via a

small surface coil under 3 conditions: no occlusion, partial flow occlusion (120 Torr cuff placed above knee). and near complete occlusion (160-180 Torr cuff).

RESULTS: As expected, PCr recovery after exercise with no occlusion followed an exponentia time course (see Fiqure top panel). In contrast, recovery during partial occlusion was biphasic, with a brief fast phase, followed by linear PCr recovery, During near-comnlete occlusion onl the brief, fast-phase of PCr recovery was observed. These three patterns of PCr recovery could be mimicked by a metabolic model in which glycogenolytic rate depends solely on changes in cytoplasmic AMP and inorganic phosphate (see Figure bottom panel)

CoNcLusIoN: The results suggest that PCr recovery in human muscle is not entirelv dependent on oxidative metabolism, and that feedforward mechanisms are not required tc explain control of muscle glycogenolysis.

# Linear Relation Between Time Constant of $\pmb { 0 } _ { 2 }$ Uptake Kinetics and Mitochondrial Content In Vitro

Brian Glancy², Thomas Barstow, FACsM², Wayne Willis, FACSM². Arizona State University, Tempe, AZ, 2Kansas State University, Manhattan, KS

In 1988, Meyer (Am J Physiol 254:C548, 1988) proposed a model in which oxidative phosphorylation is represented by an RC electrical circuit. In this model, the time constant for O uptake (J.) is given by $\vdots T = R _ { \Pi } C$ , where the mitochondrial resistance to energy transfer (Rm) is viewed to be a function of the number and properties of mitochondria in the cell, and the metabolic capacitance (C) is proportional to the cellular total creatine pool $( \mathsf { T C r } = \mathsf { \dot { P } C r } + \mathsf { C r } ) .$ , In a previous experiment in which we respired isolated mitochondria in a novel in vitro system, we observed that T does indeed vary linearly with the TCr added to the respiration medium. PURPOSE: To assess whether the mass of mitochondrial protein added to the respiratory chamber also elicits the predicted proportional changes in T. METHoDS: Rat mixed hindlimb skeletal muscle mitochondria (n=3 separate preparations) were isolated and added in aliquots of varying protein content (0.1 to 0.7 mg) to 2.0 ml KCI-based medium. All incubations contained 5.0 mM ATP, 150 U creatine kinase, an ATPsplitting system of glucose + hexokinase (HK), and pyruvate (1 mM) + malate (1 mM) as oxidative substrates. TCr was present at one of two levels, 0.15 or 0.30 mM. J at steady state $\langle \mathsf { J } _ { \circ ( \mathsf { s s } ) } \rangle$ was deterrmined from HK additions in the absence of a creatine pool in separate incubations. In the presence of varying mitochondrial content, Jort) was measured across time after HK addition sufficient to elicit 40% state 3 Jo. T was evaluated according $\mathsf { t o } \mathsf { J } _ { \circ ( \mathrm { t } ) } = \mathsf { J } _ { \circ ( \mathsf { s s } ) } ( 1 - \mathsf { e } ^ { - \mathsf { t } / \mathsf { T } } )$ RESULTS: T decreased linearly with increasing mitochondrial content (R{ = 0.999 for 0.15 mM TCr and ${ \ R } ^ { 2 } = 0$ for 0.0 mM TCr Moreover, the slope of the T:Rm line varied according to the TCr in the system; when TCr was doubled from 0.15 to 0.30 mM, the T: Rm slope was 1.82 times greater. CONCLUsIONS: These in vitro results are consistent with the concept that mitochondria in the presence of TCr + creatine kinase respond to a step change in ATP demand with a T that conforms to the behavior of an RC electrical circuit, T = RmC. Specifically, the present results indicate that the resistance term, $\mathsf { R } _ { m _ { \prime } }$ is inversely proportional to mitochondrial content. Supported by NSF IBN-0116997

## Metabolic

## Functional Characteristics of Subsarcolemmal and Intermyofibrillar Mitochondria Isolated from H-FABP Deficient Mice

Vladimir Ljubicic1, Peter J. Adhihetty1, Keir J. Menzies1, Bert Binas², Arend Bonen³, David A. Hood, FACSM1. York University, Toronto, ON, Canada. Texas A&M University, College Station, TX. 3University of Guelph, Guelph, ON, Canada

Subsarcolemmal (SS) and intermyofibrillar (IMF) mitochondria are two morphologically distinct subfractions located in different regions of the myofiber, possessing disparate biochemical properties which may contribute to their adaptive potentials. Although mice lacking the skeletal muscle cytosolic fatty acid (FA) transporter heart-type fatty acidbinding protein (H-FABP) exhibit abnormal FA metabolism, it is unknown how SS and IMF mitochondria adapt functionally to this deficit. PuRposE: To investigate the compositior and function of SS and IMF mitochondria isolated from WT compared to H-FABP KC animals. METHoDS: SS and IMF mitochondria were isolated from muscle of WT and H-FABP KO animals and cardiolipin content was assessed using flow cytometry. State 3 (active) and state 4 (passive) mitochondrial oxygen consumption (Vo2) was measured. Fluorometric and flow cytometric techniques were used to measure mitochondrial reactive oxygen species (RoS) generation and membrane potential. Mitochondrial permeability transition pore (mtPTP) opening kinetics, including the maximal rate of pore opening (Vmax) and the time required to achieve Vmax, were also assessed. REsuLTs: Cardiolipin content was similar between SS and IMF mitochondria isolated from WT and H-FABP KO mice. IMF mitochondrial VO2 was 1.5- and 2-fold greater compared to SS during state 4 and state 3 respiration, respectively. IMF mitochondrial ROS production, along with membrane potential, were 35-70% lower compared to the levels in SS mitochondria in both WT and H-FABP KO mice. ROS generation during SS state 3 respiration was 30% higher in H-FABP KO compared to WT animals. mtPTP Vmax was 2.7-fold higher in IMF mitochondria compared to the SS subfraction isolated from WT and H-FABP KO mice. Time to Vmax in IMF mitochondria harvested from H-FABP KO mice was 40% greater compared to WT littermates. In addition, within the H-FABP deficient genotype, time to Vmax was 66% higher for the IMF subfraction compared to SS mitochondria. coNcLusIoN: These findings reveal unique adaptive strategies between SS and IMF mitochondria due to an alteration in FA handling. The data demonstrate an association between high rates of mitochondrial VO2, low membrane potential, and reduced levels of ROS production in IMF mitochondria, while the inverse appears to hold for the SS subfraction. Further, SS mitochondria upregulate ROS production as a potential signal to increase the transcription of other genes, possibly involved in FA metabolism. The IMF subfraction demonstrates a reduced susceptibility to mitochondrially-mediated apoptosis, a protective adaptation to possible lipotoxic conditions within the myocyte.

## Metabolic

## Effects of the Antidiabetic Drug Metformin on Maximal Aerobic Capacity

Brooke R. Stephens, Todd A. Hagobian, Carrie G. Sharoff, Pamela N. Eze, Benjamin Goldstein, Stuart R. Chipkin, Barry Braun, FACSM. University of Massachusetts, Amherst MA.

Email: brstephe@kin.umass.edu

Metformin is a commonly prescribed antidiabetic drug that promotes normoglycemia mainly by decreasing liver glucose production. Metformin has been shown to inhibit Complex 1 of the electron transport system, reducing mitochondrial oxidative phosphorylation (OxPhos). Lower capacity for OxPhos is expected to constrain maximal aerobic capacity $( V O _ { 2 m a x } )$ . This impact on VOzmax is clinically relevant given that the prediabetic and diabetic individuals prescribed metformin are also encouraged to be physically active. Purpose: To examine the effects of metformin on VO2max as well as maximal heart rate $( \mathsf { H R } _ { \mathsf { m a x } } )$ and ventilation $( \mathsf { V E } _ { \mathsf { m a x } } ) .$ Methods: Using a randomized, counterbalanced, placebo-controlled design, 7 healthy, normoglycemic men and women $( 3 3 . 6 \pm 3 . 9 \ \forall \Gamma \mathsf { S } )$ underwent an initial VOzmax test after at least 3 days stabilization at the typical clinical dose of metformin (20o0 mg/day) or placebo (single-blind). Following at least 7 days of the alternate treatment, subjects underwent a second VO2max test. Each continuous exercise test was conducted on a cycle ergometer or treadmill and commenced at a low work rate with incremental increases in treadmill grade or ergometer resistance until a maximal voluntary effort was achieved. Gas exchange measurements were obtained continuously throughout the test by open-circuit spirometry. HR was measured by telemetry using a Polar monitor. Results: After treatment with metformin, absolute (L/min1) and relative (mL/kg $^ 1 / \mathsf { m i n } ^ { - 1 } ) \mathsf { V O } _ { 2 \mathsf { m a x } }$ were consistently lower relative to placebo (- 4.7 ± 1.6% and -4.6 ± 1.5%, respectively). In addition, HRmax (bpm"1) and $\mathsf { V E } _ { \mathsf { m a x } } ^ { \mathsf { ^ { * } } } ( \mathsf { L } / \mathsf { m i n } ^ { \mathsf { ^ { * } 1 } } )$ were lower after metformin treatment compared to placebo $( - 4 . \dot { 0 } \dot { \pm } 0 . \dot { 8 }$ and -7.7 ± 1.8%, respectively). Maximal work output achieved was the same across conditions and mean test duration was 15.2 ± 1.1 min"1 on placebo versus 14.5 ± 0.7 min"1 with metformin treatment. Conclusion: Treatment with metformin appears to lower $\mathsf { V O } _ { 2 \mathsf { m a x } _ { t } } \mathsf { H R } _ { \mathsf { m a x } _ { t } }$ and $V E _ { m a x } .$ We hypothesized that $\mathsf { V O } _ { 2 \mathsf { m a } }$ ;would be lower with metformin treatment due to reduced OxPhos from the inhibition of Complex 1. However, because HRmax was also lower with metformin, it is unclear whether the decrease in $\mathsf { V O } _ { 2 \mathsf { m a y } }$ , is a result of central or peripheral factors, or both. These findings may have clinical relevance qiven the millions of people who are prescribed metformin and also encouraged to be physically active. This study was supported by a grant from the American Diabetes Association

## Metabolic

## Nitric Oxide Is Involved In Basal But Not Acute Exercise-Induced Mitochondrial Biogenesis In Skeletal Muscle

Glenn Wadley, Glenn McConell. The University of Melbourne, Melbourne, Australia Email: gdwadley@unimelb.edu.au

BAckGRouND: Recent findinas suggest the endothelial nitric oxide synthase (eNOS) and neuronal Nos (nNos) isoforms may be differentially involyed in the basal regulation of mitochondrial biogenesis in skeletal muscle (1, 3). Since NOS activity increases during contraction in skeletal muscle (2) NO may be involved in exercise-induced mitochondrial biogenesis.

PURPosE: To determine if 1) basal levels of mitochondrial biogenesis mRNA markers are reduced in skeletal muscle of mice deficient in eNOs (eNOs') or nNos (nNos') and 2) increases in mitochondrial biogenesis mRNA markers are attenuated in the skeletal muscle of eNOs or nNos/ mice following acute exercise.

METHoDS: Male C57BI6 (CON), eNOS-/ and nNOS-/- mice (16.3 ± 0.2 weeks old) either rested in their cages or ran on a treadmill (16 m/min, 5% grade) for 60 min (n=8 per group). Six hours after the cessation of exercise (or rest), mice were killed. RNA was isolated from the soleus using Trizol and real-time PCR was performed with all genes normalized to B2-microalobulin.

REsuLTS: Soleus eNOS expression was similar in CON and nNOS/ mice and nNOs expression was similar in CoN and eNos/ mice (no compensation evident). Compared with CON mice, eNOS mice had significantly (P<0.05) lower basal PGC1a mRNA (31%), higher basal PGC1β mRNA (24%) but similar basal NRF1, NRF2a, mtTFA and COX I1I mRNA expression. Compared with CON mice, nNOS-/ mice tended to have higher basal PGC1B mRNA (23%, P=0.08) and significantly (P<0.05) higher basal NRF1 (69%). NRF2a (47%) and mtTFA (32%) mRNA. Basal PGC1a and COX III mRNA were not significantly different in nNOs/" mice to CON mice.

Compared with rested mice, PGC1a mRNA was significantly increased six hours after exercise in all groups (P<0.05, \~2-fold) with no significant differences between groups. Exercise did not significantly increase NRF1, NRF2a, mtTFA, PGC1β or COX III mRNA in any of the groups.

coNcLusIoN: The eNOS and nNOS isoforms appear to be differentially involved in the basal regulation of mitochondrial biogenesis in soleus muscle. Surprisingly, nNoS and eNOS deficiency in skeletal muscle are both associated with increased basal PGC1B mRNA. However only nNOS/ mice display increased NRF1, NRF2a and mtTFA mRNA, possibly since eNOS/ mice also have diminished basal PGC1a mRNA (may counteract the higher PGC1β mRNA). It appears that eNOS and nNOS are not critical for acute exercise-induced increases in mitochondrial biogenesis since exercise increased PGC1a mRNA expression normally in the soleus of eNOSand nNOs" mice.

## REFERENCES:

3. Schild et al. FASEB J 20: 145-7, 2006.

## Metabolic

# UCP3 Attenuates Mitochondrial H2O2 Production in Skeletal Muscle During Recovery from Exercise

Ethan J. Anderson1, Hanae Akeda-Yamazaki1, Darrell Neufer². 1Yale University, New Haven, CT. 2John B. Pierce Laboratory. New Haven. CT. Email: ethan.anderson@yale.edu

Metabolic states requiring an increased reliance on fatty acid oxidation in skeletal muscle are associated with increased expression of mitochondrial uncoupling protein 3 (UCP3). Although the function of UCp3 is still a matter of considerable debate, a leading hypothesis suggests that UcP3 may attenuate mitochondrial oxidant production under metabolic states that lead to elevated ROS production, In this study, 2h of low-intensity exercise followed by food restriction (0h -18h recovery; 18h-48h food provided) was used to increase endogenous expression of UCP3 protein in red (type II oxidative; RG) and white (type II glycolytic; WG) gastrocnerius muscle of Sprague-Dawley rats. UCP3 mRNA peaked 4h after exercise at \~8-fold over basal (non-exercised controls) in RG, and \~20- fold over basal in WG (P<0.05). UCP3 protein expression peaked 18h into fasting postexercise at \~1.7-fold and \~3-fold over basal in RG and WG, respectively (P<0.05). To investigate UCP3 function, permeabilized fiber bundles were prepared from RG and WG 18h after exercise (Ex/F) and mitochondrial state 4 respiration and H>O, emission were assayed and compared to rates from identical, non-exercised control preparations. To maximize endogenous ROS production (putative activator of UcP3), experiments were conducted under state 4 conditions with succinate as substrate in the presence or absence of GDP (UCP3 inhibitor). Mitochondrial state 4 H>O emission (pmol H>O2·min"1·mg dry weight-1) was significantly higher in the presence of GDP only in Ex/F preparations in both RG (90.3 ± 7.1 vs 69.9 ± 3.7 , +/-GDP) and WG (76.3 ± 6.0 vs 51.9 ± 4.7, +/-GDP). H>O> emission averaged \~45 and \~58 in control RG and WG, respectively, regardless of the presence or absence of GDP. State 4 respiration was also increased by \~28% in RG and 50% in WG from Ex/F only in the absence of GDP (P<0.05). A GDP-inhibitable increase was not observed in controls. In additional experiments conducted with the physiological fatty-acid substrate palmitoyl-L-carnitine, mitochondrial state 4 H2O2 emission (pmol H2O2-min"1-mg dry weight"1) was also significantly higher in the presence of GDP only in Ex/F preparations in both RG (13.6 ± 0.4 vs 6.0 ± 1.8, +/-GDP) and WG (13.4 ± 0.8 vs 4.1 ± 1.4, +/-GDP). Using an in-situ model of mitochondrial function, these data provide evidence that induction of UCP3 in a physiological context attenuates mitochondrial H2O2 emission and increases state 4 respiration, consistent with its putative role in protecting against conditions associated with elevated ROS production.

# VO2 Kinetics and PDH Activation Slowed in Old Adults During the to Moderate Exercise

Brendon J. Gurd², Sandra J. Peters², George JF Heigenhauser²³, Paul J. Leblanc², Tim J Doherty², Donald H. Paterson, FACSM1, John M. Kowalchuk². 1The University of Western Ontario, London, ON, Canada. Brock University, St Catharines, ON, Canada. 3McMaster University, Hamilton, ON, Canada. Email: bgurd@uwo.ca

Introduction: Older adults demonstrate slower on-kinetics than younger adults during the transition to moderate-intensity exercise (Delorey et al., J App/ Physiol 97:165, 2004) Although the mechanism for this slower response is not established, it may be related to slower activation of enzymes and provision of oxidative substrates to the energy producting pathways in the mitochondrion, to inadequate muscle blood flow and mitochondrial O2 delivery, or both. The purpose of this study was to examine the activation of mitochondrial pyruvate dehydrogenase (PDHa) during the transition to moderate-intensity exercise in both young and old adults. Methods: Healthy young (YA; n=7; age, 24 (3) yrs; peak, 51 (3) mL•kg min1; mean (± SD)) and older adults (OA; n=6; age, 78 (2) yrs; peak, 31 (4) mL•kg perfomed  tnsitons t a moderatntensity work at coespondig  0% of estimated lactate threshold (θ.). Each transition lasted 6 min and was preceded by 6 min baseline cycling at 2ow. Muscle biopsies were taken from the vastus lateralis muscle at baseline and at 30 s and 6 min of the exercise transition. Results: The adaptation of the fundamental, phase 2 VO2 response was faster in YA (T, 21 (6) s) than OA (T, 40 (16) s). In YA, baseline PDHa activity was 1.09 (0.6) mmol acetyl CoA•min"•kg ww1 and by 30 s exercise, PDHa activity had increased (P<0.05) to 2.05 (0.2) mmol acetyl CoA•min-1kg ww1 and showed no further change at 6 min (2.07 (0.3) mmol acetyl CoA•min"1•kg ww-1). In OA, PDHa was 1.25 (0.2) mmol acetyl CoA•min"1•kg ww"1 at baseline, was unchanged at 30 s (1.56 (0.6) mmol acetyl CoA•minkg ww1), but was significantly increased (P<0.05) by 6 min exercise (2.24 (0.4)). Conclusion: The slower activation of PDH in OA compared to YA is consistent with the slower VO2 kinetics being limited, in part, by a metabolic inertia Iocated at the mitochondrial PDHa, which [imits the delivery of carbohydrate-derivec substrate (NADH; acetyl CoA) to the tricarboxylic acid cycle and electron transport chain. ## Metabolic

## Muscle Bioenergetics during Exercise Recovery

Youngran Chung², Paul Mole1, Tuan-Khanh Tran1, Napapon Sailasuta², Kazumi Masuda³, Ralph Hurd², Thomas Jue. University of California Davis, Davis, CA. GE Medical Systems, Inc, Fremont, CA. 3Kanazawa Univeristy, Kanazawa, Japan. Email: yrchung@ucdavis.edu

Four untrained young adult men participated in a study to investigate the bioenergetics of muscle contraction after plantar flexion exercise at 0.75, 0.92, and 1.17 Hz and a constant load. Indirect calorimetry measured whole body O uptake. 31p NMR assessed the time course of high energy phosphate levels and intracellular pH changes. 1H NMR followed the kinetics of intracellular oxygenation with the deoxy Mb proximal histidyl NaH signal. During recovery from three different exercise intensities, the 1H NMR signal of deoxy Mb disappears with a time constant (T) T = 16-22s. VO2 and PCr recover more slowly, T = 73- 133s and T = 39-67s, respectively. The VO2 and PCr kinetics appear uncoupled with the O supply. An analysis of the VO2 as a function of PO2 confirms that VO2 rises as PO2 falls. Moreover, an Eadie Hofstee analysis shows that PCr resynthesis also does not depend upon PO2. In fact, the ATP generated by VO2 exceeds the energy demand of PCr resynthesis, which consumes only 22-58% of the available oxidative ATP. The PCr resynthesis rate then does not accurately reflect oxidative metabolic capacity. The study proposes that glycogen resynthesis utilizes the available energy during postexercise recovery and creates the energy demand that drives the excess post exercise oxygen consumption (EPoC), commonly designated with the oxygen debt metaphor. Lactate serves as a likely fuel source for oxidative phosphorylation.

## Metabolic

# Convective, Diffusive, and Metabolic Limitations Of Oxygen In Canine Muscle: In Vivo vs. In Silico Studies

Nicola Lai, Gerald M. Saidel, Marco E. Cabrera, FACSM. Case Western Reserve University, Cleveland, OH. Email: nicola.lai@case.edu

Experimental approaches have been used to investigate factors requlating muscle O, uptake (VmO2) dynamics during exercise, such as the dynamics of convective O2 delivery and diffusion and the mitochondrial rate of oxidative phosphorylation. Understanding the role of these factors in health and disease is important to improve functional capacity in subjects with chronic cardio-respiratory disorders. Despite characterization of VmO2 dynamics during exercise (Fick principle). a controversy remains with respect to the main source of limitation in the adjustment of VmO under a variety of conditions A computational model of O2 transport and utilization in skeletal muscle which incorporates convective, diffusive and reaction processes of O2 in blood and tissue cells was developed and applied to predict muscle dynamic responses to changes in blood flow over a range of arterial O, concentrations during the transition from rest to various levels of exercise. The mathematical model validity as well as its predictive capability is demonstrated by a direct comparison between experimental data (O2 a-v differences) and model results from canine muscle during exercise. Model simulations confirm that neither convective nor diffusive O, delivery affects muscle O2 uptake dynamics during the transition from rest to exercise corresponding to 60-70 % of maximal VO2. From analysis of model simulations, it was possible to deterrine the extent to which convective, diffusive, and/or reactive processes limit muscle function under various conditions. Supported by grant (P50 GM-66309) from the National Institute of General Medical Sciences (NIH)

## Metabolic

# Adiponectin Resistance Develops in Rat Soleus Muscle in Response to High-Fat Diets

Kerry L. Mullen, Kathryn A. Junkin, Angela C. Smith, David J. Dyck. University of Guelph, Guelph, ON, Canada Email: mullenk@uoquelph.ca

High-fat diets have been shown to induce insulin resistance (IR). High-fat diets have also been shown to produce skeletal muscle resistance to leptin, a recognized insulin-sensitizing cytokine. Similar to leptin, adiponectin (Ad) is a stimulatory cytokine, known to enhance fatty acid (FA) oxidation. However, it is unknown if Ad resistance develops in skeletal muscle following high-fat feeding, and if Ad resistance is a precursor to the ensuing dietinduced IR. The purpose of this study was to determine whether Ad's stimulatory effects on muscle alucose and lipid metabolism would be reduced after exposure to different high-fat diets, and if this Ad resistance was independent of the development of IR. Rats were fed a control (12% kcal fat, CON), high-unsaturated fat (60% kcal safflower oil, SAFF) or high saturated fat diet (60% kcal lard, LARD) for 4 weeks. Following the dietary intervention, glucose uptake and lipid oxidation and esterification was measured in the presence and absence of Ad (2.5ug/ml) in resting, isolated soleus muscle. All 3 groups had similar rates of basal glucose uptake, but LARD rats showed siqnificantly reduced rates of insulin stimulated alucose uptake compared to CON and SAFF (+68%, v5. +172%, +184% p= O.oo1). Ad had no effect on basal or insulin-stimulated glucose uptake in any of the diet treatments. With respect to lipid metabolism, the CoN group had a significantly lower basal FA oxidation rate (34.4±2.8 nmol/g vs. 49.8±3.5 SAFF, 46.4±3.4 LARD, p<0.03), and triglyceride esterification (TG) (47.6±3.3 nmol/g vs. 67.9±5.8 SAFF, 66.8±3.4 LARD, p<0.o1), compared to both high fat groups, suggesting a diet-induced adaptation by the SAFF and LARD group to the higher fat availability. Ad significantly increased FA oxidation within CoN rats (+28%, p=0.03), but had no stimulatory effect on FA oxidation in either high-fat group. Additionally, the FA oxidation: TG esterification ratio in the CoN group (0.93±0.1) was greater than both SAFF and LARD (0.56±0.05, 0.68±0.07, p<0.04) when all groups were exposed to Ad. Therefore, we conclude that Ad's ability to stimulate FA oxidation and repartition FA away from storage is blunted in soleus muscle of rats fed either a high saturated or unsaturated fat diet for 4 weeks. In contrast, only rats fed a hiqh saturated fat diet developed IR. We hypothesize that as a result of high-fat feeding, skeletal muscle may become Ad resistant. However, it is unclear whether Ad resistance necessarily leads to IR. Further studies are warranted to determine the long-term effect of polyunsaturated fat on insulin sensitivity.

## Emphysema-Induced Reductions in Diaphragm Mass

John P. Mattson. FAcsM1 , Richard T. Hinkle², Robert J. Isfort². Leonardo E. Ferreria³ Timothy 1. Musch, FACSM³, David C. Poole, FACSM3. 1Gustavus Adolphus College, St. Peter MN. 2Proctor & Gamble Pharmaceuticals, Mason, OH. 3Kansas State University, Manhattan, KS.

Email: jmattson@qustavus.edu

Profound diaphragm adaptations occur secondary to chronic lung hyperinflation in emphysema (EMP). Specifically, in EMP diaphragm oxidative capacity and fiber cross sectional area are elevated whereas fiber length is reduced via sarcomere loss. However, the consequence of EMP-induced hyperinflation on diaphragm mass remains poorly understood. PURPOSE: To investigate the effect of EMP on diaphragm mass. METHODS: Male Syrian golden hamsters were either sacrificed at 4 or 8 months following intratracheal instillation of either saline (CON=10) or elastase (25 units/100 g body weight, EMP=15) RESULTS: The presence of EMP (P<0.01) was verified visually and by measurement of excised lung volume (4-month: CON=1.6±0.3 g; EMP=4.0±1.2 and 8-month: CON=1.84±0.5 g; EMP=4.8±1.3). There were no differences in costal diaphragm mass ater 4-months CON=144±22 EMP=140±32, mg) of EMP. However, there was a significant decrease (P<0.01) in costal diaphragm mass after 8-months of EMP (CON=275±54 EMP=221±33, mg) which was correlated with disease severity (r=-.65 P<0.01, Figure). CoNCLUSION: These findings support the notion that EMP per se can induce decrements in diaphragm mass which might contribute to respiratory limitations ir this patient population. Therapeutic interventions that maintain diaphragm mass may therefore prove beneficial in EMP.

## Pulmonary

# Activity-dependent Protein Ubiquitination in Diaphragm Muscle

Nathan J. Hellyer, Carlos Mantilla, Eunice Park, Wen-Zhi Zhan, Gary C. Sieck. Mayo Clinic College of Medicine, Rochester, MN. Email: hellyer.nathan@mayo.edu

PuRPosE: The diaphragm muscle (DIAm) is the most important inspiratory muscle with a high duty cycle (\~40%) relative to limb muscles such as the soleus (\~14%) or extensor digitorum longus (\~2%). In this regard, DIAm cross-sectional area, tetanic force, and myosin heavy chain expression have been observed to be particularly sensitive to inactivity. Two distinct types of rat DIAm inactivity were investigated in this study, namely spinal isolation (SI) by hemisection of the spinal cord at C2 and unilateral phrenic nerve denervation (DNv). With SI, excitatory respiratory drive to the phrenic motor neurons is absent resulting in muscle paralysis. With DNV, there is a complete neuromuscular disruption resulting in muscle paralysis. In both cases, the diaphragm is mechanically unloaded and not mediating contractions. Therefore, the major difference between SI and DNV is the disruption of neuromuscular interactions. The purpose of this study was to investigate the state of protein ubiquitination as an indicator of DIAm protein degradation and to elucidate whether the degree of ubiquitination varies following two different conditions of DIAm inactivity (SI versus DNV).

METHoDs: Sprague-Dawley rats underwent SI, DNV, or sham surgery. DIAm was removed at three, seven, or fourteen days post surgery, homogenized, and protein analyzed by SDS-PAGE and immunoblotting techniques. Metamorph software was used to quantitate proteins immunoreacting with ubiquitin-specific antibodies.

REsuLTS: DIAm protein ubiquitination increased following DNV surgery. Compared to sham-treated animals, ubiquitination increased approximately four, ten, and seven-folc following three, seven, or fourteen days of DIAm DNV. In contrast, there was no apparent change in protein ubiquitination following SI at each of the three times points analyzed

CoNCLusIoNs: The findings in this study are consistent with prior reports that DIAm cross-sectional area, tetanic force, and myosin heavy chain expression significantly decrease acutely following DNV, but do not significantly decrease following SI. This observation further emphasizes the critical role of neuromuscular interactions for DIAm homeostasis bevond maintenance by mechanical contraction per se. We hypothesize that neuromuscular interactions, such as trophic factor signaling, may delay protein ubiquitination and resultant muscle deficits following acute periods of inactivity.

## Pulmonary

# Effect of Inspiratory Muscle Work on Peripheral Locomotor Muscle Fatigue in Hypoxia

Markus Amann, David F. Pegelow, Jerome A. Dempsey, FACSM. University of Wisconsin, Madison, WI. Email: amann@wisc.edu

The work of breathing required during heavy intensity exercise in normoxia compromises blood flow to the working limb exaggerating peripheral locomotor muscle fatigue. During exercise in hypoxia, ventilation and the work of breathing is significantly increased over normoxia. Purpose: We asked if the high force output of the inspiratory muscles experienced during heavy intensity exercise in hypoxia further affected exercise-induced peripheral muscle fatigue and consequently exercise performance as compared to exercise in normoxia. Methods: To determine exercise-induced peripheral fatigue, potentiated quadriceps twitch force $( \mathsf { Q } _ { \mathsf { c w } , \mathsf { p o t } } ) ,$ in response to supramaximal single magnetic stimuli of the femoral nerve (1 Hz), was assessed pre- and 2.5 min post-exercise. Eight cyclists exercised to exhaustion in hypoxia (8.6 ± 0.5 min, 273 W, F1O2 0.15, SpO2 81%) at \~83% peak power output in hypoxia (HYPO). On a second occasion, subjects exercised for the same duration and power output as HYpo, but force output of the inspiratory muscles was reduced by 69% using a proportional assist ventilator (HYPO-PAV). On further occasions, subjects repeated both trials in normoxia (without and with inspiratory muscle unloading) The force output of the inspiratory muscles was 25 ± 4% greater in hypoxia vs. normoxia. Finally, to reveal the effects of inspiratory muscle work on exercise performance ir hypoxia, subjects exercised at the same workload to exhaustion in hypoxia (10.0 ± 0.9 min, SpO2 81%) while force output of the inspiratory muscles was again reduced via PAV. Results: Immediately after HYPO exercise, Qtw,pot was reduced by 30 ± 3% below preexercise baseline and this reduction was attenuated following the HYPO-PAV exercise (21 ± 4%; P < 0.05). When the identical exercise was repeated in normoxia, ΔQtw,pot was only reduced by 17 ± 3% below pre-exercise baseline and this reduction was similar when the inspiratory muscles were unloaded (16 ± 2%, P = 0.6). Time to exhaustion in hypoxia increased by 16 ± 3% when the inspiratory muscles were unloaded (8.6 vs. 10.0 min, p < 0.01). Conclusions: In conclusion, peripheral quadriceps fatigue induced via high-intensity sustained exercise in hypoxia is, to a significant extent, due to the accompanying high levels of respiratory muscle work. As a consequence, the WOB during high intensity exercise imposes a significant limitation to exercise performance in hypoxia.

## Pulmonary

# Does Lung Size Affect Pulmonary Gas Exchange During Exercise?

I. Mark Olfert, Markus Flatz, Tatsuya Arai, Peter D. Wagner, Susan R. Hopkins. UCSD, La Jolla, CA. Email: molfert@ucsd.edu

Pulmonary gas exchange may be impaired during intense exercise, however the individual response is highly variable. Even among subjects of similar aerobic fitness, alveolar arterial difference for oxygen (AaDO) may vary 5 fold. It has been suggested that lung size may be an important factor determining the pulmonary gas exchange response to exercise. We hypothesized that if lung size (represented by forced vital capacity, FvC) and aerobic fitness (maximal oxygen consumption, VOzmax) are both taken into account, individuals with small lunas relative to aerobic fitness would experience greater gas exchange impairment during exercise compared to those with larger lungs relative to fitness. Using the multiple inert gas elimination technique we studied 6 male subjects with FvC/VO2max ratio < 1.3 (defined as small lungs relative to VOmax, S) and compared indices of gas exchange (AaDO2; arterial PO2, and logSDQ) at rest and during cycle egometry at 30%, 60%, and 90% of VO2max in normoxia against data from subjects (n=21) with a FVC/VO,max ratio >1.3 (defined as large lungs relative to VO,max, L). Neither, VO,max (S= 4.0±0.2 vs. L= 3.5±0.2 L/min, p=0.12) nor FVC (S= 4.9±0.3 vs. L= 5.5±0.2, p=0.13) were significantly different in S compared to L. However, % predicted of FVC was lower in S compared to L (S= 95±5 vs. L= 113±3 %, p<0.05). Durinq heavy exercise (90% VO2max), PaO2 was significantly lower (96.7±2.7 vs. 104.7±1.8, p<0.05) and AaDO; was greater (27.3±3.3 vs. 15.5±1.6, p<0.05) in S compared to L, respectively. Ventilation-perfusion matching, assessed by logSDQ, was not different between S and L during exercise (S= 0.42±0.03 vs. L= 0.48±0.01, p=0.08), however measured-minuspredicted AaDO (an index of pulmonary diffusion limitation of O transport in the lung derived from the inert gas data) was greater in S compared to L (S= 13.5±2.4 S vs. L= 5.9±1.5 Torr, p<0.05) indicating significantly greater O diffusion limitation in the S group. These data demonstrate that individuals with small lungs relative to VO2max (FVC/VO2max ratio < 1.3) experience a greater degree of diffusion limitation during exercise compared tc those with larger lungs relative to VOmax. This suggests that the ratio of lung size (FVC) and VOmax may provide an index capable of predicting individuals susceptible to gas exchange impairment during intense exercise and who may experience exercise-inducec arterial hypoxemia. Funding support by NIH# MO1 RR000827 and AHA 0540002N

## Cardiovascular

# The Role of ASIC Channels in the Exercise Pressor Reflex

Shawn G. Hayes, FACSM, Angela E. Kindig, Jong Kyung Kim, Marc P. Kaufman. UC Davis, Davis, CA. Email: sghayes@ucdavis.edu

In vivo, H+ activate thin fiber muscle afferents involved in the exercise pressor reflex: however, the receptor for this effect is unknown. We hypothesized that the hydrogen ions associated with lactic acid accumulation in the exercising muscles act on ASIC channels on thin fiber muscle afferents. To test this hypothesis we examined if amiloride, an ASIC antagonist, attenuated the reflex pressor and cardioaccelerator responses to static contraction. stretch of the calcaneal tendon, as well as popliteal arterial iniections of lactic acid and capsaicin. We established a dose of amiloride that blocked the reflex pressor response to static contraction and lactic acid injection but had no effect on the reflex pressor responses to stretch and capsaicin injection. Specifically, in four decerebrate cats we examined the pressor and cardioaccelerator responses to static contraction, stretch of the calcaneal tendon, and popliteal artery injections of lactic acid (0.5 ml, 24mM; i.a) and capsaicin (2-5 ug; i.a.) before and after popliteal arterial injection of amiloride. The pressor responses to static contraction averaged 28 ± 4 mmHg before amiloride and 5 ± 2 mmHg after (0.5 µg/kg; i.a.; p = 0.09; n=4). Likewise, the pressor response to lactic acid injections averaged 30 ± 4 mmHg before amiloride and 12 ± 3 mmHg after (p= 0.06; n=4). The pressor responses to tendon stretch and capsaicin were unchanged by amiloride The heart rate responses were similar to those of blood pressure. In three separate decerebrate cats a high dose of amiloride (5 µg/kg) abolished all cardiovascular responses to static contraction, stretch of the calcaneal tendon, and injections of lactic acid and capsaicin. These data suggest AsIC channels may play a role in the exercise pressor reflex.

## Cardiovascular

## Leq Sympathetic Transduction and Vasoconstrictor Responsiveness Are Preserved in Older Women

Beth A. Parker, Sara S. Jarvis, Sandra L. Smithmyer, Samuel J. Ridout, David N. Proctor FACSM, James A. Pawelczyk, FACSM. The Pennsylvania State University, University Park PA. Email: bap202@psu.edu

PuRPosE: To determine the influence of age on the relationship between an acute sympathetic stimulation (cold pressor test, or CPT) and calf vascular resistance (CvR) in healthy women. METHods: Beat-to-beat blood pressure and heart rate (Colin), calf blood flow (venous occlusion plethysmography), and peroneal nerve muscle sympathetic nerve activity (MSNA) were assessed in 7 young (Y:24±5) and 7 older (O:66±3) women at rest, during CPT (3 min ice-water immersion of the dominant hand), and during 3 min recovery. CVR (mmHg/mL/1oomL/min) was calculated as the quotient of mean arterial pressure (MAP) and calf blood flow. MSNA was expressed as the sum of discharges per minute (total activity; U/min) and the frequency of discharges (burst frequency; bursts/min), with the former expressed as a percentage of peak values to account for between-subject differences in electrode placement. Vascular transduction of the sympathetic stimulus into the calf vasculature was calculated as the slope of the linear relationship between group averages of CVR and MSNA at rest, during CPT and during recovery. REsULTS: Data are expressed as group means ± S.E.M. MAP was always significantly higher in O during rest CPT and recovery; however, the change in MAP from rest to peak measured during CPT was similar (YΔMAP: 22.5±2.3 mmHg; OΔMAP: 24.9±2.6 mmHg; p=0.50). There were no age-group differences in CVR at any time. Resting MSNA was significantly higher in older women (Y: 13.8±2.9 bursts/min or 31.9±4.1%; 0: 28.5±2.9 bursts/min or 62.4±6.8 %; p < 0.01). While Y and O subjects exhibited similar peak MSNA during CPT (Y: 26.6±5.7 bursts/min; O: 36.3±2.3 bursts/min; p>0.60), Y had a significantly greater change in MSNA from rest to peak (YΔ MSNA: 12.7±3.6 bursts/min or 51.4 ± 7.9%; OΔ MSNA: 7.8±2.5 bursts/min or 20.7±10.1%; p<0.05). Additionally, transduction of the sympathetic stimulus was greater (CVR vs % peak MSNA: Y slope: 0.28; O slope: 0.41; p<0.01) with age. coNCLUsIoNs: Although the magnitude of change in MSNA during CPT was blunted with age, CVR increased similarly. These results suggest that sympathetically mediated vasoconstrictor responsiveness is maintained or possibly augmented in older women.

03

## Cardiovascular

# Reversibility of Exercise-Induced Neuroplasticity in Brain Cardiorespiratory and Locomotor Areas following Exercise Detraining

Amanda J. Nelson, Gary A. Iwamoto. University of Illinois @ Urbana-Champaign, Urbana IL.

Email: ajnelso1@uiuc.edu

puRPosE: It has been shown previously that dendritic branching in cardiorespiratory and locomotor brain areas can be attenuated with exercise training (ET). The purpose of this study was to determine if this process was reversible.

METHoDs: Twenty-three (n=23) male Sprague-Dawley rats were individually caged and divided into two groups, untrained (UN: n=11) and detrained (DTR: n=12). DTR were provided with a running wheel at 21 days of age and exercised spontaneously. After 120 days (70 days of ET followed by 50 days of detraining), ET indices were obtained, including: VO-max, percent body fat, resting heart rate, and heart weight-body weight ratios. The brain was processed according to a modified Golgi-Cox procedure. Impregnated neurons from the periaqueductal gray (PAG), posterior hypothalamic area (PH), nucleus of the tractus solitarius (NTS), and cuneiform nucleus (CfN) were examined in corona sections. Neurons were traced using a camera lucida technique and analyzed using the Sholl concentric ring analysis of dendritic branching. T-tests compared the mean number of intersections per neuron by grouping inner rings, outer rings and total number of intersections per animal

REsuLTS: There were no sianificant differences between UN and DTR in the PH, PAG, CfN. and NTS in the inner rings, outer rings and total number of intersections per animal. A separate group of animals was used to show that a training effect in the CfN and NTS was present at 56-days of ET. It could be reasonably assumed that had the DTR animals continued with exercise the dendrites would have demonstrated attenuation as shown in our previous study.

coNcLusIoNs: Our results show that dendritic attenuation, which could be assumed to result from 70 days of ET in PH, PAG, CfN, and NTS is completely reversed with 50 days of detraining.

# Effect of Age on Leg Vascular Responsiveness to Sympathetic Stimulation during Passive and Active Exercise

Dennis W. Koch1, Samuel J. Ridout², Cheryl A. Blaha², Cynthia S. Hogeman², Nicholas C. King², Lawrence I. Sinoway², Urs A. Leuenberger²2, David N. Proctor, FACSM1 1Pennsylvania State University, University Park, PA. Pennsylvania State University Hershey, PA.

Email: koch5@canisius.edu

BAcKGRouND: Functional sympatholysis, defined as reduced vascular responsiveness to sympathetic outflow in exercising vs. non-exercising muscles, may be reduced in the forearms of older vs. younger men and women. PurPosE: To extend these findings to the leg vasculature during active and passive exercise. METHoDs: Five younger (Y; 21-27 yrs) and three older (O; 62-78 yrs) healthy, recreationally-active men performed passive (KEpassive; limb moved by investigator) and active (KEactive) single leg knee extension exercise (40 contractions per min) in random order before, during, after acute sympathetic stimulation by ischemic handgrip to exhaustion (HG), followed by post handgrip circulatory arrest (POST HG). Heart rate (ECG), blood pressure (MAP; Finometer), femoral artery blood flow (FBF; Doppler ultrasound), and tissue oxygenation in the vastus lateralis muscle (near infrared spectroscopy) were measured continuously. REsULTS: MAP increased substantially from KE to POST HG in all tests, and these increases were larger in KEpassive vs. KEactive, and were also larger in younger vs. older men (Y KEactive: +18%; Y KEpassive: +42%; O KEactive: +11%; O KEpassive: +18%). Changes in FBF from exercise to POST HG were similar in younger and older men, but larger during KEpassive vs KEactive (Y KEactive: +4%; Y KEpassive: +35%; O KEactive: +11%; O KEpassive: +27%). Leg vascular conductance (LVC) decreased during sympathetic stimulation during all tests, but to a larger extent in younger men. Furthermore, decreases in LVC were similar between active and passive exercise (Y KEactive: -11%; Y KEpassive: -15%; O KEactive: -7%; O KEpassive: -5%). concLusIoNs: These preliminary results do not support our working hypothesis that sympathetic vascular responsiveness is greater in the leg vasculature of older men during KEactive. Funding: NIH RO1 AG018246 (DNP), RO1-HL-68699 (UAL), and M01-RR010732 (Hershey GCRC).

## Cardiovascular

# The Effect of an Intra-dialytic Exercise Program on Autonomic Nervious System Function in End-Stage Renal Disease Patients

Cheryl E. King-VanVlack1, Christopher Pawliuk², Matthew Orava³, Edwin Toffelmire1 1Queen's University, Kingston, ON, Canada. Queen's Univesity, Kingston, ON, Canada. 3McMaster University, Hamilton, ON, Canada. Email: kingce@post.queensu.ca

PURPosE: ANS dysfunction is common in end-stage renal disease (ESRD) and can be related to the level of uremic toxins; of which regular hemodialysis (HD) acts to minimize this effect. Previously, we have shown that intra-dialytic exercise (exercise during the HD procedure) can enhance the removal of toxins during HD by 20%. Therefore, we wished to determine if exercise during HD alters the level of autonomic nervous system (ANS) function in individuals with ESRD. METHoDS: HD patients exercised for 30 min in each of the first 2 hours of HD (Exercise Group,n=7, EX ) during the thrice-weekly HD sessions; 8 HD patients served as a control group (CoN). ANS function testing (5 standard cardiovascular tests) was performed prior to and following this 12-week exercise program. Each person was graded on a total ANS function scale out of 10 (0-2 for each test) with 0 meaning no autonomic neuropathy (AN) and 10 meaning severe AN. REsuLTS: In the EX group, subjects with or without AN, decreased their ANS function scores by -1.0±2.6 and - 1.0±1.6 respectively; no such decreases were observed in the CON group. When the ANS function scores were separated into sympathetic (SNS) and parasympathetic (PNS) function, a significant reduction in the PNS function score occurred in the EX group but not in the CON group. No changes were observed in SNS function scores in either group.

coNCLusIoNs: These data indicate that intra-dialytic exercise may improve ANS function by decreasing the amount of PNS dysfunction in individuals with ESRD. These improvements in ANS function have implications for cardiovascular and/or gastrointestinal function in ESRD since both systems are under the regulation of the ANS.
