## Cardiovascular

# WISE 2005: Does Cardiac Output Contribute to The Pressor Response During Isometric Handgrip Exercise in Humans?

J. Kevin Shoemaker², Louis Mattar², Pascaline Kerbeci³. Sarah Trotter1, Phillippe Arbeille³3. Richard L. Hughson². The University of Western Ontario, London, ON, Canada. University of Waterloo, Waterloo, ON, Canada. 3University Tours, Tours, France. Email: kshoemak@uwo.ca

PurPosE: The mechanism of the pressor response to metaboreflex activation remains in debate with proponents posing sympathetically-mediated increases in total peripheral resistance (TPR) or increases in cardiac output (Q) as the major determinants. Interindividual differences in such control are possible. Therefore, the purpose of this study was to test the hypothesis that elevations in Q determine the pressor response during fatiguing volitional exercise. METHoDS: 17 healthy women, (age = 32 yrs, height = 165 cm, weight = 59 Kg), performed two minutes of ischemic static handgrip exercise (SHG; 40% of maximal voluntary contraction force) while HR, stroke volume (Doppler), blood pressure (Finometer), and muscle sympathetic nerve activity (MSNA) were measured followed by the calculation of Q and TPR. 11 participants also performed 3 min of -45 mmHq lower body negative pressure (LBNP) and 5 minutes of 60 degrees head-up tilt (HUT) as control conditions where TPR responses were expected. RESULTS: Total MSNA increased above baseline by the second minute (P<0.05) whereas Q increased in each min of exercise (\~1 L/min; P<0.05). The average TPR was unchanged from baseline during SHG (n=17) but increased \~7 mmHg/L/min (P<0.05) during both LBNP and HUT (n= 11). Inter-individual differences were evident in SHG with elevated TPR observed in 9/1 7 individuals but no change or a decrease observed in the remaining participants (TPR was elevated in all 11 participants during LBNP and HUT). Concurrently, elevations in Q during the first and second minute of exercise were evident in 15/17 participants. cöNcLUsIoNs: The ability to elevate TPR was normal in these individuals. Nonetheless, the contribution of O and TPR to hemodynamic control during volitional ischemic SHG exercise was variable with the majority of the blood pressure response involving changes in cardiac output rather than TPR.

Supported by ESA, NASA, CSA and CNES and performed at MEDES, Institute for Space Physiology and Medicine in Toulouse, France.

## Cardiovascular

# Isometric Handgrip Training alters Oxidative Stress during an Ischemic Forearm Exercise Test

Mark Rakobowchuk1, Andrew S. Levy², James W.E. Rush², Cheri L.M. McGowan3³, Maureen J. MacDonald². 1McMaster University, Hamilton, ON, Canada. 2University of Waterloo, Waterloo, ON, Canada. 3University Health Network/University of Toronto, Toronto, ON Canada.

Email: rakobome@mcmaster.ca

Isometric handgrip training (IHT) has been previously shown to increase flow-mediated dilation in the brachial artery of the trained limb (McGowan et al. Am J Physiol, In press) Reduced oxidative stress resulting in increased nitric oxide availability is one potential mechanism for the increased dilation observed following this occlusive challenge.

puRposE: The aim of the present study was to evaluate oxidative stress during a forearm ischemic test (FIT) before, and after 8 weeks of IHT. METHoDs: Nine older adults completed 3 sessions of IHT weekly at 30% of their 1RM. Before and after training, each participant completed a FIT which involved 6 maximal contractions for 9 seconds with 1 second rest intervals with a forearm ischeric cuff in place located above the crease of the elbow. Handgrip force was recorded throughout the FIT protocol. Blood samples obtained from a catheter placed distal to the ischemia cuff were collected pre, and immediately (im. post.), and 1 minute post FIT. These samples were analyzed for malondialdehyde (MDA) via HPLC methodology. RESULTS: Results indicate a greater change in MDA prior to training at the immediately post and 1 minute post time points (rest: 16.85 ± 2.5 vs. im. post: 18.59 ± 2.7 vs. 1 min post 18.65 ± 2.5; µmol/L p<0.05) compared to no change after training (rest: 18.91 ± 3.3 vs. im. post: 18.42 ± 2.1 vs. 1 min post 17.55 ± 2.1 umol/L). Overall mean force during the FIT was higher following training (149.9 ± 23.7 vs. 182.2 ± 27.7 N, p=0.03). concLusIoN: These results suggest that greater vasodilatory responses following IHT may be related to reduced oxidative stress. This attenuated change in oxidative stress is observed despite greater muscle force, which likely induces greater reactive oxygen species production during the FIT protocol. In addition, one should note that contraction intensity during the FIT protocol in aged individuals, may not produce high levels of oxidative stress due lower muscle mass, when compared to previous studies performed in healthy young populations (Rodriquez et al. Med. Sci. Sports Exerc., 2o03).

## Cardiovascular

# Influence Of Age On Cardiac Baroreflex Sensitivity During Dynamic Exercise

James P. Fisher1, Abrar Ahmed1, Jasmine Nelson², Shigehiko Ogoh², Paul J. Fadel1 University of Missouri, Columbia, MO. University of North Texas Health Science Center, Fort Worth, TX. Email: fisherjp@health.missouri.edu

pURPosE: This study was desianed to beain to investigate age-related changes in baroreflex control of blood pressure during dynamic exercise. Although studies indicate that the blood pressure response to dynamic exercise is augmented in older individuals, the mechanisms responsible for this exaggerated pressor response remain unclear Because the arterial baroreflex is important for the normal regulation of blood pressure during exercise, we hypothesized that impaired baroreflex function contributes to the greater pressor response during dynamic exercise in older individuals.

METHoDS: We examined cardiac baroreflex sensitivity in 5 young (25±1 yr) and 5 older (57±1 yr) healthy subjects at rest and during low, moderate, and high intensity cycling exercise representing 30, 50, and 70% heart rate reserve, respectively. Blood pressure was measured beat-to-beat using finger photoplethysmography (Finometer) and every minute using an automated sphygmomanometer (SunTech). Transfer function analysis between the changes in systolic blood pressure (SBP) and heart rate in the low frequency range (0.07-0.2 Hz) were used to estimate cardiac baroreflex sensitivity.

REsuLTs: At rest, blood pressure was similar between the older and younger subjects. In contrast, resting cardiac baroreflex sensitivity was significantly lower in the older subjects (0.42±0.06 vs. 1.08±0.18 bpm/mmHg). During all exercise bouts the blood pressure responses were higher in the older subjects with the greatest difference being observec during high intensity exercise (SBP; 200±7 vs. 164±6 mmHg, p<0.01). However, cardiac baroreflex sensitivity was similar in the older and younger subjects during low (0.27±0.04 vs. 0.39±0.03 bpm/mmHg, p=0.2), moderate (0.17±0.04 vs. 0.13±0.02 bpm/mmHg p=0.7), and high intensity exercise (0.08 ± 0.02 vs. 0.09±0.01 bpm/mmHg, p=0.9).

coNcLusIoNs: In summary, our preliminary findings suggest that age-related alterations in cardiac baroreflex sensitivity do not appear to be involved in mediating the greater pressor response in older subjects during dynamic exercise.

# Effects of Forskolin on Inotropic Performance and Phospholamban Phosphorylation in Exercise-Trained Hypertensive Myocardium

Stephen C. Kolwicz, Hajime Kubo, Scott M. MacDonnell, Steven R. Houser, Joseph R. Libonati, Temnle University, Philadelnhia, PA

PuRPosE: β-adrenergic receptor (BAR) responsiveness is down-regulated in left ventricular (LV) hypertrophy induced by chronic hypertension. While exercise training in hypertension enhances BAR responsiveness, the role of adenylyl cyclase remains unclear. The purpose of the present study was to test whether treadmill running in the spontaneous hypertension rat (SHR) model improves LV responsiveness to forskolin (FOR) or the combination of FOR + isoproterenol (FOR+ISO). METHoDS: Female SHR (16-wks) were randomly placed into sedentary (SHR-SED, n= 7) or treadmill trained (SHR-TRD, n=8) groups. Wistar-Kyoto (WKY, n=7) animals acted as normotensive controls. Langendorff, isovolumic LV performance (Krebs buffer, 2 mM Ca²\*, LVEDP=10 mmHg) was established at baseline and during incremental FOR infusion (1 and 5 µmol/L) and FOR + ISO (5 μmol/L + 1\*10-8 mol/L, respectively).REsuLTS: Heart rate (HR), systolic blood pressure (SBP), and heart to body weight ratio were lower in WKY relative to both SHR groups (p<0.05). LV inotropy and lusitropy increased similarly from baseline in all groups with incremental forskolin infusion. In the presence of 5 umol/L forskolin, isoprotereno increased LV developed pressure (See Figure), +dP/Dt and -dP/DT to a greater extent in SHR-TRD relative to SHR-SED (p<0.05). Phospholamban phosphorylation at the Thr17 was greater in SHR-TRD relative to SHR-SED and WKY (p<O.05). Absolute LV developed pressure was moderately correlated with phospholamban phosphorylation at both the Ser16 (r=0.64; p<0.05) and Thr17 (r=0.52;

p<0.05). CONCLUSIONS: Our data suggests that the adenylyl cyclase step in the BAR cascade is not downregulated in the early course of hypertension and that the enhanced BAR responsiveness with training is likely mediated at levels other than adenylyl cyclase. Our data alsc suggests that BAR inotropic responsiveness in the presence of direct adenylyl cyclase agonism is improyed in trained compared to sedentary SHR hearts.

## Acute Exercise Worsens Myocardial Ischemia-Reperfusion Tolerance in Hypertension

Patricia O. Reger', Steven C. Kolwicz?, Mary F. Barbe?, Mamta Amin?. Steven R. Houser Joseph R. Libonati2. 1Eastern University, St. Davids, PA. 2Temple University, Philadelphia PA.

puRposE: Acute exercise has been shown to protect the normotensive myocardium from ischeria/reperfusion (I/R) injury. The purpose of the present study was to test whether a single bout of acute exercise protects the hypertensive myocardium from I/R injury and whether this protection is associated with an increased abundance of heat shock protein 72 (HSP 72). METHoDS: Hearts from female, Wistar-Kyoto (WKY; n = 24) and spontaneously hypertensive rats (SHR; n = 27) (age: 10 weeks) were subjected to myocardial I/R in an isovolumic, Langendorff mode (22 min of no-flow ischemia and 10 min of reperfusion; modified Krebs buffer; 2 mM Ca²†) following exposure to one of the following conditions: 1) no exercise (WKY-CON, n=8; SHR-CON, n=8); 2) one hour post-exercise (WKY-1HR, n = 8; SHR-1HR, n = 11); and 3) 24 hours post exercise (WKY-24HR; n = 8; SHR-24HR, n = 8). Exercise consisted of motorized treadmill running at 25 m/min for 60 continuous minutes. REsULTS: Heart weight was similar between WKY and SHR despite elevated systolic blood pressure in SHR (P<0.05). Left ventricular (LV) diastolic performance during ischemia was impaired in SHR vs. WKY (P<0.05), and was worsened in both WKY and SHR one hour post-exercise (See Table 1 below). LV systolic dysfunction was observed during reperfusion in both WKY and SHR and was worsened with acute exercise. Post-reperfusion HSP 72 abundance was similar between WKY and SHR and was unaltered with acute exercise. coNcLusIoN: These data suggest that myocardial tolerance to I/R is more compromised in the young SHR myocardium relative to WKY. Our data also suggest that acute exercise promotes I/R injury rather than inducing cardioprotection. Table 1. LV Diastolic Performance During Ischemia.

# Tissue Doppler Imaging can Distinguish Pathological from Physiological Left Ventricular Hypertrophy in Master Athletes with Mild Hypertension

Loira Toncelli, Brunello Cappelli, M.C.R Vono, Laura Stefani, Marco Gianassi, Francesca Del Furia, Andrea Moretti, Giorgio Galanti. Azienda Ospedaliera Careggi-Medicine Sport centre-Florence, Italy.

PuRposE: Left ventricular wall thicknesses at transthoracic echocardiography are often increased in master athletes, a growing population of trained people observed in Sport Medicine. The observed Left Ventricular Hypertrophy (LVH) may be a physioloqica remodeling induced by physical training or the expression of a pathological hypertrophy because of the mild hypertension often relieved in this middle-aged population. The conventional Pulsed Wave (PW) Doppler analysis of diastolic function, always affected in pathological LVH, is poorly useful to distinguish between physiological and pathogical LVH. Aim of this study is to evaluate the role of pulsed wave Tissue Doppler Imaging (TDI) in differentiating pathological from physiological LVH in middle-aged population.

METHoDS: We have selected a group of 80 master athletes with mild hypertensive state and a group of 80 sedentary subjects suffering from essential hypertension but with a normal diastolic function on standard echocardiography. The subjects of the two groups were comparable by sex male, age (50.3 ± 10.0 vs 51.6 ± 7.9 years; p>.05), increasec left ventricular wall thicknesses and mass index (134.4 ± 19.7 vs 134.5 ± 22.1 gr/m2 p>. 05). The diastolic function indexes by PW technique were in the range of normality for both qroups (E/A 1.2 ± 0.4 vs 1.0 ± 0.4, p<.05)

RESULTS: The pulsed wave TDI study of diastolic function immediately separated the two groups . While in master athletes the diastolic TDI parameters have been within the range of normality (E' 9.4 ± 3.1 cm/sec; E/E' 7.8 ± 2.1), in hypertensive group these parameters have resulted constantly altered, with median values and variation ranges always out ot normal validated limits (E' 7.2 ± 2.4 cm/sec; E/E' 10.6 ± 3.2), with E' and E/E' statistically different in the two groups (p<.001)

## CONCLUSIONS:

Our study showed that TDI technique is an easy and validated method for the accurate assessment of diastolic function because of its sensibility and specificity in differentiating the normal from pseudonormal diastolic pattern, and its superiority from Wp Doppler in differentiating patholoqical from physioloqical LVH in middle-aged population. It turns to be an useful instrument to distinguish physiological from pathological LVH, particularly useful when a sportive idoneity certification is required by legal medical legislation, such as in Italy.

## Mild Enlargement of Left Atria in Athletes: Relationship Between Flow Propagation Velocity and Systolic Atrial Strain-Rate

Valentina Di Tante, Laura Stefani, Loira Toncelli, Brunello Cappelli, Marco Gianassi, Andrea Moretti, M.C.R Vono, Giorgio Galanti. Azienda Ospedaliera Careggi-Medicine Sport centre-Florence, Italy.

INTRoDuCTION: The enlargement of LA ( Left Atrium ) dimensions is associated with risks for atria fibrillation(AF). In regularly trained athletes, LA dimensions are frequently near to the upper limit of the normal range but the implications on atria contractility anc diastolic function are not well studied . The mean peak systolic LA Strain Rate is the parameter here considered for evaluation of atrial systole , in addition its relation with the Flow Propagation Velocity (FPV ), commonly related with a decrease of diastolic relaxation only is analyzed . This study is based on two groups : athletes with mild enlargement of LA and patients with same LA dimensions and a story of recurrent AF. MATERIAL AND

lateral, inferior and anterior wall of the LA calculated with a new software not Doppler derived (IXyS prototype supported by-Esaote).Statistical analysis included t-student test and r-correlation RESULTS: FPV and E/A valUes are

significantly higher in athletes no further differences are evident in the two groups ( table1) There is a negative correspondence ( r = -1) among LA systolic SR of every segment and FPV in both groups. No relationship between LA size and mean SR values

# Comparative Analysis of Two Methodologies to Determine Myocardial Longitudinal Strain in Left and Right Ventricles in Athletes During a Stress Test

Laura Stefani, Loira Toncelli, Marco Gianassi, Paolo Manetti, Valentina Di Tante, Andrea Moretti, Gianni Pedrizzetti, Brunello Cappelli, MCR Vono, Giorgio Galanti. Azienda Ospedaliera Caregqi-Medicine Sport centre-, Florence, Italy. Email: laura-stefani@tiscali.i

INTRoDUcTIoN: Longitudinal strain ( S) can be calculated using either the Dopplerderived TDI method or a new not-Doppler derived method based on the evaluation of 2D tissue displacement in the B-mode like Esaote X-Strain software Both show an high reproducibility of the data but a comparative analysis of their results has not beer conducted in basal interventricular septum ( IVS) an lateral wall ( LW) of left and right ventricles ( LV ,RV) at rest and during stress. This study is aimed to balance the results obtained from two different methods applied in a group of athletes with an high and gold reproducibility of the images , and with enhancement of strain due to stress test

REsuLTS: Cardiac mass index and EF values results in both a in the normal range (132± 5 gr/ m² and 58± 5 % )

## Quantitative Assessment of Regional Myocardial Performance in Athlete's Heart During an Acute Effort : A Physiological Behaviour

Giorgio Galanti, Laura Stefani, Marco Gianassi, Loira Toncelli, Brunello Cappeli, Valentina Di Tante, Andrea Moretti, Paolo Manetti, Gianni Pedrizzetti, MCR Vono. Azienda Ospedaliera Careggi-Medicine Sport centre-, Florence, Italy.

PuRposE: Contractility of myocardial fibres is a complex mechanism characterized by the thickness, the translational and torsional movement with the normal decrease in velocity from basal to apical segments of the heart. Quantitative assessment of the left ventricular function, is actually non-invasively investigated using Strain ( S) strain rate ( S/R) and Velocity (V) calculated with a new not Doppler derived that provides good accuracy and reproducibility of the results. This method examines the wall deformation in every segments of the heart, even in the apex without limits of high noise and angle like TD]. The interest in athletes, is due to the hypothesis of the consequences of the morphological and geometrical deformations in trained heart

METHoDs: 35 subjects ( 25 athletes from different sports, reqularly trained and 10 sedentary controls mean age of 30 years) were submitted to a 2D echo- exam at rest and during an HG ( hand grip at 30 % of maximum effort.) The 2D images obtained were processed with the XStrain-Esaote software to calculate S, S/R, V in basal and apical seaments. EF ( ejection fraction) and the LVM( left ventricular mass) were also measured .

RESULTS:  In athletes, LVM is significantly higher than controls (97,541 g/m at significant increase in S % ( from -17,31±2,3 rest to -24,47±2,8 effort p<0,05) , S/R (1/S) ( from -0,96±2,1 rest to -1,22±0,3 effort p <0,05) and V(cm/sec)( from -0,93±0,5 rest to -1,40±0,6 effort p<0,05) in apical segments In the controls group, no differences were present at rest and after the effort.

coNcLusIoNs: In athletes' heart, a short acute isometric effort produces an increase in apical performance with significant enhancement in S S/R . The average values of the fibre's contraction velocity at the apex is significantly higher with effort than at rest. However, it maintains a physiological behaviour that decreases from basal to apical .In the control group, the same behaviour is not significantly recognizable

# Relative Systolic Dysfunction in Young Spontaneously Hypertensive Rat Myocardium

Brian F. Renna, Scott M. MacDonnell, Patricia O. Reger, Deborah L. Crabbe, Steven R. Houser, Joseph R. Libonati. Temple University, Philadelphia, PA.

Hypertension and exercise independently induce left ventricular (LV) remodeling and alter LV function. The purpose of this study was to determine systolic and diastolic LV pressurevolume relationships (LV-PV) in spontaneously hypertensive rats (SHR) with and without LV hypertrophy, and to determine whether 6 months of exercise training modified the LV-PV in SHR. Methods: 4-month old female SHR (n=20), were assigned to a sedentary (SHR-SED) or treadmill-trained (SHR-TRD) group (60% VO2 peak, 5 d/wk, 6 months), while Wistar-Kyoto rats (WKY:n=13). served as normotensive controls. The LV-PV was determined using a Langendorff isolated heart preparation at 4 months (no hypertrophy; n=10) and 10 months of age (hypertrophy; n=23). Results: At 4 months, the LV-PV in SHR were similar to that observed in WKY controls. However, at 10 months of age, a rightward shift in the LV-PV occurred in SHR. Exercise training did not alter the extent of the shift in the LV-PV relative to SHR-SED animals. Absolute and relative systolic function, i.e. systolic elastance (EAbs and ERel, respectively), were up to 50% lower in SHR than WKY at 10 months of age (Table 1). Echocardiographic-determined fractional shortening (FS) Was loWer in SHR than WKY (WKY 0.57 ± 0.02, SHR-SED 0.50 ± 0.02, SHR-TRD 0.53 ± 0.01; P<0.05 WKY vs. SHR-SED), while Doppler-derived LV filling parameters, i.e. E, A, and E/A ratio were similar between groups. LV capacitance, i.e. V2s, was increased in SHR at 10 months relative to both WkY and SHR at 4 months of age (Table 1) while LV diastolic chamber stiffness was similar between groups at 10 months. Conclusion: Hypertrophic remodeling at 10 months of age in SHR is manifest with relative systolic decompensation without evidence of overt LV diastolic dysfunction. Exercise training did not alter the LV-Pv in SHR.

# Case Report on the Physical Work Capacity of a 37 Year Old Competitive Cyclist Prior to and Following Orthotopic Heart Transplant

Jeremy A. Patterson², Kenneth H. Pitetti², William F. Goodman², Kaelin C. Young², Hussam H. Farhoud². 'Wichita State University, Wichita, KS. Cyprus Heart, Wichita, KS. Email: jeremy.patterson@wichita.edu

PURPosE: It has been well documented that for heart transplant recipients (HTRs), posttransplantation physical work capacity (PwC) normally does not exceed 6o% of the value for healthy age-match controls. Few, if any, studies have undertaken post-tranplantation PWC measurements of well conditioned individuals (i.e., PWC > 300 watts)

CAsE suMMARY: A 37 year-old, professionally trained male cyclist suffered an AMI immediately following a road race and received a heart transplant four months following the AMI The participant resumed training one month following surgery and underwent a maximal exercise test 6 months post surgery.

RESULTS: Peak PWC (33.8 ml•kg"1•min1, 250 Watts) and peak heart rate (165 bpm were 92% and 90% age predicted, respectively. These results were similar to the participants in a study (Richard et al., 1999) who had been training reaularly for 36 ± 24 months prior to testing and PWC evaluations occurred 43 ± 12 months following HTR.

coNcLusIoNs: Although the participant was highly motivated to return to competitive cycling, results suggests: 1) lifestyle prior to HTR positively affect post-transplantation PwC; and 2) a more aggressive approach to heart transplant recovery could be applied to HTRs with similar activity histories.

## Cardiovascular

# Low-Intensity Exercise Training Improves Survival in Female Spontaneously Hypertensive Heart Failure Rats

Sylvia A. McCune, Adam J. Chicco, Craiq A. Emter, Genevieve C. . Sparagna, Kurt D Marshall, Russell L. Moore. University of Colorado at Boulder, Boulder, CO. Email: smccune1@iuno.com

PuRposE: Exercise training has been shown to improve functional capacity and quality of life in patients with heart failure (HF). A recent study conducted in our laboratory indicated that 6 months of low-intensity exercise training (LIET) initiated at 16 months of age delayed the onset of decompensated HF in the male spontaneously hypertensive heart failure (SHHF) rat. The present study was conducted to determine if similar effects of long terrm LIET in female SHHF rats would be found on HF and from all other causes.

METHoDs: Lean female SHHF rats used in this study are a well-characterized aenetic animal model of idiopathic dilated cardiomyopathy that exhibits many of the hallmark biochemical and pathophysiological features seen in human HF. They develop severe hypertension by 4-5 months of age and typically develop classic signs of decompensated HF by 22-26 months of age. Female SHHF rats (16 months of age (n= 10 per group)) were either sedentary (SED) or exercise trained on a motorized treadmill at 14.5 m - min1 at a 10% grade, 45 min day, 3 days per week until rats developed signs of overt HF (dramatic weight gain/loss, labored breathing, peripheral edema, piloerection, and/or LV fractional shortening < 30%), or needed to be sacrificed due to other age-related complications (e.g., pituitary or mammary tumors). The effect of LIET on LV function and morphology was assessed via transthoracic echocardiography at the time of sacrifice. In addition, the content and composition of cardiolipin, a phospholipid that is essential for optimal mitochondrial respiration in the heart, protein expression of calcium handling proteins (phospholamban and the sodium-calcium exchanger) and antioxidant enzymes (MnSOD, CuZnSOD, glutathione peroxidase) were also examined. REsULTS: LIET significantly improved mortality resulting from HF (P < 0.004) with the LIET rats living an average of 4 months longer than SED rats. Mortality from all causes was also significantly (P < 0.05) delayed by LIET. Heart weights were not significantly different between groups. Echocardiography indicated no significant effect of LIET on LV fractional shortening, end diastolic volume, wall thickness compared to SED at the time of sacrifice. LIET had no effect on cardiac antioxidant enzyme protein expression (MnSOD, CuZnSOD, alutathione peroxidase) or calcium handling proteins. LIET did significantly improve levels of tetralinleoyl cardiolipin. coNcLusIoN: LIET significantly improved survival and delayed overt HF as well as mortality from all causes in aoed female SHHF rats, There were few differences between groups in heart function or biochemical parameters examined at the time they developed final HF.

# HSPs are Altered with Age Associated Increases in Oxidative Stress in the Heart of the Fischer 344/Nnia X Brown Norway/Binia Rat

Shinichi Asano1, Kevin M. Rice², Sunil K. Kakarla1, Paulette S. Wehner²³, Ernest M. Walker Jr.³, Eric R. Blough². 1Marshall University, Huntington, WV. 2Marshall University, and Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Marshal! University, Huntington, WV. 3Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Marshall University, Huntington, WV.

BAckGRouND: Ischemic studies, a known stimulator of intracellular ROS, have suggested that Heat Shock Protein (HSP) 27 may play a role in cardioprotection. We speculate that age-associated increases in ROS may also increase HSPs and that this may be a compensatory mechanism to circumvent the auamented ROS seen in the aging heart

PURPosE: Here we determine the influence of aging on HSPs in the heart of adult (6 month), aged (30-month) and very aged (36-month) Fischer 344/NNiaHSd X Brown Norway/BiNia (F344/NXBN) rats, METHODS: Immunoblotting and immunohistochemical analyses were performed on hearts samples to examine the expression of HSP and to determine changes in ("O2') expression and localization. REsULTS: Compared to adults, increases in ("O2") as determined by oxidation of hydroethidine to ethidium (Et) were increased 168.6± 5.2% in 36-month heart and this finding was highly correlated with increases in left ventricular wall thickness (r=0.669; p<0.01) and total protein nitration (r=0.663, p<0.01). Compared to 6-month animals, cardiac HSP27 content was 76.6 ± 14.0% and 82.5 ± 17.4% higher in the 30- and 36-month hearts, respectively. Similarly, the content of HSP70 in the heart was 47.5 ± 6.1% and 90.2 ± 3.1% higher in the 30- and 36-month hearts. Regression analysis showed that increases in cardiac ("O2'") with aging were sianificantly correlated with changes in the cardiac HSP content. coNcLusIoN: These results suggest that HSP regulation in the aging F344/NXBN heart may be potentiated by increase in ROS. Further, HSPs may be play a pivotal role in unraveling the molecular events that lead to age-associated alterations in cardiac oxidative stress (Supported by funds from NSF Grant 0314742)

# Altered Dystrophin-Glycoprotein Complex Composition in the Aging Rat Heart

Sunil K. Kakarla1, Kevin M. Rice², Devashish H. Desai³, Paulette S. Wehner³, Eric R. Blough², 1Marshal! University, Huntinaton, Wy, 2Marshall University, and Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Marshal! University, Huntington, WV. 3Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Marshall University, Huntington, WV.

BAckGRouND: Advancing age is associated with alteration in cardiac morphology and impaired function. Recent data has suggested that disruption of the dystrophinglycoprotein complex (DGC) may be involved in mediating the progression of cardiac hypertrophy and failure. PuRPosE: We exarined the effects of aging on the regulation of DGC proteins in cardiac muscle of adult (6 month). aged (30 month). and very aged (36 month) Fischer 344/NNiaHSD X Brown Norway / BiNia rats. METHODS: Immunoblotting and immunohistochemical analyses were performed on membrane and cytosolic fractions of hearts obtained from 6-, 30- and 36-month old rats to examine the expression and localization of components of the DGC complex. RESULTS: Compared to the 6-month heart, immunoblot analysis revealed that the dystrophin content was decreased 15.07 ± 2.85% in 36-month hearts (P<0.05). As compared to the 6month hearts, dystropin content in the cytosolic fraction was significantly lower in the 36month hearts (14.79%). Content of 3-dystroglycan in the membrane fraction of 36month hearts was markedly higher than 6- month controls (58.36 ± 3.64%; P<0.05), while in the cytosolic fraction of 30- and 36- month hearts, it was 32.98 ± 2.6% and 33.8 ± 1.86% lower than 6-month hearts respectively (P<0.05). Immunohistochemical analysis was used to examine qualitative differences in localization of the DGC molecules. coNcLusIoN: These data suggest marked age associated differences in the composition of the DGC and may play an important role in aging of the heart muscle. (Supported by funds from NSF Grant 0314742)

# Cardiac β-adrenoceptor Expression is Markedly Depressed in the Ossabaw Swine Model of Cardiometabolic Risk

U. Deniz Dincer, Yong Gao, Mouhamad Alloosh, Michael Sturek, Johnathan D. Tune. IUPUI Medical Center, Indianapolis, IN. Email: udincer@iupui.edu

Ossabaw swine have a "thrifty genotype' and consumption of excess calories induces many classical components of the metabolic syndrome, including obesity, insulin resistance, impaired glucose tolerance, dyslipidemia, hyperleptinemia and hypertension. Earlier studies indicate that the metabolic syndrome is associated with diminished cardiac function; however, to what dearee this impairment is associated with alterations in mvocardial Badrenoceptor expression has not been fully elucidated. Accordingly, the present study was designed to investigate the effects of the prediabetic metabolic syndrome on cardiac B and B -adrenoceptor mRNA and protein expression. Studies were conducted on left ventricular tissue samples from normal, control $( \mathsf { n } = 7 )$ and chronically highfat/cholesterol-fed obese Ossabaw swine (> 50 weeks diet, n=8). Chronic feeding significantly increased fasting plasma insulin (4.8 ± 1.6 μU/ml to 12.1 ± 4.6), total cholesterol (57 ± 6 to 166 ± 8 mg/dl), triglycerides (25 ± 3 to 50 ± 3 mg/dl), blood glucose (79 ± 3 to 106 ± 9 mg/dl), systolic blood pressure (106 ± 3 to 148 ± 2 mmHg) and diastolic blood pressure (67 ± 4 to 89 ± 2 mmHg). Real-time PCR revealed nc significant alterations in cardiac β:- and β2-adrenoceptor mRNA expression in left ventricle from high-fat-fed Ossabaw swine, relative to normal controls (2  1.1 ± 0.5 s. 1.4 ± 0.4, respectively). In contrast, Western blot analysis revealed a significant decrease ir ventricular β1- and β2-adrenoceptor protein expression (19.86% and 22.6%, respectively). This is the first report in a novel large animal model that induction of metabolic syndrome is accompanied by a significant reduction in cardiac β-adrenoceptor protein expression that could contribute to impaired cardiac function at rest and during exercise. Supported by HL67804 (JDT), HL062552, and RR013223 (MS).

## Cardiovascular

# Sarcolemmal Katp Channel Blockade Abolishes the Cardioprotective Effect of Short-term Exercise in Male and Female Rats

Adam J. Chicco, Micah S. Johnson, Casey J. Armstrong, Joshua M. Lynch, Ryan T. Gardner, Geof S. Fasen, Cody . Gillenwater, Russell L. Moore.University of Colorado, Boulder Boulder, CO. Email: chicco@colorado.edu

Exercise training is known to confer protection against myocardial ischemia-reperfusion (I/R) injury, but the mechanisms of this cardioprotection have not been fully elucidated. Opening of myocardial ATP-sensitive potassium channels (KaTp) has been hypothesized tc play an important role in the cardioprotection afforded by a variety of preconditioning stimuli. Previous studies on our laboratory have demonstrated that 5 days of exercise training reduces myocardial infarct size following I/R in male and female rats, and increases protein expression of the regulatory subunit of the sarcolemmal Katp channel (sarcKarp) in the heart. pURPosE: The present study was conducted to determine if the infarct-sparing effect of short-term exercise is dependent on the opening of the myocardial sarcKaTp channel. METHoDS: Adult male and female Sprague-Dawley rats were randomly assigned to sedentary or exercise training groups. Animals were trained on a motorized treadmill for 5 days at 15/30/15 m·min" at a 10% grade for 10/40/10 min·d-1. Twenty-four hours following the training or sedentary period, hearts were excised and perfused on a modified Langendorff apparatus and exposed to 1 h of regional ischemia (induced by left coronary artery ligation) followed by 2 h of reperfusion. Prior to ischemia, hearts were perfused with buffer containing the sarcKarp channel antagonist HMR 1098, or with buffer containing no drug for the duration of the I/R protocol. Infarct size was assessed in transverse left ventricular sections as a percentage of the ischemic zone at risk using Evans blue dye and triphenyltetrazolium chloride staining methods. REsuLTS: Short-term exercise significantly reduced infarct size in both male and female hearts compared to their sedentary counterparts. SarcKatp channel blockade completely abolished the cardioprotective effect of exercise in both males and females. As previously demonstrated by our laboratory, infarct size in females was significantly lower than in males, and this sex difference was abolished by sarcKaTp blockade. In addition, HMR 1098 significantly increased infarct size in the sedentary females, but had no effect in the sedentary males coNcLusIoN: This study indicates that the infarct sparing effect of short-term exercise training involves the opening of the sarcKare channel in both male and female rat hearts. In addition. our data confirm prior evidence that the intrinsic resistance of the female rat heart to I/R injury appears to involve an increased reliance on the opening of cardioprotective sarcKarr channels.

# Different Linear Relationships Between Maximal Oxygen Uptake and Maximal Power Resulting from Different Cycle Ergometry Exercise Testing Protocols

Walter van der Weegen, Thierry Barten, Hans yan Kuyk, Sports and Health Center St Anna Hospital, Geldrop, The Netherlands. Email: w.vd.weegen@st-anna.nl

PuRposE: In this study the hypothesis was tested that the use of a gradual ramp protocol would result in a different relationship between peak vO, and peak power.

METHoDS: 82 healthy volunteers (44 male and 38 ferale volunteers between 20 and 65 years with a mean age of 41.5 yrs, SD 13.3) were randomly assigned to either the adapted Bruce protocol or the ramp protocol first. After completing the first test the volunteer woulc perform the next exercise test within three weeks using the other protocol. The applied gradual ramp varied, based on an estimated level of cardiovascular fitness, with six different ramps possible. With the adapted Bruce test, workload increased with 20 Watts per minute. Volunteers ranged in cardiovascular fitness from poor to excellent with an average peak VO2 of 43.5 ml/min/kg (SD 12.7) and a range from 16.1 to 72.6 ml/min/kg Peak power and peak VO> were measured.

REsuLTS: Mean absolute peak VO2 when using the adapted Bruce protocol was 3329 ml/min and 3349 ml/min when using the ramp protocols. Relative peak VO2 was 43.8 ml/min/kg (Bruce) versus 44.1 ml/min/kg (Ramp). The mean difference in absolute peak VO2 was 21.9 ml/min (p = 0.543) and the mean difference in relative peak VO2 was 0.385 $( \mathsf { p } = \mathsf { 0 } . 3 8 9 )$ . No statistical difference in resulting absolute or relative peak VO was found when subgroups were analyzed for age, gender, or level of cardiovascular fitness. However, peak power differed significantly in favour of the ramp protocol. Mean peak power using the ramp protocol was 308 Watts versus 292 Watts in the adapted Bruce protocol $( { \mathsf { p } } = 0 . 0 0 0 ) .$ . With sub analysis peak power differed significantly in favour of the ramp protocol for the male volunteers but not for the female volunteers, and for the volunteers (male and female) with medium and high cardiovascular fitness but not for the volunteers with low cardiovascular fitness.

coNcLusIoNs: Our results indicate that using gradual ramp protocols for maximal exercise testing do not result in higher peak VO2 values but do result in higher peak power when testing male volunteers or when testing medium to highly trained individuals. Therefore the constant linear relationship between Vo2max and peak power appears to be dependent on the protocol used. Usefulness of gradual ramp exercise testing may be more applicable towards testing the performance-level of athletes and patients then the study of gas-exchange kinetics.

# The Adaptation of Oxygen Uptake, Limb Blood Flow, and Muscle Deoxygentation at the Onset of Moderate-Intensity Knee-Extension Exercise in Young and Old Adults

Gregory R. duManoir, John M. Kowalchuk, Donald H. Paterson, FACSM. University of Western Ontario, London, ON, Canada.

The slowed pulmonary O2 uptake $( \mathsf { V O } _ { 2 \mathsf { P } } )$ kinetics (and muscle O2 consumption) of older adults may be limited by convective O delivery to the exercising limb. However, the effects of age on the kinetics of femoral artery blood flow (LBF) remain unknown PURPoSE: To deterrmine the effect of age on $V \mathsf { O } _ { 2 \mathsf { P } } ,$ LBF and muscle deoxygenation kinetics during moderate-intensity exercise. METHoDS: 5 young $( \mathsf { Y } ; 2 5 \pm 2$ yrs) and 5 old (0; 70 ± 6 yrs) male subjects performed repeated (n=4) step-transitions (6 min) from an active baseline (3 W) to moderate-intensity (80% θL), alternate-leg, knee-extension (KE) exercise. VO2p was measured breath-by-breath by mass spectrometer and volume turbine. LBF was measured via Doppler ultrasound at the femoral artery. Deoxygenated hemoglobin/myoglobin (∆HHb) of the vastus lateralis muscle was measured continuously by near-infrared spectroscopy. The $\mathsf { V O } _ { 2 \mathsf { p } } ,$ LBF and HHb data were filtered, time-aligned and ensemble-averaged to provide a single response for each subject, and then further averaged into 10 s (VO2p, LBF) or 5 s (∆HHb) bins. $V C _ { 2 p }$ data were fit with a monoexponential function from the phase 1- phase 2 interface to the end of exercise and LBF was fit from the onset to the end of exercise. Following a delay $( H H b + b ) ,$ HHb data were fit with a monoexponential function to 18o s to assess the adaptation of muscle deoxygenation during the adaptation period of VOzp. REsuLTS: Phase 2 TVO2p was greater in O (45 ± 12 s) compared to Y (30 ± 5 s) during the on-transient of KE exercise. The magnitude of the steady-state increase in LBF (ΔLBF/Δ $\lor \odot _ { 2 \mathsf { p } } ; \odot ; \mathsf { 5 } . 5 \pm \mathsf { 1 } . 3 ; \mathsf { Y } ; \mathsf { 5 } . 3 \pm \mathsf { 0 } . 3 )$ and the rate of increase of LBF (tLBF; O: 39 ± 19 s; Y: 29 ± 12 s) were not different between O and Y. HHbrD (O: 17 ± 4 s; Y: 17 ± 3 s), THHb $( \mathsf { O } ; \mathsf { 1 5 } ^ { \cdot } \pm \mathsf { 8 5 } ; \mathsf { Y } ; \mathsf { 1 0 } \pm \mathsf { 6 5 } )$ and the effective THHb (HHb1p + THHb; O: 32 ± 9 s; Y: 27 ± 5 s) were not different between groups. coNcLusIoNs: These results demonstrate a slower adaptation of VO2p in older subjects during moderate-intensity KE exercise but no significant age-related differences in the adaptation of bulk limb blood flow or muscle deoxygenation. The slower adaptation of muscle O2 consumption in O compared to Y and a similar adaptation of HHb (representing a faster contribution of HHb relative to the rise in VO2p in O compared to Y) would suggest that an impairment in microvascular flow/O, delivery but not bulk limb blood flow contributes to the slower VOz kinetics in O compared to Y. (Supported by NSERC)

# Body Cooling Attenuates the Decrease in Maximal Oxygen Uptake Associated with Cardiovascular Drift During Heat Stress

Jonathan Wingo, Kirk Cureton, FACSM. University of Georgia, Athens, GA. Email: jewingo@comcast.net

Previous research suqgests cardiovascular drift (CV drift) is associated with decreased maximal oxygen uptake (V.O2max) during heat stress, but more research manipulating CV drift with subsequent measurement of V.Ozmax is needed to assess whether this relationship is causal. To assess causation, V.O>max was measured during the same time interval that CV drift occurred (between 15 and 45 min of submaximal exercise under different conditions of body cooling intended to manipulate CV drift). Ten men completed a contro graded exercise test (GXT) in 22°C to measure V.Ozmax, then on separate occasions they cycled in 35°C at 60% V.O2max for 15 min (15max), 45 min with no cooling (NC), and 45 min with fan airflow (FAN) beginning at \~18 min into exercise, and each bout was immediately followed by a GXT to measure $\mathsf { V } . \mathsf { O } _ { 2 m a x } .$

In NC, V.O2max decreased $1 8 \% _ { r }$ heart rate (HR) increased 16%, and stroke volume (SV) fell 12% (P<0.05) from min 15 to min 45. In FAN. V.O2max fell less (5.7%. P<0.05). HR rose less $( 4 \% , 1 7 < 0 . 0 5 ) ,$ ,and SV decreased less (3%, P<0.05) from 15 to 45 min. The fall in V.O2max associated with CV drift during exercise in a hot environment is attenuated with body cooling via fan airflow. The findings support the notion that a causal link exists between CV drift that occurs during prolonged exercise in a hot environment and a decrease in V.O2max-

# Effects of Exercise- or Caloric Restriction-Induced Weight Loss on Muscle Size and Strength and VO2max

Edward P. Weiss, Susan B. Racette, Dennis T. Villareal, Luigi Fontana, Karen Steger-May, Ken B. Schechtman, Samuel Klein, Ali A. Ehsani, John O. Holloszy, FACSM. Washington University School of Medicine, St. Louis, MO

Caloric restriction (CR) results in fat loss; however, it also results in loss of lean tissue, including muscle, and thereby can reduce muscle strenath and aerobic capacity (vO,max). These effects may not occur with exercise-induced weight loss (Ex) because of the anabolic training effects of exercise on muscle and the cardiorespiratory system. We tested the hypothesis that CR reduces muscle size and strength and VO2max while EX preserves or improves these parameters. Healthy 50- to 60-year-old men and women (BMI 23.5-29.9 kg/m²) were studied before and after 1 year of weight loss by CR (n=18) or EX (n=16) Lean mass was assessed by DXA, thigh muscle volume by MRI, isometric and isokinetic knee flexor strength by dynamometry, and treadmill VO2max by indirect calorimetry. Both interventions caused significant decreases in body weight (CR: -10.7±1.4%, EX: - 9.5±1.5%) and lean mass (CR: -3.5±0.7%, EX: -2.2±0.8%), with no significant differences between groups. Significant decreases in thigh muscle volume (-6.9±0.8%) and composite knee flexion strength (-7.2±3%) occurred in the CR group only. Absolute VO2max decreased significantly in the CR group (6.8±2.3%), whereas the EX group had significant increases in both absolute (15.5±2.4%) and relative (28.3±3.0%) VO>max These data provide evidence that muscle mass and absolute physical work capacity decrease in response to 1 year of CR. However, in response to similar weight loss induced by exercise, these effects are prevented, suggesting that during an exercise-induced energy deficit, the body adapts to maintain muscle mass and function and cardiovascular function to maintain or enhance exercise capacity.

## Cardiovascular

# Relationship Between Cardiorespiratory Fitness and Carotid Artery Atherosclerosis in Middle-Aged and Elderly Men

Chong-Do Lee², Hea-Gin Choi?, Sae-Young Jae³. 'Arizona State University, Mesa, AZ. University of Louisville, Louisville, KY. 'University of Illinois, Urbana Champaign, IL.

Whether cardiorespiratory fitness relates to carotid atherosclerotic vascular disease across race, gender, and age groups remains unknown

PURPosE: We investigated the relation of cardiorespiratory fitness (CRF) with carotic artery atherosclerosis in 6,410 Korean men aged 40 to 81 years.

METHoDs: We measured carotid intima-media thickness by using B-mode ultrasonography, and cardiorespiratory fitness was measured by a maximal treadmill exercise test using the Balke protocol. Carotid atherosclerosis was defined as an intimamedia far wall thickness greater than 1 mm or identification of plaque at any site, while CRF was classified as low fit (<20%), moderately fit (20-<60%), or high fit (≥60%) categories based on age-specific treadmill time percentiles

REsuLTS: The presence of carotid atherosclerosis across CRF categories was 3.1% (low fit), 4.9%, and 4.2%. After adjustment for age, there was a direct inverse association between CRF and carotid artery atherosclerosis (P <0.01 for trend). The odds ratio of presence of carotid artery atherosclerosis in the low-fit men versus the high-fit men was 1.43 (95% CI, 1.17, 1.76). After additional adjustment for cigarette smoking, low-density lipoprotein and total cholesterol levels, systolic blood pressure, c-reactive protein, fibrinogen level, diabetes mellitus, and antihypertensive medication, the results remain unchanged and the odds ratios across CRF levels were (95% CI): 1.00 (low fit. referent) 0.84 (0.69, 1.03), 0.78 (0.63, 0.96) (P = 0.02 for trend). The odds ratios of presence of carotid atherosclerosis were 1.2 for current smokers, 1.8 for diabetes, 1.2 for unfit, and 1.3 for hypertension after adjustment for other risk factors.

coNcLusIoNs: Cardiorespiratory fitness is inversely associated with carotid artery atherosclerosis in Korean middle-aged and elderly men. This suggests an involvement of physical activity or fitness in the occurrence of carotid atherosclerosis in men.

# Association of White Blood Cell Count With Cardiorespiratory Fitness, Body Composition, and Blood Lipids in Female College Students

Heagin Choi1, Chong-Do Lee². 1University of Louisville, Louisville, KY. 2Arizona State University, Mesa, AZ

Email: heaqin@yahoo.com

Whether inflammary markers are associated with cardiorespiratory fitness, body composition, and blood lipids across gender and ethnic groups remain less clear.

PURPosE: We investigated the relations of white blood cell count (WBC) with cardiorespiratory fitness, body composition (percent body fat), and blood lipids (highdensity lipoprotein, HDL-C, low-density lipoprotein, LDL-C, and total cholesterols, TC, and triglycerides, TG) in 82 Korean female college students aged 18 to 34 years.

METHoDS: We measured WBC count and blood lipids (HDL-C TC, and TG) using an enzymatic method. HDL-C was measured after dextran-magnesium precipitation, and LDL C was calculated using the Friedewald equation. Percent body fat was analyzed by using the bioelectrical impedance (Biospace Co.), and cardiorespiratory fitness levels were indirectly assessed by using Harvard 5-minute step test. Pearson product-moment correlation was used to investigate the partial associations of WBC count with cardiorespiratory fitness, percent body fat, and blood lipids (HDL-C, TC, and TG) after adjustment for age, body mass index, cigarette smoking, alcohol intake, physical activity, and dietary habits.

REsuLTS: WBC count was inversely associated with cardiorespiratory fitness (r = -0.26, p = 0.02), and positively associated with percent body fat (r = 0.25, p = 0.03) after adiustment for multiple risk factors, Howeyer, there was a weak and non-significant association between WBC count with HDL-C (r = -0.04), LDL-C (r = -0.06), TC (r = -0.05), and TG (r = 0.07)], respectively.

coNcLusIoNs: We conclude that improvements in cardiorespiratory fitness may reduce white blood cell count, while being obese may increase white blood cell count in female Korean college students.

# Physical Fitness and Clinically Relevant Immune Responses in Older Adults

Ryan W. Grant², Todd Keylock², Thomas Lowder1, Kurt Leifheit², Marc Cook², Rachel Mariani', Kijin Kim², Karen Chapman-Novokofski1', Edward McAuley², Jeffrey A. Woods, FACSM1. University of Illinois, Urbana, IL. Keimyung University, Daegu, Democratic People's Republic of Korea Email: rwgrant2@uiuc.edu

PuRPosE: The purpose of this study was to examine the extent to which cardiovascular fitness, independent of confounding factors, was associated with immune responsiveness to clinically relevant challenges in older adults (60-76 years). METHoDs: Thirteen sedentary, low fit (LF; VO2max = 21.1 ± 1.1 ml Kg"1min"1) and 13 physically active, high fit (HF; VOzmax = 46.8 ± 3.4 ml'Kg"1 min"1) older adults participated in this study. Each subject was screened for health status and each performed a maximal graded exercise test with oxygen uptake assessment. Dietary intake was assessed via recall and interview with a registered dietician and a battery of psvchosocial tests were administered, In vivo antibody and ex vivo proliferative and cytokine responses to influenza (Flu) and tetanus toxoid (TT) vaccination, and in vivo responses to delayed-type hypersensitivity (DTH) skin test antigens were performed. REsuLTS: HF elderly displayed a higher antibody response to 2 of the 3 strains included in the Flu vaccine as measured by hemagluttination inhibition, but there was no difference between HF and LF in influenza-specific ex vivo proliferation or interferon(IFN)-y or interleukin(IL)-10 production. HF elderly also exhibited a lower IgG1 and a tendency for a higher IgG2 response to the TT vaccine. There were, however, no differences in TT-specific ex vivo proliferation or IFN-y or IL-10 production. In contrast, HF subjects had higher proliferative responses to phytohemagluttinin. Lastly, there were no differences in DTH responses to fungal antigens between fitness groups. coNcLusIoNs: These results suggest that, after accounting for confounding factors, HF elderly have higher antibody responses to Flu vaccine and a Th2 skewing of the antibody response to TT. There was little evidence that HF elderly subjects mounted better cell-mediated immune responses to the Flu or TT vaccine or to other recall antigens

# Role of Dystrophin-Glycoprotein Complex and Focal Adhesion Complex on Contractile Property in Rat Skeletal Muscles

Shinya Masuda², Tatsuya Hayashi², Sadayoshi Taguchi, FACSM². 1Kyoto University, Kyoto, Japan. Hanazono University, Kyoto, Japan. Email: iammassan@hotmail.com

PURPosE:Dystrophin-glycoprotein complex (DGC) and focal adhesion complex (FAC) are transmembrane structures which make a linkage between extracellular matrix and intracellular cytoskeleton. Both DGC and FAC have critical roles for muscle contraction, but the relationship between these complexes and contractile property is poorly understood. The purpose of this study was to examine the relationship between contractile property and the content of dystrophin (component of DGC) and beta1 integrin (component of FAC) ir rat skeletal muscles.

METHoDs:Eight kinds of skeletal muscles (sloeus, plantaris, extensor digitorum, tibialis anterior, deep portion and surface portion of gastrocnemius, vastus lateralis, and diaphraam) were dissected from each rat. The composition of mvosin heayy chain (MHC) isoforms of muscle was measured by SDS-PAGE. The dystrophin content was quantified by Western blotting. The beta1 integrin content was measured by immunoprecipitation and Western blotting. The expression of dystrophin and beta1 integrin were also detected by immunohistochemical staining.

RESuLTS:Our main findings were that (1) the dystrophin content had a negative correlation with the percentage of type IIb MHC (r2=0.66, p<0.01), (2) the β1 integrin content was very low in the fast type muscles in which type IIx and IIb MHC is highly dominant (>95%), and (3) the expression of beta1 integrin was fiber type specific and was almost undetectable in type IIx and IIb fibers

coNcLusIoNS:Our data suggest that the expression of both DGC and FAC are promoted depending on the duration of mechanical overload rather than the intensity, and that they are among the factors that determine muscle contractile function as a slow type muscle. Our study has provided a new understanding for the difference of molecular mechanisms between fast and slow type muscles.

# Anaerobic Threshold and EMG Activity During Incrementa Cycling Exercise

Kerem T. Ozqunen, Sami Arica, Elif Akkurt, Selcen Korkmaz, Zubeyde Yazici, Arsen Firat Sadi Kurdak. Cukurova University, Adana, Turkey. Email: kozgunen@cu.edu.tr

PURPoSE: Anaerobic threshold (AT) has been defined as the level of exercise at which a change from aerobic to partially anaerobic energy supply is supposed to occur. Even though lactate [La] accumulation is expected at the work loads above AT. accumulation rate differs between individuals Beside the alteration of metabolic pathways, progressive recruitment of fast twitch fibers may explain the changes in [La] accumulation rate. In this study we aimed to investigate the relationship between AT and mean frequency (MF) and Root Mean Square (RMs) parameters of surface electromyoaram (SEMG) during incremental cvcling

METHODS: 8 male subjects aged 23.5 ± 1.4 (mear ± SE) underwent one minute incremental cycling exercise to determine peak VO2. Predetermined loads are added every minute up to voluntarily exhaustion. Anaerobic threshold was calculated according to Vslope method. The SEMG activities were recorded by bipolar surface electrodes from the left rectus femoris (RF), vastus medialis (VM), gastrocnemius lateralis (GL) and gastrocnemius medialis (GM). RMS and MF data were averaged for every work load. RMS values were normalized with VO at the initial, AT and maximal Ievel of exercise for each individual. Repeated measures and paired-t test were used to analyze the SEMG data.

REsULTS: Peak values obtained during the exhausting work load (281 ± 15 W) for ventilatory, metabolic and Figus 7 cardiovascular parameters were VE, 156.6 ± 9 1/min; VO2, 3.59 ± 0.2 I/min (50.01 ± 3.17 ml.kg1.min1); VCO2, 4.27 ± 0.21 l/min; HR, 187 ± 3 beats/min. Changes in MF and RMS/VO values for initial, AT and maximal steps of exercise are given in figure 1 and 2. coNcLUsIoNs: Presence of hiqh and low MF may indicate the different contractile and excitation characteristics of muscle fibers together with motor unit type. Since the MF value did not increase during the incremental exercise (with the exception of VM AT value), it is possible to argue the absence of fiber recruitment with various firing characteristics. The significant elevation of RMS/VO2 in VM and RF beyond AT may indicate the addition of new motor units with similar contractile properties. This may be an important factor to discuss the possible causes of [La] accumulation.

# Examination of Metabolic Responses Using the Digi-Jump Machine: Gender and Cadence Comparisons

Thomas S. Lyons², John R. McLester², Zachary J. Callahan², John C. Faircloth², J. K. Davis1. 1Western Kentucky University, Bowling Green, KY. Kennesaw State University, Kennesaw, GA. Email: scott.lyons@wku.edu

purposE: This study investigated metabolic variables in active male and female subjects following both 120 and 100 jumps per minute (JPM) protocols. These protocols were conducted on the Diqi-Jump, a machine desiqned to requlate subjects' JpM as well as height per jump. This and other similar studies are currently underway pursuant to the recent Surgeon General's report identifying bone health and osteoporosis as a public health priority and its recommendation of repetitive jumping as a preferred exercise for ameliorating this growing problem

METHoDs: 28 recreationally active males and females (males: age 21.8 +/- 1.6 yrs; body fat 10.3 +/- 3.1%; females: age 20.2 +/- 1.7 yrs; body fat 18.9 +/- 4.3%) performed in counterbalanced order both a 120 and 100 JpM trial, each for a maximum of 15 minutes. Subjects were also required to reach a minimum of 1/2" height for each jump. Jump cadence and jump height were both requlated by the Diqi-Jump. Cadence was monitored through a series of lights and audible "beeps," while height was requlated by infrared beams. Metabolic data and RPE were collected at each minute and at test termination. Participants were asked a series of subjective questions following each of the trials for researchers to gain a more thorough understanding of the fatique associated with repetitive jumping.

REsuLTS: 17 of 28 subjects were able to jump for the full 15 minute duration during the 120 JPM trial, while only 8 of 28 completed 15 minutes for the 100 JPM trial. Subjects whc were unable to complete a trial terminated eariy due to cardiovascular stress, upper-leg muscle fatigue, lower-leg muscle fatigue, or a combination of these. Metabolic and RPE data demonstrated main effect differences for all subjects between 120 and 100 JPM for average RER (p=.002), average RPE-upper legs (p=.044), average RPE-lower legs (p=.018), and test duration (p= .001). No differences were demonstrated when comparing gender data across both protocols.

coNcLusIoNs: Our data indicate that when considering repetitive jumping at either 100 or 120 JPM, the more rapid cadence is preferable as subjects reported a lower average RPE for both upper and lower legs, lower average RER, and improved test tolerance as indicated by a longer test duration. Future research will be focused on specific jump cadences and jump heights and their direct applicability to bone health

# The Inverse Relationship Between Anaerobic Threshold and Lactate Accumulation Rate

Sadi Kurdak, Kerem T. Ozqunen, Elif Akkurt, Zubeyde Yazici, Selcen Korkmaz, Arsen Firat. Cukurova University, Adana, Turkey. Email: sskurdak@cu.edu.tr

PURPosE: The oxygen uptake (VO2) at which blood lactate level beains to rise has been used to define anaerobic threshold (AT) in endurance athletes and non-invasively measured by V-slope method. When VO and carbon dioxide output (vcO2) are plotted against each other, the relationship composed of two apparently linear components, the lower of which (Si) has a slope of slightly less than 1.0, whereas the upper component (S2) has a slope steeper than 1.0. Changes in S2 slope may reflect the accumulation rate of lactic acid and may exhibit inter-individual variability. In this study we aimed to investigate the relationship between the changes of S2 slope together with AT/peak VO in incremental cycle exercise

METHoDS: 9 male subjects aged 24.2 ± 1.4 (mean ± SE) underwent incremental cycling exercise to determine peak VO2. Measurements of blood lactate ([La]p) were performed from the samples withdrawn from antecubital vein at rest and during the last 15 seconds of each one minute work load. Anaerobic threshold was calculated according to V-slope method. Regression analyses were used to determine the relationship between the evaluated variables

REsuLTs: Peak values obtained during the exhausting work load (256 ± 11 W) for ventilatory, metabolic and cardiovascular parameters were VE, 158 ± 8.1 l/min; VO2, 3.55 ± 0.12 1/min (49.1 ± 2.96 ml.kg"1.min2); VCO2, 4.29 ± 0.19 I/min; HR, 186 ± 2 beats/min and

[La]b, 4.8 ± 0.69 mM. The significant relationship was found between VCO2 and [La]b accumulation rate (r² = 0.75, p < 0.01) is important to show that changes in S2 slope may be an evidence for anaerobic metabolic contribution (Fig. 1). Subjects that had higher AT/peak VO2 had steeper S2 slope values compare to the less fit individuals (r² = 0.60, p < 0.05) (Fig. 2).

coNcLusIoNs: Findings of this study may raise the possibility of various [La] accumulation rate may be important to interpret relative exercise intensity above AT. The inverse relationship between S2 slope and AT/peak VO, may indicate differences in anaerobic metabolic pathways. Further investigations are needed to clarify the relationship between AT/peak VO2 and changes in [La]p accumulation during incremental exercise.

# Rating of Perceived Exertion in different moments of walking and running in individuals from Brazilia/DF city

Sérqio R. Moreira², Pedro P. Morais², Ricardo M. Lima1, Thiago Athayde², Maria A. Germano², Guilherme C. Samy². Tatiane G. Carrijo². Renata F. Costa², Herbert G. Simöes1. 1Catholic University of Brasília, Brasilia - DF, Brazil. 'Paulista University, Brasilia - DF Brazil. Email: sergior@pos.ucb.br

PuRposE:Evaluate and compare the RPE within different moments of a walking or running session, as well as between these two types of activities in men and women that exercises in leisure parks of Brasília/DF city.

METHoDS:Thirty two volunteers were divided in two groups similar in their baseline characteristics (p>0,05) as follows: G1: walking (n.24; 38,9±14,0 years; 71,1±19,6 Kg; 167,0±10,4 cm; BMI=25,4±5,8 Kg/m²); e G2: running (n.8; 42,0±11,6 years; 68,3±11,4 Kg; 166,0±7,6 cm; BMI=24,7±2,9 Kg/m²). Both groups exercised in a leisure park with a track of approximately 2,5 Km. The individuals volunteered, after an explanation covering the measure instrument, to answer the 15-grade Borg's RPE scale (Borg, 1982) in three different moments of exercise (MRPE1 = initial phase; MRPE2 = mid phase; and MRPE3 : final phase). The evaluator monitored each individual during the whole exercise session, avoiding interference on the intensity chosen by the volunteer, showing the scale on the previously determined phases to data acquisition (MRPE1 \~5-7 min; MRPE2 \~10-14 min; MRPE3 \~15-21 min). Descriptive statistical was done to present the data, witch are expressed as the means and standard deviation. Independent-samples "t" test was applied to compare the same moments between G1 and G2. ANOvA for repeated measures was used to examine differences between the moments within each group and results were considered significant at P<0,05 (InStat versão 3.0).

## RESULTS:

It wasn't observed significant differences when cormparing G1 and G2 RPE in any of the moments, as well as between groups RPE means, however, significant differences were noted between the different moments in G1 (table 1).

coNcLusioNs: Individuals that performed walking in the leisure park presented similar RPE to those that performed running, however, the walking group presented a significant increase in RPE during the different exercise phases, These findings suggest a possible Iack of instruction about the exercise intensity to be performed, what may have negative implications on adherence and adaptations of aerobic exercise training.

# Skeletal Muscle Metabolic Adaptations in Response to 6 Weeks of High-Intensity Interval Training

Christopher G.R. Perry1, Jason L. Talanian², George J.F. Heigenhauser, FACSM², Lawrence L. Spriet, FACSM1. University of Guelph, Guelph, ON, Canada. ²McMaster University, Hamilton, ON, Canada. Email: perryc@uoguelph.ca

purPosE: There is sparse data in regards to skeletal muscle metabolic adaptations that occur in response to hiqh intensity (80-100% VO,max) interval training (HIIT). Repeated short bouts of exercise at this intensity challenges both the aerobic and anaerobic ATr producing pathways and leads to an increased capacity of these pathways. We investigated the adaptive responses in the skeletal muscle's aerobic capacity and ability to distribute pyruvate to oxidative phosphorylation during high intensity exercise following 6 wks of HIIT, and hypothesized that there would be improved sensitivity in the regulation of PDH and reduced reliance on glycogenolysis and PCr. METHoDs: 8 untrained but recreationally active subjects trained 3 d/wk for 6 wks on a cycle ergometer following a VOzmax test and time trial to exhaustion (TTE) at 90% VOmax, which were repeated after training. Workouts consisted of ten 4 min bouts at 90% VO2max separated by 2 min of rest. This equated to 12 hours of training over 6 wks. Training power outputs (PO) were increased to maintain heart rate at \~95 % of maximum. Muscle biopsies were taken during the TTE at rest, 5 min and exhaustion (EX)

RESULTS: PO increased by 21% over 6 wk (209 ± 47 to 252 ± 51 W). Following training, VO2max increased by 9% (3.29 ± 0.24 to 3.58 ± 0.26 l/min) and TTE by 111% (7.1 ± 0.2 to 15.0 ± 1.1 min). The maximal activity of citrate synthase increased by 26% (18.4 ± 1.4 to 23.1 + 1.2 mmol/min/kg wet muscle) and β-hydroxyacyl-CoA dehydrogenase increased by 29% (15.8 ± 1.1 to 20.3 ± 0.9 mmol/min/kg). PDH total increased by 23% (2.54 + 0.21 to 3.09 ± 0.29 mmol/min/kg). Activation of PDH (PDHa) at 5 min in the TTE did not change with training (Pre, 2.32 + 0.24; Post, 2.39 + 0.18 mmol/min/kq) but was higher at EX (Pre, 1.94 ± 0.20; Post, 2.55 ± 0.27 mmol/min/kg wet muscle). The rate of glycogenolysis in the first 5 mins of TTE decreased (34.1 ± 4.8 to 23.3 ± 3.5 mmol/min/kg dry muscle) as did PCr utilization (12.5 ± 0.7 to 10.5 ± 1.1 mmol/min/kg dry muscle) and lactate accumulation (22.4 ± 1.1 to 17.9 ± 1.6 mmol/min/kg dry muscle) following training. Free ADP (ADPf) was reduced at 5 min after training (366.1 ± 42.5 to 265.4 ± 34.1 mmol/kg wet muscle). coNcLusIoNs: Only 12 hours of HIIT over 6 wks resulted in impressive increases in the aerobic capacity of the skeletal muscle. The reduced levels of ADPf but similar PDHa post-training suggest an improved sensitivity in the regulation of PDH. This, coupled with attenuated glycogenolysis, resulted in a greater proportion of pyruvate directed to oxidative phosphorylation. A decrease in PCr utilization supports these findings of HIIT-induced enhancements in aerobic ATP production and endurance performance during very intense exercise.

## Metabolic

# Confirmation of Treadmill $\yen 023,456$ in Sprinters and Long Distance Runners

James E. Harris, Andres Hernandez. Matthew L. Goodwin, L Bruce Gladden. FACSM. Auburr University, Auburn, AL Email: harri13@auburn.edu

A plateau in oxygen uptake (VO2) despite an increase in work rate is often not observed during continuous incremental exercise tests. Indirect criteria including respiratory exchange ratio (R > 1.10) and blood lactate concentration ([La] > 8.0 mM) are frequently used to confirm maximal oxygen uptake $( \textsf { V O } _ { 2 \max } )$ in the absence of a plateau in VO2. Recently, a test to directly confirm VOzpeak was developed for healthy males performing cycle ergometry (J Appl Physiol 100: 764-770, 2006).

purposE: The purpose of this investigation was to determine whether long distance runners and sprinters routinely display a VO> plateau during continuous incremental treadmill tests, and if not, whether the highest VO observed was in fact VOzmax-METHoDs: Nine male long distance runners (age 21 ± 1 yrs, VO2max 71.0 ± 2.8 mL•kg 1min1) and six male sprinters (age 26 ± 3 yrs, VO2max 55.9 ± 5.8 mL•kg1•min1) ran to volitional exhaustion at a constant treadmill speed previously determined to elicit 4 mM blood [La"]. This continuous incremental test consisted of two-minute stages with 2% grade increments. A VO2 plateau was defined as less than half the expected increase in VO2 between the last two completed stages. Following a 15 minute recovery period, subjects performed a constant work rate test to exhaustion at a steeper grade, Data were analyzed by paired-samples t-test.

REsuLTS: None of the long distance runners and one of the sprinters achieved a plateau on the continuous incremental test. However, by combining the data from the continuous incremental test and the constant work rate test, all subjects exhibited a discontinuous plateau in VO. Peak VO on the continuous incremental test for the long distance runners (70.6 ± 2.8 mL•kg•min1) was not significantly different (p = 0.12) from peak VO on the constant work rate test $( 6 9 . 2 \pm 2 . 3 $ 5 mL•kg"1•min"1). Peak VO2 on the continuous incremental test for the sprinters $( 5 5 . 6 \pm 5 . 5$ 9mL•kq"1•min"1) was not significantly different (p = 0.09) from peak VO2 on the constant work rate test (53.4 ± 5.0 mL•kg"1•min"1).

coNcLusIoNs: Trained competitive sprinters and long distance runners do not routinely exhibit a plateau at $\mathsf { V O } _ { 2 \mathsf { m a x } }$ : during continuous incremental treadmill tests. Peak VO, on a continuous incremental treadmill test can be directly confirmed as VOzmay by performing ar additional higher work rate test following a short rest.

# Effects of Short Term Hypoxia on Sub-maximal Exercise in Cross Country Skiers

Federico F. Schena. Filippo Balestreri. University of Trento. Rovereto. Italy. Email: federico.schena@unitn.it

purposE: To evaluate the response to sub-maximal aerobic exercise at altitude after a short period of exposure to hypoxia in cross country skiers which usually experience several training camps (5-6days lasting) at moderate altitude

METHoDs: Nine male cross country skiers were selected from national teams (age: 29,4±1,2ys, V'O2 max: 68,3± 2,3 ml/kg/min; average ±sd). All the athletes were wel used to altitude training since at least 5 years and they never suffered from problems in acclimatization. The athletes underwent two incremental treadmill tests: 1- at habitual living height (about 800 mt) and 2- 36 h after ascending at 2800 mt. Tests were carried out by running at 5% fixed slope with speed increasing 1km/h every 4 min, starting from 9 km/h to 13 km/h (determined as sub maximal during previous trial) . During each trial heart rate (HR), oxygen consumption (V'O2), pulmonary ventilation (V'E), and hemoglobin saturation (SaO2) were continuously measured by metabolimeter (K4b², Cosmed, Italy). Blood lactate concentration (BLa) was measured (Esatt 602, Eppendorf, Germany) 3 min after the end of each step

REsuLTS: From 9 to 12 km/h HR and V'O2 were statistically unchanged by acute altitude exposure while the difference becomes significant only for V'O2 (- 12%, p<0,05) at the last workload. BLa and V'E were significantly higher at any steps after the initial one (average changes from 25 to 42%, p>0,05). SaO2 was significantly decreased at 2800 mt during rest as well as any exercise level ( from -5% to -16%) but, also at 800 mt, it was reduced (<92%) during the upper steps. The relationship HR vs V'O2 showed an increased slope at altitude reaching a difference after the level of 5Oml/kg/min, on the contrary V'E vs V'O2 was up shifted at any metabolic level.

DIscussIoN/coNcLusIoNs: These data show that acute adaptation to moderate altitude in well trained and experienced cross country skiers allows a quite good level of aerobic performance at low or moderate intensity. An anaerobic contribution to the energy requirements appears to limited only at higher percentage of $\mathsf { V } ^ { \prime } \mathsf { O } _ { 2 \mathsf { m a x } } .$ The hypoxic stimulation on the tissues, as determined by haemoglobin saturation, is important at any Ievel of exercise while cardiac and ventilation short term adaptations are able to maintair oxygen delivery as reauested by sub-maximal workloads, This could suagest a specific quick response in these athletes to moderate altitude exposure which allow them to train properly also during short lasting altitude camps.

puRPosE: To compare maximum oxygen consumption acquired by two maximum cardiopul monary exercise tests with fifteen minutes of recovery between them.

## Congenic Strains Confirm the Linkage of Chromosome 16 to Aerobic Running Capacity in the Rat

Justin A. Ways², Brian M. Smith², John C. Barbato², Ramona S. Ramdath², Krista M. Pettee1, Sarah j. DeRaedt², David C. Allison1. Lauren G. Koch³. Soon Jin Lee1, George T. Cicila. Health Sciences Campus, University of Toledo, Toledo, OH. 2Lerner Research Institute, Cleveland Clinic Foundation, Cleveland, OH. 3University of Michigan, Ann Arbor, MI.

Email: iways@meduohio.edu

PURPosE: We previously identified two inbred rat strains divergent for treadmill aerobic running capacity (ARC): the low performing Copenhagen (CoP) and the high performing DA rats. A subsequent genome scan performed on an F2 (CoPxDA) population linked rat chromosome 16 (RNO16) and the proximal portion of rat chromosome 3 (RNO3) to the observed strain differences in ARC. To confirm the link between these chromosomal regions and ARC, we bred 2 congenic strains by replacing either RNO16 or the proximal portion of RNO3 in COP rats with the corresponding regions from DA rats. Running capacity, body weiqhts, organ weights, and plasma concentrations of free fatty acids, triglycerides, and glucose were then measured to characterize the resultant congenic strains.

METHoDS: RNO16 and the proximal portion of RNO3 from the DA strain were transferrec separately into CoP rat genetic backgrounds via a marker assisted successive backcrossbreeding paradigm. The resultant congenic strains were named COP.DA(chr 16) and COP.DA(chr 3), respectively. At 11-weeks of age, male rats from each congenic strain and the parental cop strain were tested for their ability to perform a treadmill running test to exhaustion. After a 3-week sedentary period, body weights, organ weights, and plasma concentrations of free fatty acids, triglycerides, and glucose were measured. Statistical significance (p ≤ 0.05) was determined using one-way ANOvA comparing the congenic strains to COP.

RESULTS: Significantly greater ARC was observed in COP.DA(chr 16) compared to COP rats (696.7±38.2 m and 571.9±27.5 m, respectively; p = 0.025). Although ARC of COP.DA(chr 3) rats tended to be higher than the parental COP rats (643.6±40.9 m vs 571.9±27.5 m), this was not statistically significant (p = 0.213). COP.DA(chr 16) rats hac significantly more subcutaneous abdominal fat accompanied by a significantly lower fasting plasma triglyceride concentrations compared to COP.

coNcLusIoN: The COP.DA(chr 16) congenic strain confirmed that there are genes on RNO16 that regulate ARC in DA and COP rats. Increased subcutaneous abdominal fat anc lower fasting plasma triglyceride concentrations in COP.DA(chr 16) rats compared to COP rats suggest that genes regulating lipid metabolism are also located on RNO16. Identifying the genes and establishing a relationship between lipid metabolism and ARC will require the breeding of congenic substrains that contain smaller regions of RNO16 from DA rats

## Metabolic

# Neuroendocrine Response to Short-Term Energy Surplus and Exercise

Todd A. Hagobian, Carrie G. Sharoff, Brooke R. Stephens, Stuart R. Chipkin, Barry Braun, FACSM. University of Massachusetts Amherst, Amherst, MA. Email: hagobian@kin.umass.edu

Energy surplus and physical exercise have opposing effects on some key neuroendocrine facors (concentrations of leptin, insulin, and ghrelin) that modulate energy intake. Energy surplus causes changes in the neuroendocrine response that decrease energy intake, whereas exercise, at least when expended energy is not replaced, has the opposite effect.

PURposE: To determine whether the exercise effect is independent of concurrent changes in energy balance. To do that, we assessed the neuroendocrine response (leptin, insulin, ghrelin) to a single bout of exercise, performed against the background of a short-term energy surplus. METHoDs: After 2 days in energy balance and without exercise, baseline fasting leptin, insulin, and ghrelin concentrations were measured in nine healthy, habitually active subjects (6 M, 3 F). Subjects were then overfed (OF) to generate a daily energy surplus of 768 ± 203 kcal/d for 3 more sedentary days and fasting blood samples were repeated. In the following 24 hours, overfeeding was increased 2-fold (+1502 ± 399 kcal/d) and subjects performed a single bout of exercise (expenditure = 732 ± 192 kcal), to maintain the same energy surplus (+747 ± 223 kcal/d;OF+EX) as OF. REsULTS: Compared to baseline, after OF fasting leptin concentrations were significantly higher (5.2 ± 7.0 vs. 6.8 ± 8.9 ng/ml, respectively; p=0.045), insulin concentrations tended to be higher (52.8 ± 21.9 vs. 71.9 ± 38.1 pmol/L, respectively; p=.099), and ghrelin concentrations did not change (681 ± 133 vs. 664 ± 135 pg/ml, respectively; p=0.77) After OF+EX, fasting leptin (6.4 ± 2.9 ng/ml; p=0.17) and insulin (75.7 ± 33.0 pmol/L p=0.043) remained higher than baseline, with no change in ghrelin concentrations (658 ± 173 pg/ml; p=0.61). There was a positive relationship between plasma leptin and ghrelin concentrations (r2=0.29, p<0.05). coNcLusIoNs: Short-term energy surplus increased fasting leptin and insulin concentrations but had no effect on fasting ghrelin. A single exercise bout, when performed against a background of concurrent energy surplus, had nc impact on fasting leptin, insulin, and ghrelin concentrations. These data suggest that the effect of exercise on key neuroendocrine factors is at least partially mediated by perturbations in energy balance. This study was supported by a grant from the Americar Diabetes Association.
