## Metabolic

# Voluntary Exercise and the Development of Osteoarthritis in Mice Fed a High-fat Diet

Timothy M. Griffin, Zhen Yan, Farshid Guilak, Duke University Medical Center, Durham, NC Email: tmgriff@duke.edu

Osteoarthritis (OA) is a progressive, degenerative joint disease characterized by an imbalance of articular cartilage biosynthesis and degradation attributed to both inflammatory and biomechanical factors. Obesity, or factors associated with obesity, are a primary risk factor for OA in both load-bearing and non-load bearing joints, suggesting that systemic factors mediate obesity-induced OA. puRPosE: To test the hypothesis that voluntary exercise mitigates the development of OA in diet-induced obese mice.

METHoDS: 12-week old male mice (C57BL/6J) were fed either normal chow (NC) (n=10) or high-fat (HF) chow (60% kcal fat) (n=10). After 8 weeks of feeding. half the mice from each diet group were housed in cages equipped with a custom-designed running wheel that allowed for continuous monitoring of voluntary running activity. Mice continued to have free access to their respective diets durina the exercise period, The study ended when the mice were 24 weeks old (i.e., after 4 weeks of exercise). Percent body fat was assessed using DExA analysis. Knee joint degeneration was assessed using histomorphometric analysis following a modified Mankin OA scoring system developed for mice. REsULTS: HF feeding significantly increased body mass (HF: 37.9 ± 1.3g, NC: 24.4 ± 0.35g, P<0.05) percent body fat (HF: 34.7 ± 2.1%, NC: 11.0 ± 0.44%, P<0.05), and joint degeneration (HF: 18.2 ± 2.4, NC: 10.4 ± 2.1, P<0.05) in non-exercised mice. Diet, however, did not affect the average daily running distance in exercised mice (HF: 6.15 ± 0.67 km/day, NC: 6.75 ± 0.70 km/day, P=0.6). Contrary to our hypothesis, exercise did not affect joint degeneration in either the HF (18.2 ± 0.7, P=0.75) or the NC (12.4 ± 2.0, P=0.67) fed mice. Body mass and percent body fat were not affected by 4 weeks of voluntary exercise in either diet group. coNcLusIoN: High-fat feeding is an effective means of inducing non-traumatic joint degeneration in mice at a relatively young age. Voluntary wheel running exercise did not affect the development of joint degeneration in the medial compartment of the knee joint. Our previous studies of HF diet-induced OA in mice indicate that joint degeneration is positively correlated with body mass and body fat. Thus, longer duration or hiaher intensity exercise that is sufficient to reduce body mass or fat levels may be needed to alter the pathogenesis of HF diet-induced OA in mice Supported by NIH grants AR50245 and AR51672.

# Exercise Training Reverses the Effects of a High Fat Diet on the ACTH Response to Stress

Ryan Jankord, JR Turk, VK Ganjam, MH Laughlin, FACSM. University of Missouri, Columbia, MO.

Email: jankordr@missouri.edu

PURposE: This study was conducted to determine the effects of diet and exercise on the hormone response to stress, We hypothesized that a high fat/high cholesterol diet would compromise the AcTH and cortisol response to stress, and that this decrease would be ameliorated by exercise training. We also hypothesized that exercise training, in animals on a normal control diet, would augment the AcTH and cortisol response to stress

METHoDs: Twelve sexually mature, Yucatan miniature swine, aged 9-13 mo, were usec for this study. Six animals were placed on a hiah fat/hiah cholesterol diet for 16-20 wks and 6 animals received a normal pig chow diet. Three animals from each group underwent treadmill training for 16-20 wks. This distribution of animals resulted in 4 groups with 3 pigs in each group (normal diet sedentary (NS); normal diet exercise training (NEX); high fat/high cholesterol diet sedentary (HFS); high fat/high cholesterol diet exercise training (HFEX)). Blopd samples were collected in EDTA Vacutainers while animals were unde anesthesia. Anesthesia induces an increase in both ACTH and cortisol in pigs. A two-way ANOvA test of exercise and diet interactions and t-tests were run to compare groups with siqnificance set at P < 0.05.

REsuLTS: The high fat/high cholesterol diet significantly decreased the ACTH response to anesthesia-induced stress compared to the Controls (NS: 165 ± 22 pg/ml vs. HFS: 79 ± 7 pg/ml). Exercise training did not affect the ACTH response in animals on the normal diet (NEX: 127 ± 17 pg/ml), but siqnificantly increased the ACTH response in the animals on the high fat/high cholesterol diet (HFEX: 230 ± 46 pg/ml). There is a significant interaction between diet and exercise so that the greatest AcTH response was seen in animals receiving both exercise training and a high fat/high cholesterol diet. Neither diet nor exercise affected the cortisol response to anesthesia-induced stress (NS: 116 ± 26 ng/ml; NEX: 106 ± 11 ng/ml; HFS: 140 ± 9 ng/ml; HFEX: 148 ± 30 ng/ml)

coNcLusIoN: In pigs on a normal chow diet, exercise training does not affect the ACTH or cortisol response to anesthesia-induced stress, A hiah fat/high cholesterol diet significantly compromises the ACTH response to anesthesia-induced stress and, this decrease is ameliorated by exercise training.

# Molecular Control of Skeletal Muscle Protein Metabolism is Altered by Resistance Training

David L. Mayhew, Jeong-su Kim, David J. Kosek, James M. Cross, Marcas M. Bamman, FAcsM University of Alabama at Birminaham Birmingham Al Email: dmayhew@uab.edu

Protein fractional synthesis (FSR) and breakdown (FBR) rates sum to determine the net protein balance and consequently the state of muscle mass. Resistance exercise has been shown to modulate these parameters in favor of a hypertrophic phenotype.

PuRposE: The current study sought to determine the effect of a lower-extremity resistance training program on net protein balance and molecular markers of skeletal muscle protein synthesis and breakdown pathways.

METHoDS: A mixed age. mixed gender population (n = 10) underwent 8 weeks of a lower-extremity resistance training program consisting of 3 d/wk of 3 sets of 8-12 RM on each of squat, leg press, and leg extension. Stable isotope infusions of L-[ring-2Hs]phenylalanine and L-[15N]phenylalanine were used to determine mixed muscle FSR and FBR, respectively. Western blots were used to determine cytosolic protein expression levels in vastus lateralis muscle biopsies of total and phosphorylated Akt and 4EBP1, total caspase-3, and total ubiquitin-activating enzyme E1 (Ub-E1). All measures were taken at baseline and 24-hours after acute exercise bouts at weeks 1 and 8 of the training program

REsULTS: Repeated measures ANOVA indicated a significant time effect for FSR, net protein balance, Akt, and Ub-E1 (p < 0.05). Tukey post hoc analysis revealed that FSR experienced a summative response to training with sequential increases at wks 1 and 8 with wk 8 significantly higher than baseline (p = 0.003). FBR did not change with training. Therefore, net protein synthesis (FSR - FBR) followed a similar summative course as FSR (baseline to wk 8, p = 0.019). Total Akt increased at wk 8 with respect to baseline (p = 0.0004) and wk 1 (p = 0.0006). Ub-E1 increased at wk 8 with respect to baseline (p = 0.034). Phospho-Akt, phospho-Akt/total Akt ratio, phospho-4EBP1, total 4EBP1, and caspase-3 did not change from baseline. Phospho-4EBP1/total 4EBP1 ratio trended toward significance (p = 0.096) with increasing ratios at each successive time point

coNcLusIoNs: Eight weeks of resistance training significantly increased total Akt and Ub-E1, with FSR and net protein balance favoring hypertrophy.

# Muscle Oxygenation During Incremental Arm-Cranking Exercise in Healthy and Hypertensive Elderly Humans

Silvia Poaliaghi, Elisa Dussin, Cantor Tarperi, Antonio Cevese, Federico Schena. Universita di Verona, Verona, Italy

Email: silvia.pogliaghi@univr.it

PuRposE: We evaluated the factors limiting aerobic arm exercise performance in compensated hypertensive vs healthy elderly males. We hypothesized that, due to cardiovascular modifications associated with high blood pressure, central factors play a larger role, in the age-related decline in arm exercise capacity, in hypertensive rather than in normotensive subjects.

METHoDs: Non-smoking elderly (14 normotensive, mean age ± SD 69 ± 5 yrs and 13 hypertensive, 68 ± 5) were compared to 10 young males (29 ± 6 yrs). The subjects performed an incremental arm-cranking test to exhaustion. Ventilation, gas exchange and heart rate (HR) were measured breath by breath (Quark b², Cosmed, Italy). Changes in concentration of deoxygenated hemoglobin ([deoxyHb], an index of the ratio between O consumption and O2 delivery, similar to O2 extraction) were monitored non-invasively by near infrared spectroscopy (HEO-200, Omron, Japan) at the biceps brachii. O extraction was expressed as % of the value obtained during arm ischemia (physiological calibration). Peak data were compared for significant differences by one-way analysis of variance.

## RESULTS:

As expected, peak exercise variables were significantly hiaher in the young compared tc the elderly subjects. Yet, no differences in peak values of power output (83±11; 89±14 W), VO2 (1.62±0.29; 1.64±0.41 I\*min-1), HR (147±14; 152±11 b\*min-2), respiratory quotient (1.18±0.06; 1.18±0.08) and oxygen pulse (11±1.8; 11±2.4 ml\*b-2) were detected in the healthy compared to the hypertensive elderly subjects. Δ[deoxyHb] increased as a function of absolute and relative exercise intensity, reaching upon exhaustion 77±17 and 68±13 % of ischemia in healthy and hypertensive subjects, respectively (difference not significant). In both elderly populations, peak O2 extraction, was not significantly different from that of young healthy sedentaries (75±12% of ischemia

## CONCLUSIONS

Our data show that arm maximal exercise capacity is reduced to a similar extent in normotensive and hypertensive older compared to younq subjects. Since O2 utilization by the working muscles appears unaffected, we suggest that an impairment of O delivery is the main responsible for the reduction of arm exercise capacity observed in elderly hypertensive subjects and age-matched healthy sedentaries, compared to young subjects. Furthermore, the relative role of central and peripheral factors in causing the age-related loss of arm exercise capacity is apparently not altered by pathophysiological factors related to compensated hypertension.

# Using Blood Lactate and pH Parameters to Predict Time Trial Performance During Cycling Ergometry

David M. Morris. RacersReady,com, Daphne, AL Email: performax66@aol.com

Lactate/lactic acid accumulation has traditionally been viewed as a contributing factor to metabolic acidosis and fatigue during high-intensity exercise. These associations have led to the use of lactate threshold working capacity as an indicator of performance in competitive endurance events. However, current evidence suggests that lactate production does not contribute to acidosis and that work rate at lactate threshold may not accurately reflect performance in competitions featuring sustained, high-intensity efforts. PurposE: The purpose of this investigation was to evaluate relationships between power outputs at blood lactate threshold, blood maximal lactate steady state, blood pH threshold, and the average power output during a simulated 20 km time trial each determined on a bicycle ergometer. METHoDs: Subjects (N = 13) were trained male and female cyclists and triathletes all permanent residents of moderate altitude (1525-2225). Testing was performed at 1525 or 1860 m. Power outputs were determined during a simulated 20 km time trial (PTT), at blood pH threshold (PpHT), maximal lactate steady state (PMLSS), and blood lactate threshold determined by two methods; 1) the hiahest power output that did not result in consecutive and continued increases in blood lactate concentrations from exercising baseline (PLT), and 2) the highest power output that did not result in consecutive and continued increases of ≥ 1 mmol · L"1 in blood lactate concentrations from exercising baseline (PLT1). RESULTS: PLT (219 ± 32 W), PLT1 (226 ± 26 W), and PMLSS (233 ± 35 W) were all significantly lower than PpHT (261 ± 29 W, P < 0.05) and PTT (257 ± 31 W, P < 0.05). No significant difference was observed between PpHT and PTT (P > 0.05). Significant relationships were observed between each of the predictors, PLT (R² = 0.95), PLT1 (R² = 0.77), PMLSS (R² = 0.67), and PpHT (R² = 0.93), when compared to PTT (P < 0.05). coNcLusIoN: The results demonstrate that PTT was accurately reflected only by PpHT, and that PLT, PLT1 and PMLSS are not representative of competitive performance in 20 km time trials. However, regression equations can improve the predictive capabilities of the power outputs from blood lactate assessments on 20 km time trial performance.

# Substrate Oxidation During Prolonged Upper and Lower-Body Exercise with Glucose Ingestion: Cyclists vs Kayakers

Jonathan Tremblay1, François Péronnet, FACSM1, Denis Massicotte, FACSM², Carole Lavoie. 1Université de Montréal, Montréal, PQ, Canada. Université du Québec à Montréal, Montréal, PO, Canada. 3Université du Québec à Trois-Riviéres, Trois-Rivières, PO, Canada. Email: jonathan.tremblay@umontreal.ca

Substrate oxidation during 120-min upper and lower-body exercise (UBE and LBE: arm cranking vs cycling) was compared in recreational cyclists (n = 6, 67±6 kg, VOmax = 45±5 and 69±7 mL·kg1·min" for UBE and LBE respectively) and kayakers (n = 6, 75±8 kg, VO2max = 51±9 and 55±4 mL·kg1·min-1 for UBE and LBE respectively) at \~50% of their maximal power output on each ergometer (cyclists: 69±13 and 182±22 W vs kayakers: 89±10 and 159±6 W, UBE and LBE respectively), with water (22 mL·kg1) or 13C-labelled glucose ingestion (2 g-kg1), using indirect respiratory calorimetry corrected for urea excretion in urine and sweat combined with tracer techniques. Protein oxidation was not different between cyclists and kayakers but its contribution to the energy yield was higher in UBE than in LBE in both cyclists (7.4±0.2 vs 3.8±0.1 %, in UBE and LBE respectively) and kayakers (6.0±0.2 vs 4.8±0.1 %, in UBE and LBE, respectively) because of the lower energy expenditure during UBE than LBE. When only water was ingested, total carbohydrate (CHO) oxidation was higher during LBE than UBE in both cyclists and kayakers, also because of the higher workload sustained. The contribution of CHO oxidation to the energy yield was similar during UBE and LBE in kayakers (66.6±6.6 and 68.0±6.4 %, respectively) but was higher in cyclists during UBE than LBE (70.6±6.7 vs 65.2±5.7 %). Glucose ingestion increased total CHO oxidation during UBE and LBE especially in cyclists during UBE (cyclists: 79.6±6.4 and 73.0±2.1 %; kayakers: 78.4±1.1 and 76.8±2.1 %, in UBE and LBE, respectively). This was due to a large oxidation rate of exogenous glucose which was significantly higher in kayakers than cyclists and during LBE than UBE (0.64±0.16 vs 0.71±0.15 g/min in UBE and LBE, respectively, in kayakers, vs 0.51±0.15 and 0.62±0.14 g/min in cyclists). The contribution of exogenous glucose oxidation was also slightly higher in kayakers than in cyclists especially during LBE (kayakers: 25.7±6.1 and 21.2±4.6 %; cyclists: 24.3±6.7 and 18.6±4.0 %, in UBE and LBE respectively). Exogenous glucose ingestion significantly spared endogenous CHO: the contribution of endogenous glucose oxidation was significantly reduced to 52-55, vs 65-71 % with water ingestion. These results show that substrate selection and exogenous glucose oxidation are different during prolonged exercise at \~50 % of the maximal workload during arm cranking and cycling, and favours CHO oxidation during arm cranking. This phenomenon is more pronounced in subjects who regularly perform LBE than in those accustomed to UBE.

Supported by NSERC

Cheng-Jung Chung, Hsin-Liang Chen, Chang-Jun Wu, Trevor-Ching Chen. National Chia-Yi University, Chia-Yi, Taiwan. Email: seasonal1797@hotmail.com

(2) Compare to other researches, they found that the torque in athletes (soccer, basketball, and others...) or the untrained subjects to perform 3050times knee extension is decline 41% (Kawabata et al., 2000; Pincivero et al., 2003). The decline percentage is more than out research 19%. It may reflect that the badminton athletes lower limb have higher resistance ability. # Phosphocreatine Metabolism and Acidosis during Repeated Bouts of Heavy-Intensity Exercise Separated by 15-min Rest

Sean C. Forbes, Graydon H. Raymer, John M. Kowalchuk, R. Terry Thompson, Gregory D. Marsh. The University of Western Ontario, London, ON, Canada Email: sforbes2@uwo.ca

Prior heavy-intensity exercise (HVY) results in a reduced reliance on substrate-level phosphorylation during a subsequent exercise bout when the bouts are separated by 6-min rest. Proposed mechanisms for this response have been associated with acidosis and lactate accumulation.

PuRposE: To determine if a similar favourable energetic response in the second exercise is evident when the bouts are separated by 15-min of rest. In this condition intracellular acid-base status will have returned to pre-exercise resting levels prior to the second bout

METHoDs: Healthy young adult male subjects (n = 7) performed a 6-min bout of HVY isotonic plantar flexion exercise (HVY1) followed by 15-min of rest, then an identical 6-min bout (HVY2). Muscle phosphocreatine (PCr) and intracellular acid-base status were measured using 3-tesla 31p-magnetic resonance spectroscopy. Each subject repeated the protocol three times. PCr was expressed as percent (%) of average pre-HVY1 resting value.

REsuLTS: Prior to the onset of exercise, resting intracellular hydrogen ion ([H\*1) was not different (p=0.11) at the onset of exercise in HVY1 [94 nM (SD 4)] and HVY2 [99 nM (SD 8)]. The increase in [H'], during exercise was reduced \~ 45% during HVY2, with endexercise [H\*] lower (p<0.01) in HVY2 [139 nM (SD 38)] than HVY1 [167 nM (SD 48)]. Resting [PCr] was greater (p=0.03) in HVY2 [101.8% (SD 2.1)] than HVY1, while at endexercise, [PCr] was greater (p=0.02) in HVY2 [55.1% (SD 15.1)] than HVY1 [48.7 % (SD 10.9)].

coNcLusIoNs: The lower accumulation of [H'1: (and presumably lactate accumulation) in HVY2 (delta [H+]i 40 nM) than HVY1 (delta [H+], 73 nM), along with the decreased PCr breakdown, are consistent with reduced substrate-level phosphorylation. Therefore, these results demonstrate that the benefits of prior heavy-intensity exercise are evident after 15 min of rest, when intracellular acid-base status has returned to pre-exercise resting levels.

# The Effect of Training and Sustained Exercise on Gastric Ulceration and Gastrointestinal Protein Loss in Racing Sled Dogs

Michael S. Davis. Oklahoma State University, Stillwater, OK Email: msdavis@okstate.edu

PuRposE: Prolonged submaximal exercise is frequently associated with signs of gastrointestinal disease, including gastric ulceration, gastrointestinal bleeding, anc diarrhea, with reports of gastrointestinal bleeding prevalence as high as 10o% in triathletes. The cause of exercise-induced qastrointestinal disease is unknown. We used a novel animal model of prolonged submaximal exercise to test the hypothesis that the development of gastrointestinal dysfunction during exercise is a function of duration of exercise.

METHops: Forty-two Alaskan sled dogs were used in this study: Six doas served as conditioned controls, and the remaining dogs were randomly chosen for examination after 1 to 5 consecutive days of running at 100 miles/day. Gastroduodenoscopy, gastric biopsy, and measurement of gastric permeability were performed 24 hr after cessation of exercise. Intestinal protein loss (represented by fecal alpha-1 protease inhibitor concentration) was measured within 6 h of cessation of exercise. Twelve of the 42 dogs were exarined again after 5 months of detraining to determine the effect of training on gastrointestinal mucosal function.

REsuLTS: Exercise increased gastric permeability (p = 0.04) and endoscopic severity of gastric lesions (p < 0.0oo1), but neither variable was significantly affected by distance traveled. There was no effect of acute exercise on intestinal protein loss. Untrained dogs had significantly lower fecal alpha-1 protease inhibitor concentrations compared to trained. unexercised dogs. There was no effect of training on gastric permeability to sucrose or the endoscopic appearance of the stomach. However, many dogs had gastric biopsies with evidence of gastritis, including those used as conditioned controls and those examinec after 5 months of detraining. Biopsies from exercised dogs had increased staining for apoptotic nuclei in gastric epithelium.

coNcLusIoNs: These data suggest that training for sustained strenuous exercise causes subclinical gastrointestinal dysfunction but more substantial exercise is required to cause clinical alterations, None of these alterations appear to proaress with increasing exercise duration. Exercise-induced apoptosis of gastric epithelium may be an important event in the development of exercise-induced gastric ulcers.

# Effect of Sprint Exercise on Serum Growth Hormone, Ghrelin, IGF-I, IGF-II and IGF-I Bioactivity

Keith A. Stokes², Dave Sykes², Kate L. Gilbert², Jian-Wen Chen², Jan Frystyk². 1University of Bath, Bath, United Kingdom. ²Aarhus University Hospital, Aarhus, Denmark. Email: k.stokes@bath.ac.uk

PURposE: The aim of this study was to examine the growth hormone (GH), insulin-like growth factor (IGF) and ghrelin responses to sprint exercise and to identify whether the number of muscle actions performed during a sprint influences any of these responses. METHoDs: Following ethics committee approval, seven physically active males (mean age (SD), 25.5 (2.9) years; body mass index, 24.9 (3.5) kg/m²) gave their informed consent to participate in this study and were familiarised before completing three trials in a random order. In two exercise trials, participants performed a single 30-s sprint on a cycle ergometer against a resistance equivalent to either 7% (FAST) or 9% (SLOW) of their body mass. In the other trial they rested in the laboratory (CoN). Blood samples were taken pre-, immediately post-, 10 and 30 min post-exercise, and at equivalent times in the CON trial. These were centrifuged after clotting, stored at -20°C and later analysed for serum concentrations of GH, free and total IGF-I, total IGF-II, IGFBP-1, IGFBP-2 and IGFBP-1- bound IGF-I (binary complex), as well as a marker of IGF-I bioactivity (assessed using an IGF-I kinase receptor activation assay; KIRA). Plasma volume changes were used to correct for haemoconcentration following exercise apart from for free IGF-I and IGF-I KIRA signal. Data were analysed using repeated measures ANovA and post hoc paired t-tests, with Bonferroni correction for multiple comparisons, where appropriate. REsuLTS: The GH response was greater in the FAST than the SLOW trial, but this difference was not significant (maximum change from pre-exercise, 23.5 (24.0) vs. 13.2 (13.7) ug/L, P = 0.07; area under the curve, 520 (588) vs. 295 (353) μg/L/30 min, P = 0.11). Thirty minutes after the sprint in both trials, ghrelin concentrations were significantly lower than pre-exercise (pre-exercise vs. 30 min; FAST, 0.62 (0.19) vs. 0.49 (0.16) μg/L, P < 0.001; SLOW, 0.59 (0.15) vs. 0.47 (0.13) μg/L , P < 0.001) and were lower than at the corresponding time in the CON trial (0.61 (0.17) μg/L; vs. FAST, P = 0.003, n.s.; vs. SLOW ${ \bar { P } } = { \bar { 0 . 0 0 1 } } )$ There were no differences in the ghrelin responses between the two exercise trials. Serum concentrations of free IGF-I, total IGF-I, total IGF-II, IGFBP-1, IGFBP-2 and binary complex, and the IGF-I KIRA signal did not change in response to exercise. coNcLusIoN: A single 30-s sprint did not elicit any significant changes in the IGF-related parameters measured in this study, but did result in increased GH and decreased ghrelin concentrations in both exercise trials. Pedal rate influenced the magnitude of changes in GH, but not ghrelin, following exercise.

Scott J. Montain, FACsM1, Lou A. Stephenson1, Samuel N. Cheuvront, FACSM1, Hank C Lukaski², Andrew J. Young, FACSM1. 1US Army Research Institute of Environmental Medicine, Natick, MA. 2ARS Grand Forks Human Nutrition Research Center, Grand Forks ND.

# Efficacy of Caffeinated and Non-Caffeinated Carbohydrate Beverages on Cycling Performance

JohnEric W. Smith, Elizabeth A. Stover, Shannon C. Lovett, Jeff J. Zachwieja, FACSM. Gatorade Sports Science Institute, Barrington, IL. Email: johneric.smith@gatorade.com

PURposE: The purpose of this study was to determine the effect of ingesting a beverage with carbohydrate and caffeine on 40-km cycling time trial performance in a laboratory setting.

METHoDS: Ten male cyclists and triathletes raced a CompuTrainer™m simulated 40-km time trial course four times with the following randomized beverage treatments: placebo before and at 20-km of the time trial (PLA); carbohydrate before and at 20-km (CHO); carbohydrate + caffeine before and carbohydrate only at 20-km (BCAF); carbohydrate only before and carbohydrate + caffeine at 20-km (MCAF). All beverage treatments were 355 ml in volume and contained 18 mEq/L sodium and 3 mEq/L potassium. Test beverages during CHO, BCAF, and MCAF trials were at a 10% carbohydrate concentration anc caffeinated beverages contained 0.282 mg/mL caffeine.

REsuLTS: Heart rate was significantly higher during BCAF compared to all other trials, while heart rate for MCAF was higher only compared to PLA and CHO. Likewise, power output was significantly higher during BCAF as compared to all other trials (p < 0.05) Power output during CHO was reduced compared to PLA (p < 0.05). An increased incidence of nausea was observed in the CHO and MCAF trials compared to the PLA and BCAF trials (p < 0.05). Despite improvements in power output for the caffeine trials, time (in minutes) to complete the 40-km course was not significantly different among treatments (PLA = 67 88 ± 1 83 CHO = 68 00 ± 1 72 BCAE = 67 44 ± 1 79 MCAF = 67 65 ± 1 681

coNcLusIoNs: Adding a small amount of caffeine to a 10% carbohydrate beverage consumed before laboratory racing elevated power output approximately 3-4% but this was not sufficient to statistically improve overall cycling performance as measured by time to complete the simulated 40-km distance. Consuming a 10% carbohydrate beverage before and during high intensity 40-km cycling can lead to an increased incidence of nausea and possibly limit performance.

# Caffeine Co-ingested with Carbohydrate: Ergogenic Effects Without Altered Metabolism During Exercise in the Heat

Melinda Millard-Stafford, FACSM1, Kirk J. Cureton, FACSM², Jonathan E. Wingo², Jennifer Trilk², Gordon L. Warren, FACsM. Georgia Institute of Technology, Atlanta, GA. ZUniversity of Georgia, Athens, GA. 3Georgia State University, Atlanta, GA. Email: mindy.millardstafford@ap.gatech.edu

puRPosE: This double-blind, repeated-measures experiment examined the effects of a caffeinated sports drink during prolonged cycling in a warm, humid environment.

METHoDS: Sixteen highly-trained male cyclists completed three trials: placebo carbohydrate-electrolyte sports drink (CES), and caffeinated sports drink (CES+CAF) containing 195 mg/L caffeine. Subjects cycled for 135 min, alternating between 60 and 75%vo2max every 15 min for the first 120 min followed by a 15-min performance ride at self-selected intensity, Maximal voluntary (MvC) and electrically-evoked contractile properties of the knee extensors were measured before and after cycling.

RESuLTS: Work completed during the performance ride was 15-23% greater for CES+CAF compared to the other beverages. Ratings of perceived exertion were lower with CES+CAF compared to placebo and CES. At 120 min, blood glucose and carbohydrate oxidation were siqnificantly lower in placebo compared to CES+CAF and CES; but CAF+CE was hiqher than CES only at the end of exercise. Following cycling, the MVC strength loss was significantly less (P< 0.05) for CES+CAF compared to the other beverages (5% vs. 15%). Data from the interpolated twitch technique indicated that the attenuated MVC strength loss with CES+CAF was explained by reduced intrinsic muscle fatigue.

CoNcLusIoNs: Improved performance with CES+CAF is independent of alterations in substrate utilization or energy metabolism. Central and peripheral effects of caffeine on the nervous system that do not alter muscle activation may alter perception of effort and contribute to improved performance. # Effect of Vitamin "E" Over Professional Marathon Runners Performance

Asdrubal Auqusto Florençano Nascimento, Rodrigo Antonio Martins Lopes, Marcos Yukio Yui, Giovanni Novaes. ESEFIC-Escola Superior de Educação Fisica de Cruzeiro, Cruzeiro, Brazil.

Email: gutonascimento@ig.com.br

purposE: The high performance sports have freguently relied on the use of supplements and ergogenic aids, enabling athletes to achieve better results, lower time, reach greater distances, jump hiqher, and lastly, beat records. The use of antioxidant supplements ir endurance sports has been exhaustinaly studied, and seems to improve results as to muscular recovery and fatique reduction. Thus, the obiective of this study was tc investigate the action of different doses of vitamin "E" on the performance of marathon runners, as well as to investigate the possibilities of implementing these supplements in large scales for long- and half-distance athletes.

METHoDs: For such, 90 marathon runners, males, between 25 and 35 years old were daily supplemented, each group with a distinct dose of vitamin "E", during a six-month period. Before the beginning of the supplementation period, the body composition, glucose, total cholesterol, Maximum VO2, maximum and resting cardiac frequency were evaluated. This protocol was carried out monthly, so as to follow the changes and evolutions in the athletes' performance. At the end of the experiment, the athletes were re-evaluated and their performance measured again. The subjects' training was not modified. The coach kept following the program, therefore this study chose not to alter it either.

REsuLTS: It was possible to perceive with this result that doses above 1.ooo international units seem to be more efficient where performance improvement is concerned; however, there are not significant differences among the doses of 1,000, 1,200 and 1,500 international units. There was a significant reduction of the lactate concentration at the end of the tests and re-tests, as well as reduction of racing time in shots of 1,000, 5,oo0 and

10,000 meters and of maximum and resting cardiac frequencies, and increase of Maximum VO2. There was not any significant alteration in glucose and cholesterol levels.

CONCLUSIoNS: Therefore, the positive and effective action of this vitamin on the performance of long- and half-distance athletes seems to be real. However, more studies with a larger number of athletes and modalities are necessary, since the present study focused only on marathon runners.

# Antioxidant Supplementation in Men Attenuates the Exercise-Induced Increase in mRNA Expression of PDK4 and IRF-1 Following Prolonged Cycling

David J. Raphael, Mazen J. Hamadeh, Jan J. Kaczor, Steven K. Baker, Mark A. Tarnopolsky. McMaster University, Hamilton, ON, Canada.

puRposE: We investigated the effects of antioxidant supplementation on skeletal muscle mRNA expression of genes involved in substrate metabolism (FOXO1, PDK4, and PPARy) mitochondrial biogenesis (PGC-1a and mitofusin2) and oxidative stress management (SOD2, GPX1, catalase, IRF-1, and JunB) in response to moderate intensity endurance exercise.

METHoDs: Following a placebo-controlled, double-blind, parallel, random design, 20 healthy, young, sedentary men performed two separate bouts of cycling for 90 min at 65% VO>max. The first bout occurred following 14 days of supplementation with placebo (PL) whereas the second bout occurred after 14 days of supplementation with either PL (n = 10) or antioxidants (ANT, n = 10). Muscle biopsies were taken from the vastus lateralis prior to and 3 h after exercise, and analyzed for the expression of the following genes: FOXO1, PDK4, PPARy, PGC-1a, mitofusin2, SOD2, GPX1, catalase, IRF-1, and JunB.

RESuLTS: Exercise increased the mRNA expression of FOXO1 (4.7 fold, P < 0.001), PDK4 (10 fold, P < 0.001), PGC-1a (16.2 fold, P < 0.001), mitofusin2 (50%, P < 0.001), SOD2 (50%, P = 0.027), GPX1 (41%, P = 0.017), IRF-1 (4.3 fold, P < 0.001), and JunB (23%, F < 0.001). ANT supplementation attenuated the exercise-induced increase in the absolute mRNA expression of PDK4 (-58%, P = 0.045) and the fold change of IRF-1 during the second exercise bout (-60%, P = 0.051). There was a 'second bout' effect, whereby changes in mRNA expression of some genes were apparent prior to and after the second bout of exercise, 2 weeks following the first bout, in both absolute expression (FOxO1 30%, P = 0.035; mitofusin2 +72%, P < 0.001; SOD2 +60%, P = 0.001; and IRF-1 -29%, P = 0.034) and fold change due to exercise (FOXO1 -71%, P = 0.005; PDK4 -73%, P = 0.006; and JunB -48%, P = 0.038).

coNcLusIoNs: Our results indicate that acute exercise up-requlates skeletal muscle mRNA expression of genes involved in substrate metabolism, mitochondrial biogenesis anc oxidative stress management and that this is attenuated only in PDK4 and IRF-1 following ANT supplementation, In addition, we are the first to establish a second bout effect at the transcriptional level for genes involved in all three outcome measures. (This research was funded by NSERC)

# The Effects of Oral Creatine in Combination with specific Nutrition to Enhance Adolescent Sports Performance.

Daniel P. Dami, FACSM. Rockwood Clinic, Spokane, WA. Email: ddami@rockwoodclinic.com

Organized physical activity in the in the adolescent population is at the highest level ir recorded history, Despite having an obese epidemic in the pediatric population, more kids are finding organized athletics in the world then ever before. Most of these athletic adventures are taken up because of friendships, boredom, parent involvement, weight loss implementation, or superhero goals in which the kids would like to achieve. But nonetheless, superior athletes are being born every day. Due to the mass entrance of athletes and what the competition has induced, the way to improve each individual's athletic ability has become an art in itself.

This study was a Cause and Effect prospective study involving 20 sixteen-year-old male football plavers from Spokane Washington. The study looked at the use of oral creatine and the combination of high amounts of oral protein and carbohydrates and what role it would play in the formation of muscle mass, strength, agility, quickness and speed. The study was a 26 week repeated design using two main groups and two sub groups. One main group would eat high amounts of protein and carbohydrate, as well as supplement their diet with 10 grams of oral creatine monophosphate on a daily reqimen. The second mair group would eat randomly with the addition of 10 grams of creatine monophosphate. The two sub groups would not have any creatine in their diets, plus one group would eat randomly and the other would have high amounts of protein and carbohydrates. All of these groups would go through an identical 4-day exercise program that would consist of a 2 day on, one day off, 2 day on weight resistance training routine for 26 weeks. These same groups would be tested every 6 weeks and the results gathered logged and statistically evaluated, Also certain measurements of muscle size, and body fat ratios would be calibrated to go along with overall muscle mass development

The study showed that the subjects consuming oral creatine and proper nutrition had a 20 % improvement in their physical performance when place into specific speed, strength, and agility testing. They also would increase muscle mass and decrease body fat percentages without any side effects from the creatine. This concludes that even at the adolescent level, creatine and proper nutrition has an essential role in the elite athletes of the future

59

## Metabolic

# Effects of Arachidonic Acid on Skeletal Muscle Protein Metabolism and Signaling

Craig E. Broeder, FACSM, David R. Bisterfeldt, Allison Wilson. Benedictine University, Lisle, IL. Email: cbroeder@ben.edu

PuRposE: With aging, muscle mass naturally declines due to a combination of factors including decreased activity levels, a reduction in anabolic hormone production, and neuromuscular changes. Much of the catabolic effects of aqing are attributed to the attenuation of protein synthesis resulting from a reduction in translational initiation anc transcription essential cellular anabolic machinery, which are activated, in contrast, by phosphorylation of the mammalian target of rapamycin (mTOR) at Ser2448. Peptide hormones such as insulin and insulin-like growth factor (IGF-1) elicit their anabolic effects through activation of mTOR. Interestingly, the essential fatty acid arachidonic acid (AA) has been shown to mimic IGF-1 activity in vitro thereby enhancing protein synthesis in vascular smooth muscle cells incubated in a medium containing 25uM AA (Neeli et al. 2003). It was proposed that AA may enhance skeletal muscle hypertrophy in vivo through its effects on inflammation repair responses, ionic membrane transport, and cell signaling Recently, evidence in humans has shown that dietary supplementation of arachidonic acid (Molecular Nutrition's X-Factor) may lead to muscular hypertrophy in resistance training men.

METHoDs: Thus, this study's purpose was to determine what effects varying concentrations of AA (12.5, 25.0, 50.0, and 100uM) had in vitro on myotube development and androgen receptor expression using mouse C2c12 mvoblast cells.

REsuLTs: Cell proliferation assays showed that increasing concentrations of AA enhanced myotube development up to 50uM. However, at 100uM concentrations, AA supplementation was cytotoxic to the C2C12 cells in vitro. Simultaneous immunohistochemical staining with DAPI (nucleus), phalliodin (actin), and myosin heavy chain polyclonal antibodies indicated AA supplementation up to 50uM caused myotube fusion and hypertrophy by enhancing myosin and actin deposition. However, although upregulation of testosterone receptors plays a major role in skeletal muscle development western blots using androgen receptor polyclonal antibodies indicated that AA-enhanced myotube hypertrophy was not caused by up-regulation in testosterone receptor expression

coNcLusIoNs: These results indicate AA supplementation may enhance skeletal muscle protein synthesis up to 50uM. Future studies need to clarify the intracellular signaling pathway responsible.

# Short-Term Creatine Supplementation Does Not Enhance Work Capacity in Multiple Sclerosis Individuals

Steven K. Malin, Nancy Cotugna, Chengshun Fang. University of Delaware, Newark, DE Email: smalin@udel.edu

Multiple Sclerosis (MS) is characterized by demyelinization of the white matter surrounding nerves that contributes to impaired muscle metabolism and physiology. Recently, the use of creatine (Cr) supplementation has been demonstrated to improve muscle strength and oppose fatique in neuroloqically diseased individuals. Previously only one study had investigated the use of Cr supplementation in MS individuals (20g/d for 5 days) and showed no effects on total work. The purpose of this study was to evaluate the effect of exogenous Cr on total work over a 14-day period in MS individuals to determine if an extended duration would improve work capacity. Work capacity was defined as the ability to improve fatigue resistance, effort levels and total work during exercise. Eleven MS subjects (18-60y; Expanded Disability Status Score 3.2 ± 0.3) partook in a randomly assigned double-blind cross-over trial with a 14-day ingestion period of exogenous Cr (5g, 4 times daily, day 1-7: 2.5g, 2 times daily, day 8-14), 3-week wash-out, and a 14-day ingestion period of placebo. Total work was measured by a Biodex Dynamometer for 3 bouts of 30 maximal knee extensions and flexions at 180°/s with 1 minute of recovery between bouts. Fatigue Severity Scale (control=3.61 ± 1.54 vs. treat=3.54 ± 1.66; p=0.73) and Rates of Perceived Exertion (control=13.55 ± 1.91 vs. treat=13.13 ± 2.72; p=0.48) were also assessed and found to be non-significant between periods. Total work was non-sianificant for between groups effect (control=1329.66] ± 175.49] vs. treat=1313.14] ± 200.54J; p=0.81) or for test of within-subject effects on knee extension (p=0.52). There was no group difference for knee flexion (control=1308.28] ± 165.56] vs. treat=1302.10] ± 189.64]; p=0.93), or within-subject effects (p=0.46). Therefore, an extended ingestion period of 14-days with Cr supplementation does not result in an improvement on work capacity in MS individuals.

## Pulmonary

# Ventilatory Threshold is Underestimated in Athletes with Ventilatroy Equivalent Method due to a Mathematical Problem

Hirotaka Nishijima1, Noriteru Morita², Koichi Okita², Takeshi Murakami. 1Sapporo Health Promotion Center, Sapporo, Japan. Asai Gakuen University, Ebetsu, Japan Email: nishijima@sapporo-hpc.com

PURPosE: For the visual determination of ventilatory threshold (VT) on the data plot twc methods have been most commonly employed: a non-linear increase in Vco2 (or VE) plotted against VO2 (V-slope method) and an increase in a VE/VO2 ratio plotted against time or power output (ventilatory equivalent method, VEQ), without a concomitant rise in a VE/Vco2 ratio. For the visual determination of a VT break point on the graph, however, along pre-VT data points the VCO2 vs. VO2 plot must show a linear rise (V-slope) and the VE/VO2 values must be constant with the graph showing a level plot (VEQ). The purpose of the study was to demonstrate that a linear rise on V-slope does not necessarily signify a level plot on VEQ purely for a mathematical reason, causing difficulty in break point detection. METHoDs: Eight athletic young males (the mean age of 22, group A), 9 healthy non-athletic young males (the mean age of 24, B), 9 healthy middle-aged males (the mear age of 47, C), 8 cardiac middle-aged male patients (the mean age of 52, D) were studied during symptom-limited ramp bicycle exercise using a breath-by-breath expiratory gas analyzer. REsuLTS: The mean peak VO2 (ml/kg/min) was 65.8, 46.3, 34.5, and 21.3, respectively in group A, B, C and D. VT using V-slope was significantly greater than VT using VEQ in groups A and B, but not in C and D (VT by V-slope vs VEQ; 40.4 vs 25.3 in group A and 28.6 vs 24.6 in B). When a linear regression line was obtained from pre-VT exercise data points for Vco2 vs VO2 (V-slope), it did not necessarily cross the oriain of the graph. The mean x-intercept was 6.3, 5.1, 4.3 and 2.3, respectively for group A, B, C and D, although the slope of the linear equation did not significantly differ among groups. The similar shift from the origin ocurred for the VE vs VO2 plt. A significant non-zero intercept results in the following mathematical consequences. In a general linear equation, y=ax + b (y=VCO2 or VE, and x=VO2 in V-slope graph with a positive a ); if b=0 (the line crosses the origin), then y/x=a (a level line on the VEQ plot). Whereas, if b ≠0 and negative, then y/x=a - (b/x); y/x is not constant, it will continue to rise until x is large enough so b/x becomes negligible. Therefore, on the VEQ plot a true physiological rise in ventilatoy equivalent (VE/VO2), a break point due to VT, will be superimposed on the preexisting upslope, making a break point difficult to discern. Although mathematical, this phenomenon probably has a physiological basis as well. coNcLusIoNs: In athletes, the ventilatory equivalent method underestimates ventilatory threshold due to an inherent mathematical problem.

62

## Pulmonary

# Heliox Delays Exercise Dynamic Hyperinflation and Leg Muscle Fatigue in Ventilatory Limited Patients with COPD

Scott J. Butcher², Olle Lagerguist². Stewart R. Petersen², David F. Collins². Darcy D. Marciniuk², Richard L. Jones1. 1University of Alberta, Edmonton, AB, Canada. 2University of Saskatchewan, Saskatoon, SK, Canada. Email: scott.butcher@ualberta.ca

PURPosE: Patients with COPD exhibit exercise intolerance that is due to dynamic hyperinflation or leg muscle fatigue, but it is unknown how these exercise limitations interact. We hypothesized that. by delaving dynamic hyperinflation with heliox, exercise tolerance and leg muscle fatique would increase in patients limited by ventilation, and not in those limited by leg muscle fatique

METHoDS: Eleven patients with COPD (FEV1 52 ± 17% predicted, VO2max 14 ± 4.6 ml/kg/min) completed two randomized exercise bouts at 80% of peak power output on a cycle ergometer breathing either room air or heliox (21% O2, 79% He) and one exercise bout breathing heliox but stopping at isotime on the room air test. Exercising end-expired lung volume was determined from inspiratory capacity (IC). Contractile leg muscle fatigue was determined by direct motor point magnetic stimulation to obtain vastus lateralis potentiated twitch prior to exercise and at 5, 10, and 20 minutes post exercise. Patients were grouped into fatiguers (F; 5 minute potentiated twitch (5PT) ≤ 85% of pre exercise value on the room air test) and non fatiquers (NF).

RESULTS: Seven of the 11 patients were NF (5PT 93 ± 4.9%) and increased their exercise endurance time while breathing heliox from 355 ± 203 to 610 ± 317s (p<0.001) while exercise endurance time did not change in the four F (5PT 74 ± 6.9%). At end exercise, the NF had a lower IC on both the room air and heliox tests (1.47 ± 0.38L and 1.57 ± 0.50L vs. 2.23 ± 0.41L and 2.58 ± 0.30L, respectively; p<0.01) and reached a higher end inspiratory lung volume (EILV; 96.6 ± 2.2 and 96.6 ± 2.2% vs. 92.6 ± 4.2 and 88.7 ± 5.9%, respectively, p<0.05). The increased exercise time with heliox in the NF resulted in a greater level of muscle fatigue (5PT decreased to 73.6 ± 6.4%; p<0.001). At isotime with heliox, the NF group demonstrated an increased IC (1.89 ± 0.59L), a lower EILV (93.3 ± 3.7%) and a similar level of muscle fatigue (89.8 ± 5.5%)(p<0.05). The change in exercise time was most highly correlated with room air 5PT (r = 0.79, p<.01) and EILV (r = 0.68, p< 0.05) and there was a significant association between room air 5PT and EILV (r = -0.77, p<0.01) indicating that patients with the least amount of muscle fatique were more ventilatory limited and had a greater response to breathing heliox.

coNcLusIoNs: The ability to decrease exercise hyperinflation with heliox in patients with COPD depends on the relative contributions of ventilatory and leg muscle limitations during cvcling exercise, Heliox was less effective in improving exercise tolerance in patients limited by leg fatigue, suggesting that targeted leg muscle rehabilitation may be more beneficial in these patients

63

## Pulmonary

# Effects of Hypoxia on Pulmonary $\scriptstyle \mathbf { o } _ { 2 }$ Uptake Dynamics during Heavy Exercise

Haiyina Zhou, Nicola Lai, Justin Fiutem, Marco E. Cabrera, FACSM. Case Western Reserve University, Cleveland, OH Email: hxz23@case.edu

Hypoxia decreases maximal oxygen uptake (VO-max) and exercise performance as indicated by the maximum work rate (WRmax). However, it has not been well established whether hypoxia either slows down or speeds up pulmonary VO dynamics during constant work rate heavy intensity exercise. We hypothesized that hypoxia would increase the amplitude of the slow component -compared to normoxia- when exercising at the same a priori-determined work rate of heavy intensity. Accordingly, we determined the VO responses to maximal and constant work rate (moderate and heavy intensity) exercise under normoxia and hypoxia $\langle \mathsf { F } _ { 1 } \mathsf { O } _ { 2 } { = } 0 . 1 2 \rangle$ in eight young adults. In agreement with previous findings, vO2 steady-state values during moderate intensity exercise under hypoxia and normoxia were similar. During heavy exercise, however, we found that VO, dynaric responses were faster and the VO steady-state values were much lower than those obtained under normoxic conditions. Moreover, at the end of the heavy intensity exercise test $, \lor \lor _ { 2 }$ kinetics started to decrease (\~50%), while VCO2 kept on increasing, even if work rate was maintained constant. This behavior may be the result of a decrease in arterial oxygen content, because of a right shift in the hemoglobin dissociation curve induced by a concomitant increase in H† and lactate concentration. As a consequence of a lower VO2 during the early period of the steady-state (4-5 min) under hypoxic conditions, lactate accumulates in blood and alters the total amount of oxygen available to the contracting muscle during the later period (last 1-2 min) leading to a drop in VO2 and thus to an increased anaerobic contribution to the energy demand. Supported by grant (P50 GM-66309) from the National Institute of General Medial Science (NIH)

## Pulmonary

# Cerebral and Muscle Oxygenation During Incremental Exercise in Normoxia and Hypoxia

Andrew C. Dimmen, Andrew W. Subudhi, Robert C. Roach, FACSM, University of Colorado Altitude Research Center, Denver and Colorado Springs, CO. Email: adimmen@uccs.edu

PURPOSE: To determine if fatigue at maximal aerobic power output was associated with a critical level of cerebral oxygenation, thirteen male cyclists performed incremental exercise tests (25 W·min"2 ramp) under normoxic (NORM: 21% F,O2) and acute hypoxic (HYPOX: 12% FO2) conditions. METHODS: Near infrared spectroscopy (NIRS) was used to assess changes in cerebral and muscle oxygenation during incremental exercise. Concentration (μM) changes in oxy- and deoxy-hemoglobin (ΔO2Hb, Δ HHb) in the left vastus lateralis and frontal cortex (Oxymon, Artinis, The Netherlands) were measured and used tc calculate an index of change in tissue oxygenation $( \Delta H b _ { \mathrm { d i f f } } = \Delta O _ { 2 } H b - \Delta H H b )$ Repeated measures ANovA analyses were performed across treatments and relative workrates (a=0.05). RESULTS: During NORM, cerebral oxygenation (ΔHbdirf) was maintained up to 75% peak power output (Powe $\mathfrak { r } _ { \mathfrak { p e a k } } )$ , but decreased thereafter. Muscle oxygenation (∆Hbart) progressively decreased up to 75% Powerpeak, but was unchanged thereafter. During HYPOx cerebral oxygenation progressively decreased across all workrates, while muscle oxygenation again decreased up to 75% Powerpeak and remained unchanged thereafter. The magnitudes of changes were greater in HYPOX than NORM for cerebral but not muscle ΔHbdiff at 100% Powerpeak. CoNCLUSION: These results demonstrate a large tolerance for changes in cerebral oxygenation at maximal aerobic power output and do not support the notion that a critical level of frontal cortex oxvgenation limits exercise in NORM.

## Phorbol Ester-induced Contraction of the Rat Aorta is ERK1/2 and p38 Independent

Brenda M. Hill², Kevin M. Rice², Devashish H. Desai³, Sean E. Thatcher³, Gary L. Wright4, Robert T. Harris², Eric R. Blough². 1West Virginia State University, Institute, WV. 2Marshall University, and Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Marshall University, Huntington, WV. 3Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Marshall University, Huntington, WV. 4Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Marshall Universtiy, Huntington, WV.

BAcKGRouND: The protein kinase C activator, 12-deoxyphorbol 13-isobutyrate (DPBu), is thought to induce smooth muscle contraction in a calcium-independent manner. The mechanism(s) of this response is unclear. Recent data has suggested that the mitogen: activated protein kinase (MApk) pathway may be involved in vascular contraction via an increase in sensitivity of the contractile machinery however, whether this occurs in the aorta is not well understood.

PuRPosE: This study tested the hypothesis that ERK1/2 and p38 activation are essentia steps in the onset of contraction (tension development) in the rat aorta.

METHoDs: The thoracic aortas of adult rats were surgically removed, cleaned of adherent tissue and cut into rings \~ 0.3 cm in width. After equilibration, isometric tension was measured in response to PKC stimulation (DPBu)10-'M, in the absence and presence of rho kinase (Y-27632) and / or myosin light chain kinase (ML-9) inhibition.

REsuLTs: Inhibition of rho kinase or myosin light chain kinase either separately or together had no effect on maximal isometric tension. After inhibition we examined by Western immunoblot the levels of phosphorylated extracellular requlated kinase (ERK)1/2- MAPK and p38-MAPK

concLusIoN: The results suggest that phorbol ester contraction is independent of ERK1/2- and p38-MAPK activation. The effect of rho kinase and MLCK inhibition on CPI-17 phoshporylation, a potent inhibitor of myosin liaht chain phosphatase will be discussed. (Research supported in part by NIH Grant RR16477and NSF Grant 0314742)

## Cardiovascular

## Pressure-Induced Regulation of Mitogen Activated Protein Kinases in the Rat Inferior Vena Cava

Devashish H. Desai1, Kevin M, Rice², Sunil K. Kakarla³, Deborah L. Preston³3, Ernest M. Walker Jr.1, Paulette S. Wehner², Eric R. Blough². 1Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Marshali University, Huntington, Wv. 2Marshall University, and Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Marshall University, Huntington, WV. 3Marshall University, Huntington, WV.

BAckGRouND: Diabetes mellitus is an important risk factor for increased vein graft failure after bypass surgery. However, the cellular and molecular mechanism(s) underlying graft failure in this population remain largely unexplored. Recent reports have suggested that the pathological remodeling of vein grafts may be mediated by mechanically-induced activation of the mitogen activated protein kinase (MAPk) signaling pathways.

PuRPosE: In this study, we examined the differences in arterial pressure-induced MAPk activation between diabetic and non-diabetic veins.

METHoDS: Venae cavae from lean (nondiabetic) and obese (diabetic) Zucker rats were isolated and incubated ex vivo for 3omins under basal or pressurized conditions (120 mmHg). MAPK protein expression, basal phosphorylation and the pressure induced changes in phosphorylation were evaluated by immunoblotting.

RESuLTS: Immunoblot analysis of the MAPK family extracellular signal-regulated kinase (ERK1/2), p38, and c-Jun NH2-terminal kinase (JNK) MAPKs showed differential expression and activation with diabetes. The expression and basal activation of p38β- (53.2 ± 13.4%; 26.7 ± 7.0%), JNK 1- (21.5 ± 9.3%; 19.4 ± 11.6%) and JNK 3-MAPK (16.8 ± 3.3%; 29.5 ± 17.6%) were significantly higher (P<0.05) in the diabetic vena cava (DVC). However, in contrast to the non-diabetic vena cava, with elevated intraluminal pressure in the diabetic vena cava, there was no change in phosphorylation of ERK1, JNK2, or any of the p38- MAPKs.

concLusIoN: These data suggest that diabetes is associated with significant alterations in the ability of the vena cava to activate MAPk signaling. (Supported by funds from NSF Grant 0314742)

## Shear Stress Activates Akt in Cultured A7r5 Aortic Smooth Muscle Cell Line

Sriram P. Mupparaju1, Devashish H. Desai², Kevin M. Rice³, Sunil K. Kakarla1, Eric R. Blough. 1Marshall University, Huntington, WV. 2Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Marshall University, Huntington, Wv. "3Marshall University, and Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Huntington, WV. "Marshall University, and Joan C. Edward School of Medicine, Marshall University, Huntington, WV.

BAckGRouND: Vascular intervention procedures such as balloon angioplasty and stent implantation lead to denudation of the vessel endothelium, exposing the underlying smooth muscle laver directly to effects of blood flow, especially shear stress Smooth muscle cells are shown to proliferate in areas of damaged endothelium. However, the effect of shear stress on smooth muscle cell signaling has not been studied in depth. Constitutive Akt activity is required for cell survival and drastic mechanical stimuli may be expected to regulate Akt signaling.

PuRPosE: In this study, we examined time dependent changes in activation of Akt, MAPK and p70S6k related signaling molecules in response to orbital shear stress on cultured A7r5 cells.

METHoDs: A7r5 cells cultured to sub-confluence on 15Omm culture dishes were subjectec to orbital shear for zero, 5min, 15min, 30min, 1h, 4h and 24h at 210rpm. SDS-PAGE and immunoblot analyses were performed using antibodies towards phosphorylated and unphosphorylated forms of various molecules of the Akt signaling pathway.

REsuLTS: Akt phosphorylation was found to increase to 165% of control at 15min then staving nearly constant up to 1h with a maximum phosphorylation at 4h (185% of control) Upon exposure to shear stress, GSK-3β phosphorylation was markedly decreased at Smin (50% of control) and stayed low up to 4h (40% of control), followed by recovery to 70% of control at 24h. The phosphorylation levels of mTOR, p70S6k and PTEN were also found to be in keeping with the activation of Akt in response to shear stress

coNcLusIoN: Akt signaling may be responsible for proliferative response of vascular smooth muscle cells when exposed to shear stress upon endothelial denudation due to vascular interventional procedures such as angioplasty and vessel arafting, leading tc increased restenosis, These data may provide insiahts into possible pharmacological interventions to prevent or retard the development of restenosis. (Supported by funds from NSF Grant 0314742)

## Cardiovascular

## Intravascular Ultrasound (IvUS) and Coherent Anti-Stokes Raman Scattering (CARs) to Assess Effects of Diet and Exercise on Atherosclerosis

Matthew Locker1, Gregory M. Dick1, Mouhamad Alloosh², Thuc Le², Ji-Xin Cheng², Michael Sturek1. 1Indiana University School of Medicine, Indianapolis, IN. 2Purdue University, West Lafayette, IN. Email: mlocker@jupui.edu

BAckGRouND: Techniques for the detection and evaluation of atherosclerosis are constantly evolving. IvuS provides excellent information about location, but could be improved with regard to identifying stable vs. unstable plaques (determined by relative amounts of collagen and lipid). CARS may offer better information, as vibrational signals from CH, aroups allow the visualization of lipids and second-harmonic generation allows the visualization of collagen.

PURPosE: This study had two goals: 1) to compare IVUS and CARS imaging, and 2) to determine the effect of a hiah fat/cholesterol diet and aerobic exercise on atherosclerosis at the iliac bifurcation. Our long-term goal is to merge IVUS and CARS technology into a single catheter-based probe, as we expect combined imaging methods to improve the detection and characterization of atherosclerosis.

METHoDs: Male Ossabaw swine were divided into three treatment groups (n=7 each) control (C), high fat/cholesterol-fed (H), and H plus exercise (Hx). Pigs were on their respective diets for 50 weeks before the aerobic exercise regimen of 7 weeks. The H diet derived 46% of calories from fat (hydrogenated soybean oil; 56% trans fatty acids) and contained 2% cholesterol by weight. IVUS (3.2 F, 30 MHz catheter, Boston Scientific, Inc.) was used to examine the iliac bifurcation in vivo. Iliac arteries were harvested for CARs imaging in vitro

REsuLTs: Pigs in the H and Hx groups were obese, hyperlipidemic, and insulin-resistant compared to C. IVUS images from H pigs demonstrated 2.8-fold greater atheroma at the iliac bifurcation vs. C. Exercise did not attenuate atheroma in the Hx group (2.9-fold increase vs. C). CARS images allowed the visualization of a layer of lipid-containing cells; the depth of which was increased in H and attenuated in Hx. In addition, CARS was able to resolve collagen within the necintima and each layer of the artery wall.

coNCLUsIoNS: CARS offers much greater spatial resolution than IVUS and detects exercise and diet-induced changes in corpositional nature of atherosclerosis at the iliac bifurcation. We found no sianificant effect of exercise to reduce the extent of atherosclerosis as detected by IvUS. This could be due to the limited duration of exercise training. Alternatively, our data support the idea that dietary changes must accompany an exercise reaimen taraeted at reducina/reversing atherosclerosis. Importantly, however, the CARS data suggest that exercise may alter the composition of atherosclerotic lesions. Support: HL062552, RR013223 (MS)

## Cardiovascular

# Physical Training Enhances Vasodilatory Function of Collateral Arteries Following Femoral Artery Occlusion

Hsiao-tung Yang, Patrick N, Colleran, Zevi Li. Harold M. Lauahlin, FACSM, Ronald L. Terjung, FACSM. University of Missouri, Columbia, MO. Email: yanqh@missouri.edu

To study the effect of exercise training on collateral vessel vasomotor properties, adult male Sprague-Dawley rats with unilateral femoral artery occlusion were run on a rodent treadmill twice per day for 3 wks at a moderate intensity (n=22). Perforating arteries from both non-occluded (coN) and occluded (Occ) hind limb were isolated, cannulated, and pressurized at low collateral-dependent (45 cmH2O), or normal pressure (120 cmH20) Vasomotor responses to sodium nitroprusside (SNP; 1x10-9 to 1x10-4), flow-induced dilation (FID) and phenylephrine (PE; 1x10-9 to 1x10-4) were recorded with a microscopevideo system. Neither training nor occlusion altered the constriction response to PE Training reversed the depressed vasodilatory effect of SNP following occlusion. Maxima vessel diameters were increased 14% and 74% at 45 cmH20, and 11% and 30% at 120 cmH2O for CON and OCC collateral arteries respectively (p<0.05) by training. ACh- or FID induced endothelium dependent vasodilation was enhanced by exercise training (p<0.05). In situ inhibition of cyclooxygenase with indomethecin (5 ÁμM), endothelial nitric oxide synthase with L-NAME (300 ÅμM), or in combination did not eliminate the training enhanced vasodilation induced by ACh or FID. Our results demonstrate that training enhances endothelium dependent vasodilatory function by NOs dependent and NOS independent pathways, likely involving the putative endothelium derived hyperpolarizing factor(s) in the newly developed collateral arteries. Supported by NIH grant HL-37387 and HL-36088.

## Cardiovascular

## The Effects of Physical Activity on Coronary Artery Calcification in Older Adults

Emily J. Tomayko, Kerri-Anne Mullen, Kevin S. Heffernan, Raj Ramanathan, Laura A. Feeney, Ellen M. Evans, Bo Fernhall, FACSM, Kenneth R. Wilund. University of Illinois, Urbana, IL.

PuRPosE: High levels of coronary artery calcium (CAC) are associated with cardiovascular disease mortality, especially in older adults. Pharmacological interventions designed to prevent CAC are largely ineffective; the purpose of this study is to examine the effects of physical activity on the development of CAC and its relationship to bone mineral density and arterial function in elderly individuals.

METHoDs: We recruited 25 adults age 60-80, half of whom were highly-trained master athletes (MA) and half of whom were sedentary (SED). In each subject we measured CAc by electron beam computed tomography, bone mineral density by dual x-ray absorptiometry, and carotid stiffness, compliance and intima-media thickness by ultrasound. We also measured risk factors for CAC, including circulating levels of lipids and mineral reaulatory proteins. including osteopontin. fetuin-A and osteocalcin. Subiects also filled out a 3-day dietary recall and a guided calcium frequency questionnaire.

REsULTS: Our preliminary data shows a trend for lower CAC in the MA group. We also found an inverse relationship between CAC and plasma osteocalcin as well as an inverse relationship between hip bone mineral density (BMD) and plasma osteocalcin. In addition, there was a positive correlation between plasma fetuin A and brachial compliance, and an inverse correlation between fetuin A and brachial stiffness.

coNcLusIoNs: This data indicates that exercise may help prevent or attenuate the progression of CAC in older adults, and suggests that altering circulating levels of mineral requlatory proteins may have a beneficial effect on arterial health and BMD. Additiona analysis of data from this ongoing study may provide further insight into the relationship between exercise, mineral metabolism, and arterial function. Furthermore, it will provide the rationale for examining additional exercise and dietary interventions designed tc prevent the accumulation of CAC in susceptible populations, including the elderly, diabetics, and chronic kidney disease patients.

## Cardiovascular

# Exercise Reduces TRP Channel-Mediated Calcium Influx in Smooth Muscle Cells from Atherosclerotic Coronary Arteries after Stenting in a Porcine Model of Cardiometabolic Risk

Jason M. Edwards, Michael Sturek. Indiana University School of Medicine, Indianapolis, IN. Email: edwardjm@iupui.edu

BACkGRouND: Patients with diabetes or cardiometabolic risk have poor prognosis after balloon angioplasty and coronary stenting. Coronary stents greatly decrease restenosis but accelerated coronary artery disease (CAD) in reqions adjacent to the stent (peri-stent CAD) remains a concern. Ossabaw swine exhibiting characteristics of cardiometabolic risk allow us to identify mechanisms underlying this pathology. Vascular smooth muscle cel proliferation, which is mediated partly by elevated myoplasmic Ca²+ increases, is a major mechanism of atherosclerosis. Transient receptor potential (TRP) Ca²+ channels activated by signals associated with depletion of Ca²  from the sarcoplasmic reticulum (SR) are increased in proliferating smooth muscle cells. Exercise has been shown to prevent SR Ca2 dysregulation in CAD, thus may protect against the increase in TRP channel-mediated Ca2+ influx.

HYPoTHEsIS: Exercise attenuates the increase in TRP channel-mediated Ca² influx in smooth muscle cells of non-stented arteries and in peri-stented regions from obese Ossabaw swine with cardiometabolic risk compared to healthy swine.

METHoDs: Male Ossabaw swine were fed control chow or 2% cholesterol/high fat diet sedentary (H) and exercised trained (HX). Multi-link bare metal stents were placed with 1:1 apposition (not over-inflation injury) verified by intravascular ultrasound (IvUS) after 40-55 weeks on the diets. Percent stenosis was assessed using IVUs 4 weeks later. Coronary smooth muscle cells were dispersed from segments 2-5 mm proximal to the stent (peri-stent) and loaded the fluorescent Ca²+ indicator fura-2. Cells were exposed to caffeine (5 mM) to release and deplete the SR Ca2\* store in the presence of the sarco endoplasmic Ca2' ATPase (SERCA) inhibitor cyclopiazonic acid (1OμM) to assess peak TRP channel-mediated Ca² influx.

REsuLTS: Peri-stented regions had significantly greater stenosis compared to all other segments of the artery aside from the area within the stent. Nifedipine-insensitive, TRP channel-mediated Ca2\* influx in cells from the Ossabaw swine model of the metabolic syndrome were observed. Ca² - influx via TRP channels was greater in H compared to C and HX in non-stented arteries. Elevations in TRP channel-mediated Ca2' influx in peri-stented segments having greater stenosis than non-stented arteries in C and H was sianificantly attenuated in the HX group.

coNCLUsIoN: Arterial segments with greatest stenosis have greatest TRP channelmediated Ca2 influx, which is prevented by exercise training.

## Cardiovascular

# Activation of Adenosine A1 Receptor Induces Coronary Smooth Muscle Cell Proliferation in an in vitro Model of Atherosclerosis

Xin Long, Jason M. Edwards, Pamela G. Lloyd, Eric A. Mokelke, Michael Sturek. Indiana University School of Medicine, Indianapolis, IN. Email: xilong@iupui.edu

PURposE: Ossabaw swine are an excellent large animal model of the cardiometabolic risk. Compared to other breeds (e.g. Yucatan), lean Ossabaws are insulin-resistant and are highly prone to develop obesity and cardiometabolic risk. Restenosis after coronary artery stent placement is a continuing clinical problem that is more severe in patients with cardiometabolic risk. However, the mechanisms underlying increased restenosis in cardiometabolic risk are not clear. Our lab previously showed that activation of adenosine A1 receptors induces proliferation of coronary smooth muscle cell in monolayer cultures Therefore, derangements in adenosine A1 receptor siqnaling could contribute to excessive cell proliferation in restenosis. Our previous work showed that the placement of bare metal coronary stents induced adenosine A1 receptor gene expression in Ossabaws. Hypothesis: Activation of the adenosine A1 receptor will elicit coronary smooth muscle cell proliferation in in vitro organ cultured arterial rings.

METHoDs: We put Ossabaw coronary arterial rings in Petri dish with RPMI media at 37 degree C for 24 hours, which we define as organ culture. Organ cultured rings were treated with either the A1R-selective agonist CCPA (10-bM) or the A1R-selective antagonist DPA (10-6M) or both CCPA (10-M) and DPA (10-M). Two groups of untreated rings at either 37 degree C (organ culture) or 4 degree C (cold store) served as controls. After 24 hour treatment, coronary smooth muscle cells were dispersed from the rings and stained with BrdU. The BrdU incorporation (DNA synthesis) was measured using confocal microscopy to determine the degree of cell proliferation.

REsuLTs: Organ culture increased BrdU incorporation in coronary smooth muscle cells by 5 fold over cold store (p<0.05), demonstrating that organ culture is a useful in vitro model of SMC proliferation and stenosis. CCPA further increased BrdU incorporation by \~4 fold over untreated organ culture control (p<0.05), whereas DPA abolished the increase in DNA synthesis observed in response to CcPA treatment (p<0.05)

CoNCLusIoN: A1 receptor mediates CASMC proliferation in the in vitro organ culture model in the setting of cardiometabolic risk. Support: NIH RR13223, HL62552, ADA.

## Cardiovascular

# Increased Peri-stent Progression of Coronary Artery Disease in Grossly Diabetic Dyslipidemic Pigs, But Not Pigs with Moderate Cardiometabolic Risk

E. O'Hara, J. M. Edwards, M. Alloosh, E. A. Mokelke, M. Sturek. Indiana University Schooi of Medicine, Indianapolis, IN Email: edohara@iupui.edu

PURposE: Drug-coated stents have virtually eliminated coronary restenosis in diabetic and non-diabetic patients; however, major coronary morbidity remains several-fold greater in diabetics. Greater progression of coronary artery disease in regions adjacent to the stent (peri-stent CAD) may be one underlying cause. We used obese Ossabaw swine as a model for moderate cardiometabolic risk and Yucatan swine that were grossly diabetic (alloxan induced) and dyslipidemic to study peri-stent CAD. We hypothesized that coronary stenting elicits increased peri-stent CAD in pigs in proportion to the severity of hyperglycemia and dyslipidemia.

METHoDs: Male swine were fed control chow, thus providing "healthy" control groups. Feeding a 2% cholesterol/high fat diet to Yucatan elicited hyperlipidemia (H), while Ossabaws provided a hyperlipidemic, obese, cardiometabolic risk group (Ho). Yucatan treated with alloxan provided the most severe hyperglycemic/diabetic and dyslipidemic (DD) group. The five groups were maintained on the diets for 30-50 weeks and then bare metal stents were placed in the circumflex (CFx) artery with 1:1 apposition (not overinflation injury) verified by intravascular ultrasound (IVuS). The left anterior descending (LAD) artery was used as a naïve control that did not undergo IvUS at stent placement. Peri-stent CAD was defined as atheroma in segments of the artery greater than 5 mm proximal or distal to the stent and assessed using IVUS 3-4 weeks later.

REsuLTS: Yucatan H were hyperlipidemic (total cholesterol \~7-fold >control), but normoglycemic. Ossabaw HO were moderately hyperlipidemic (total cholesterol \~7-folc >control, triglycerides \~2-fold >control), insulin resistant, mildly hyperglycemic, and hypertensive, thus having greater cardiometabolic risk than Yucatan H. Yucatan DD were profoundly dyslipidemic (total cholesterol \~7-fold >control, triglycerides \~3-fold >control) and hyperglycemic (blood alucose \~4-fold >control). The ratio of atheroma in the stented circumflex to the naive left anterior descending control (stented CFX/naive LAD) gave the best estimate of peri-stent CAD: Yucatan DD = 4.3, Ossabaw HO = 3.3, and Yucatan H = 1.0. Only Yucatan DD peri-stent CAD was significantly (p<0.05) increased

coNcLusIoN: These data are consistent with our hypothesis that bare metal stent placement in coronary artery elicits peri-stent CAD in proportion to the severity of hyperglyceria and dyslipidemia. Future studies will evaluate whether longer duration or more extreme metabolic dysreaulation will elicit increased peri-stent CAD in the Ossabaw swine model of cardiometabolic risk. Support: HL62552, RR13223, HL07802

## Cardiovascular

# Antisense Promoter of Beta Myosin Heavy Chain Gene Responds to Diabetes and Hypothyroidism

Julia Giger, Fadia Haddad, Kenneth M. Baldwin. University of California, Irvine, Irvine, CA. Email: julie.qiger@uci.edu

Myosin heavy chain (MHC) is an integral contractile component of the muscle sarcomere, and is fundamental in determining the rate of cross-bridge cycling, and thus the speed of muscle contraction. Heart muscle expresses two genes encoding MHC isoforms, a and β, which are arranged in tandem 4.5 Kb apart. Rat hearts typically express a predominance of the a MHC isoform and have high intrinsic contractility. Hypothyroid (PTU), hypertensive, and diabetic (STZ) rats express a significantly higher proportion of the β isoform and thus have a lower rate of tension development, but a greater energy economy of force production. The normal human heart predominantly expresses the β isoform, yet there is still an increase in β and a decrease in a MHC isoforms observed in the failing human heart. This antithetical expression of the a and β genes is highly coordinated, but the mechanism underlving this regulation is poorly understood. We discovered an antisense (AS) 3 RNA transcript that starts in the middle of the 4.5Kb (intergenic spacer, IGS) and extends upstream to the BMHC gene promoter region, which makes the AS transcript fully complementary to the BMHC gene. The expression of the AS transcript was positively correlated with levels of a MHC gene sense mRNA and negatively correlated with the β MHC gene sense mRNA.. We hypothesize that the IGS sequence contains a bidirectional promoter that regulates the expression of the two genes, We propose that the IGS bidirectional promoter in the 3' direction drives the transcription of the AS transcript which may serve to interfere with the sense βMHC processing. A promoter corresponding to the - 2285/ -945 reqion of the IGS was inserted into a luciferase plasmid in the 3' to 5' AS direction, and was injected into rat ventricle. This promoter was activated in control heart and decreased greatly in response to PTU and STZ and increased 9x in hyperthyroid rats The promoter activity responded in a manner similar to the endogenous antisense β RNA. When the retinoic acid receptor (RAR) site (a known thyroid hormone receptor cofactor) was mutated within this promoter, the reporter activity was almost abolished in Cont, PTU, and STZ hearts, and greatly diminished T3 responsiveness, indicating that RAR is an important regulatory site.

## SATURDAY, SEPTEMBER 30, 2006 • POSTER SESSION 3

## Cardiovascular

# Exercise-Induced Differential Gene Expression In PBMCs Of Early And Late Pubertal Boys

Shlomit Radom-Aizik, Frank Zaldivar, Szu-Yun Leu, Lori Wilson, Dan M. Cooper. University of California, Irvine, Irvine, CA. Email: saizik@uci.edu

PuRposE: In adults, brief exercise alters gene expression of peripheral blood mononuclear cells (PBMCs) reflecting diverse genetic pathways ranging from cell growth to both pro-and anti-inflammatory processes. Far less is known about these responses in children, although many immune and metabolic responses are substantially influenced by puberty. We hypothesized that PBMC gene expression would be affected by puberty. To test this, we cornpared PBMC gene expression in response to cycle ergometer exercise (\~80% peak WR) in early pubertal boys (EP, n=10, range 8-12 y.o.) with late puberta boys (LP, n=10, 15-18 y.0.)

METHoDS: Blood was sampled before and immediately after exercise. RNA was hybridized to Affymetrix U133+ 2.0 Genechip arrays. Differential gene expression was defined as sianificant using stringent criteria (EDR<0.05. t-test n≤0.0o41).

RESULTS: HR (as % peak) was 91% during exercise in EP compared with 88% in LP (ns). The increase in lactate in EP was significant, 154±40% of baseline, but significantly less than the 326±26% increase in LP. Similarly, PBMCs increased significantly in EP (36±7%) but was significantly less than the increase in LP (70±11%). At baseline, there was no significant difference in gene expression between the two groups. Changes in gene expression were observed after exercise in 1,953 genes (increased in 797 genes) in the LP compared with 98 genes (increased in 71 genes) in EP. Sixty-one of the 98 genes altered in EP were similarly changed in LP, and included increased expression of genes related to Response-to-Stress (Gene Ontology Database Classification) such as heat shock protein-70 peccty hoataGens elated Proteoly Apops cathepsin C, cathepsin W, granzyme A, granzyme B, granzyme H and caspase 6) were significantly upregulated after exercise only in LP.

coNcLusIoNs: Brief exercise alters PBMC gene expression in children. The pattern of change involves diverse genetic pathways, consistent with a global "danger"-type response, perhaps readying PBMCs for a range of physiological responses from inflammation to tissue repair, At the same relative work intensity, more genes were affected in LP than in EP. Whether or not this represents intrinsic maturational properties of immune cells, or, alternatively, results from the different physioloqical responses to the same relative work rate (e.g., lower lactate in EP), remains unknown.
