# The Effects of Nitric Oxide on Lipolysis in Obese Women before and After 10 Days of Exercise Training

Emily A. Johnson, Myung Dong Choi, Raymond M. Kraus, Michael J. Ormsbee, Robert C. Hickner, FACSM. East Carolina University, Greenville, NC. Email:emilyajohnson@hotmail.com

Obesity is a serious condition defined by excess body fat which may contribute to serious health concerns such as Type 2 diabetes. coronary artery disease, and dylipidemia. Nitric oxide (No) has been shown to inhibit lipolysis and obese individuals tend to have more nitric oxide synthase (Nos) content in adipose tissue compared to lean

pURposE: It was the purpose of this study to evaluate the effects of NO on regional lipolysis in obese women before and after ten days of aerobic exercise training.

METHoDs: An index of lipolysis, from dialysate glycerol concentration and nutritive flow measures, was obtained using the microdialysis technique. Three probes were inserted into the abdominal subcutaneous adipose tissue (AAT) and femoral subcutaneous adipose tissue (FAT). Resting lipolysis was evaluated under non-stimulated, and NOS inhibited (LNMMA) conditions. Participants exercised on a cycle ergometer for an hour per day for ten days.

RESuLTS: Dialysate glycerol did not change in response to exercise training in the AAT (100.6±14.7 uM PRE: 125.71±26.6 uM POST) or FAT (123.9±9.7 UM PRE: 135.8±21.8 uM POST). In AAT, dialysate glycerol concentration was higher with NOS inhibition than in the non-stimulated control probe before (160.1±26.8 μM LNMMA; 102.3±7.7 μM CON; p<0.05) and after (184.6±31.9 μM LNMMA; 114.2±16.3 μM CON; p<0.05) training. In FAT, NO suppressed resting lipolysis before (201.1±29.9 μM LNMMA; 140.9±14.4 μM CON; p<0.05) but not after (156.2±26.4 μM LNMMA 118.1±11.5 μM CON, p<0.05) training compared to the control probe.

coNcLusIoN: We found that exercise training did not alter resting, non-stimulated lipolysis. When NOS was inhibited by L-NMMA, lipolysis increased in AAT compared to the control probe before and after exercise training. However, in FAT, lipolysis increased with NOs inhibition before, but not after, exercise training compared to the control probe indicating that exercise training may decrease NO production in FAT. Our results indicate that ten davs of exercise does not provide enough stimulus to alter non-stimulated lipolysis, but may alter the NoS regulation of lipolysis, in obese women.

## Physical Activity Behavior and Lipid Profile in HIV+ Hispanic Adults

Farah A. Ramirez-Marrero, FACSM², Anita M. Rivera-Brown². Barbara A. Smith, FACSM3. 1University of Puerto Rico, Rio Piedras and Medical Sciences Campus, San Juan, PR. University of Puerto Rico - Medical Sciences Campus, San Juan, PR. 3University of Maryland, Baltimore, MD.

Email: framirez@caribe.net

Elevated plasma lipids and glucose are metabolic alterations associated with HIV infection and treatment. Studies have shown that structured aerobic and resistance exercise training help control these metabolic disturbances and reduce cardiovascular disease risk factors in this population. However, the metabolic benefits of an unstructured physical activity lifestyle in HIV+ adults are not clear, Purpose: To determine if HIV+ adults who follow the physical activity recommendations have a better lipid and glucose profile compared to inactive HIV+ adults. Methods: Thirty eight HIV+ adults (16 females, 22 males; age = 46.8±9.8 v) taking antiretroviral medications volunteered to wear an accelerometer for seven consecutive days and provide a copy of their most recent lipid and glucose laboratory test results. Participants were classified as active if engaged in ≥150 min/wk of moderate to vigorous physical activity (MvPA). Waist circumference, height and weight were measured; and questions were asked regarding smoking behavior and previous day diet. Results: Means and standard deviations of glucose, triglyceride and cholesterol were: 105.1±48.0 mg/dl, 209.7±110.3 mg/dl, and 187.6±53.9 mg/dl, respectively. Elevated levels of glucose (>125 mg/dl), triglycerides (>200 mg/dl) and cholesterol (> 200 mg/dl) were observed in 3 (8%), 17 (45%), and 10 (26%) participants, respectively. Blood lipid and glucose levels were not significantly different between those classified as physically active (29%) and those classified as inactive (71%). There were no significant associations between blood lipids and glucose levels and BMI, waist circumference, weight, or smoking behavior. However, participants with elevated triglycerides had a significantly higher energy intake vs. energy expenditure (752.9±511.3 Kcal/d) compared to those with normal triglyceride levels (260.8±243.3 Kcal/d). Conclusion: The minimal recommended level of MVPA/wk was not protective against lipid disorders in the group of HIV+ Hispanic adult participants, particularly when physical activity is unstructured and no dietary intervention is provided

This study was supported by NIH/NCRR 5 R25 RR17589 and NIH/NCI P20 CA096257.

# Central Adiposity is a Stronger Predictor of CRP Than Aerobic Fitness in Healthy Older Adults

Rudy J. Valentine, Victoria J. Vieira, Ellen M. Evans, FACSM, Jeffrey A. Woods, FACSM. University of Illinois, Urbana, IL.

Cardiorespiratory fitness and obesity have been associated with serum C-reactive protein (CRP); however, the relative contribution of fitness and fatness to CRP is not clearly defined, Moreover, central adiposity and reductions in appendicular Iean mass (aLM) have been linked to elevated levels of CRP in the elderly.

puRposE: The primary purpose of this study was to determine the independent relationships between aerobic fitness, fatness, central adiposity and CRP. A secondary aim was to evaluate the relation between alM and CRP.

METHoDS: Healthy sedentary adults (N = 85, M, n=32, F, n=53; 70.4 ± 5.2 y) who were free from corticosteroid use, inflammatory disease, recent illness and smoking were assessed for aerobic fitness (expressed as relative to body mass or fat-free mass) via a maximal oxygen consumption treadmill test, body composition via dual energy X-ray absorptiometry (DXA) and serum hs-CRP via ELISA. Relative aLM was calculated using a sarcopenia index (SI = aLM/ht²2),

REsuLTS: On average (M ± SD), subjects were overweiqht (BMI = 28.2 ± 4.9 kg/m²2), low fit (19.3 ± 4.1 mL·kgBM-min-1 and 30.1 ± 5.0 mL·kgFFM.min-1), hiqh risk for inflammation (CRP = 3.5 ± 2.9 mg/L) and low risk for sarcopenia (SI = 7.7 ± 1.5 kg/m²). Whole body fatness, expressed as total fat mass or %Fat, trunk fat and fitness were all related to CRP (all p < 0.01). Using stepwise linear regression, controlling for age and sex, only trunk fat and fitness, expressed relative to FFM, were independent predictors of CRP in the model (R2 = 20.3%) explaining 13.6% (p = 0.002) and 6.6% (p = 0.011) respectively, whereas total fat mass (p = 0.48) or %Fat (p = 0.58) were not predictors. S1 was not correlated with CRP (r = 0.17, p = 0.13), which held consistent when controlling for age, gender and %Fat (r = 0.10, p = 0.36).

coNcLusIoNs: Central adiposity and fitness are independent predictors of CRP. Importantly, central adiposity was associated with CRP independently of total adiposity The lack of an independent relationship between SI and CRP is likely impacted by the robust sample of healthy elderly individuals who were not high risk for sarcopenia or sarcopenic obesity. These findings support the measure of central adiposity to assess risk of inflammation.

## Diabetes is Associated with Alterations in the Dystrophin Glycoprotein Complex Composition in the Heart Muscle

Sarath Meduru², Devashish H. Desai², Kevin M. Rice³, M Taimoor Gill², Paulette S. Wehner2 Eric R. Blough³. 1Marshall University, Huntington, WV. 2Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Marshall University, Huntington, WV. 3Marshall University, and Joan C. Edwards School of Medicine, Marshall University, Huntington, WV.

BAckGRouND: Obesity and diabetes pose a major risk for cardiovascular disease and are associated with an increased incidence of heart failure. Myocardial dystrophin disruption has been shown to be a major cause of advanced heart failure. Whether diabetes is associated with the dystrophin glycoprotein complex (DGC) composition in the myocardium is not known.

puRposE: We compared the expression of various components of the DGC in hearts of normal lean and obese Zucker rats, an established model of syndrome-X, exhibiting type I diabetes.

METHoDs: Immunoblotting and immunohistochemical analyses were performed on cel membrane and cytosolic fractions of hearts obtained from normal lean Zucker (LNZ) rats and diabetic obese Zucker (Osxz) rats to examine the expression and localization of components of the DGC.

REsuLTS: Immunoblot analysis revealed markedly higher cytoplasmic dystrophin content (39.95 ± 3.7% over control) as compared to control lean hearts, with no significant difference in the membrane dystrophin content. The content of a-dystroglycan was 35.99 ± 2.9% and 34.74 ± 2.5% higher in the membrane and cytosolic fractions of the OSXZ hearts as compared to the LNZ hearts. The cytosolic content of B-dystroglycan was 49.84 ± 6.4% higher in the OSXZ hearts as compared to LNZ hearts, while the membrane content was 24.82% higher.

coNcLusIoN: These preliminary data suggest a difference in composition of the DGC between the normal and syndrome-X Zucker rat hearts. (Supported by funds from NSF Grant 0314742)

## Metabolic

# Training-induced Adaptation in Glucose Tolerance In Inbred Rats

Abraham D. Lee, Sumona Ghosh, George T. Cicila. The University of Toledo, Toledo, OH. Email: ablee@meduohio.edu

PuRposE: The purpose of the study was to determine if 1) training-induced adaptive change in glucose tolerance would depend on genetic factors and 2) training-induced change in muscle oxidative potential would be associated with change in glucose tolerance

METHoDs: Two inbred strains of rats (DA=15 rats & COP= 13 rats) with different genetic background were divided into control and training groups. Rats in the training group underwent swim training regimen, which consisted of two 3-hour long bouts separated by a 45-min long rest period, 6 days/wk for 4 weeks. At the completion of the training, rats in both groups underwent a glucose tolerance test. Blood glucose level was determined using a glucometer before and at 5, 10, 20, 50 and 75 minutes after i.p. glucose injection (2g/kg BW). The activity of citrate synthase (Cs) in red and white gastrocnemius, soleus, anc eipitrochlearis was determined at 25C. The level of glucose tolerance was determined by calculating the area under curve (AuC) using a trapezoid rule.

REsuLTS: The training-induced improvement in alucose tolerance was 58% (P<0.001) in DA and 25% (P<0.01) in COP without difference between the two strains in the control groups. Glucose tolerance in the trained DA was significantly better than that in the trained COP, showing the AUC in the trained DA was significantly lower (47%, P<0.001) than that in the trained COP. CS activity in red muscles (red gastrocnemius and soleus) was increased significantly in both DA (36-59%, P<0.01) and COP (42%, P<0.01). There was no change in CS in epitrochlearis in both strains but a significant increase in white gastrocnemius in COP (47%, P<0.05) not in DA

coNcLusIoNs: The results demonstrate that training-induced improvement in glucose tolerance depends on genetic factors and a change in oxidative potential in skeletal muscle is not parallel with training-induced change in glucose tolerance.

# Skeletal Muscle Insulin Resistance in Rats Fed a High Fat Diet and Treated with Acipimox

Chad R. Hancock, David C. Wright, Dong Ho Han, John O. Holloszy. Washington University in St. Louis. St. Louis, MO Email: chancock@im.wustl.edu

The mechanism by which a high fat diet causes insulin resistance is not vet understood. It has been proposed by some investigators that elevations in the circulating levels of free fatty acids are responsible for the development of insulin resistance

puRposE: The purpose of this study was to determine if the skeletal muscle insulin resistance induced by a high fat diet would persist in the context of a weeklong treatment to reduce plasma FFAs with acipimox.

METHods: Rats were fed standard chow or a high fat diet in which 50% of calories come from fat (lard and corn oil) for a period of 4 weeks. During the 5th week, a subset of the rats fed a high fat diet were given 2 doses (100mg/kg) per day of Acipimox, which inhibits lypolysis and reduces plasma FFA concentrations. Glucose uptake, Glucose tolerance, fat pad weights, and plasma FFA were measured to determine the metabolic profile and insulin resistance in these animals

REsULTS: the concentration of plasma FFA's were reduced in response to Acipimox treatment in high fat fed rats (0.75±0.08 and 0.38±0.07 mM in High fat fed and High fat+acipimox, respectively). Whole animal glucose tolerance was improved with acipimox treatment, and was not significantly different from that of the chow animals. Skeletal muscle insulin resistance was evident in the animals fed a high fat diet alone as well as rats that received acipimox. The insulin stimulated 2-Deoxvalucose uptake in the epitrochlearis muscle was 1.17±0.11, 0.82±0.11, and 0.68±0.10 μmol 2DG/ml/20min in chow, HF and Acip+HF groups respectively. High fat feeding caused a significant increase in total abdominal fat pad weights and acipimox treatment caused a further increase in fat pad mass (7.01 ±0.32. 12.80±0.71 and 15.75±0.43 ams fat in Chow. High Fat and High Fat + acipimox, respectively).

coNcLusIoN: Lowering of plasma FFA with Acipimox improved overall insulin action, yet did not improve insulin resistance measured in epitrochlearis muscle.

## Metabolic

# The Impact of Obesity, Muscle Contraction, and Insulin on Skeletal Muscle Lipids, A Metabolomic Approach

John P. Thyfault², Melanie G. Cree², Jill A. Bell³3, Jennifer J. Zwetsloot²³, Timoth R. Koves4, Robert R. Wolfe², Deborah M. Muoio, G. Lynis Dohm³. University of Missouri and Harry S. Truman VA Hospital, Columbia, MO. University of Texas Medica! Branch, Galveston, TX. 3East Carolina University, Greenville, NC. 4Duke University, Durham, NC. Email: thyfaultj@missouri.edu

Using hindlimb perfusions and metabolic analysis by mass spectrometry, we examined changes in several specific intramuscular (whole gastrocnemius) lipid pools in lean and obese Zucker rats following acute stimulation by contraction, insulin, or contraction + insulin. Both contraction and surprisingly, insulin, lowered intramuscular triglyceride (TAG) (\~25%) and diacylglycerol (DAG) (30-70%) content in lean and obese rats. Contraction + insulin had an additive effect on lowering TAG and DAG in muscle of obese rats, but had nc effect on levels in lean counterparts. Contraction did not significantly alter total long chain acyl-CoA (LCACoA) levels in either group; however, insulin alone and contraction + insulin increased LCACoA (\~20%) in muscle of obese. Profiling of mitochondrial-derived acylcarnitine esters suggested increased fatty acid supply and β-oxidative flux in mitochondria of obese compared to lean animals under basal conditions. In both lean and obese muscles, contraction caused phosphorylation (inactivation) of acetyl CoA carboxylase (pACC) and a corresponding decrease in malonyl-CoA; conditions that favor high rates of fat oxidation. Accordingly, in lean animals, these contraction-mediated events were accompanied by elevations in most fatty acylcarnitine species, consistent with increased catabolism of lipid substrate. In contrast, the initially high levels of acylcarnitines in obese muscles were either decreased or unchanged with contraction, possibly due to enhanced TCA activity that enabled a complete oxidation of the heavy fatty acid load. Finally, acylcarnitine profiling of the contraction + insulin condition revealed a complex dynamic that was distinct between the lean and obese states. These results provide a nove lipidomic view of skeletal muscle from lean and obese rats challenged by contrasting physiological stimuli.

49

# Increased Fat Mass Occurs Independently of Caloric Intake During Inactivity

Matthew ]. Laye, Frank Booth, FACSM. University of Missouri - Columbia, Columbia, MO Email: milxr9@mizzou.edu

puRPosE: Increased intra-abdominal adipose is associated with insulin resistance diabetes, and cardiovascular disease. Previously, we have determined inducing inactivity for 53 hours after 21 days of voluntary running results in a 25% and 48% in epididymal and omental fat pad weights, respectively, while continuing to eat more than a group that never had access to a running wheel (J. Physiol. 565:911-25, 2005). We wanted to test the hypothesis that inactivity, alone, could induce an increase in fat-pad mass independent of caloric intake.

METHoDs: 21-day old rats were given access to a voluntary running wheel for 42-43 days after which wheels were locked for 5, 53, or 173 hours (WL5, WL53, WL173). During the 53 and 173 hours of inactivity, one group of animals was pair fed (PF) to match sedentary controls while the other continued to eat ad libitum (AL).

REsuLTs: Epididymal, perirenal, and retroperitoneal fat masses where all significantly increased in the WL173AL group compared WL5 group, while epidiymal and retroperitoneal fat masses were significantly increased in the WL173PF versus WL5 group. Additionally, hyperplasia, and not hypertrophy, of the fat mass was responsible for the increase as demonstrated by a sianificant increase in cell number in WL173AL versus WL5, but no accompanying change in cell diameter or volume

coNcLusIoNs: Thus, two important findings have been elucidated: 1) Inactivity, alone, after habitual physical activity causes an increase in fat mass independent of caloric intake and 2) adipocyte expansion via hyperplasia can occur within 7 days.

# The Effects of 10 Days of Endurance Exercise Training on Whole Body Fat Oxidation in Lean and Obese Women

Melissa A. Reed, Jason R. Berggren, Sudip Bajpeyi, Jessica L. Basilio, Joseph A. Houmard, FACSM. East Carolina University, Greenville, NC

puRPosE: The purpose of this study was to measure whole body fat oxidation via indirect calorimetry to determine if obese subjects improve fat oxidation to the same extent as their lean counterparts with ten days of vigorous intensity (\~70-75% VO2peak) endurance exercise training (60 m/day).

METHoDs: Eight obese (BMI 37.7 ± 2.0 kg/m²) and six lean (21.3 ± 0.9 kg/m²) sedentary woren had fat oxidation measured via indirect calorimetry at 15 Watts and 65% of their VO2peak. Whole body fat oxidation was determined using the respiratory exchange ratio (RER) and O2 consumption during minutes 5-9 and 15-19 of an exercise session that was conducted in the morning after an overnight fast. The exercise training consisted of 10 consecutive days of exercise at 75% VO2 peak for 60 min/day on a cycle ergometer; all training was supervised.

REsuLTS: At the 15 Watt workload RER was significantly (P = 0.02) lower in both the lean (0.871 ± 0.016 vs. 0.840 ± 0.014) and obese (0.858 ± 0.018 vs. 0.814 ± 0.017) groups pre- vs. post- training, respectively. This finding was similar at the 65% VO2peak workload as RER significantly (P ≤ 0.05) decreased in both (lean; 0.990 ± 0.017 vs. 0.977 ± 0.020; obese; 0.966 ± 0.017 vs. 0.927 ± 0.022) groups after training. Following training, at 15 Watts, fat oxidation (g/min) significantly increased (P = 0.0061) in the lean (0.0130 ± 0.018 vs. 0.161 ± 0.021) and obese (0.170 ± 0.013 vs. 0.220 ± 0.017) qroups. At 65% VO2peak, fat oxidation also significantly increased (P = 0.0065) in the lean (0.034 ± 0.026 vs. 0.083 ± 0.028) and obese (0.082 ± 0.037 vs. 0.184 ± 0.050) groups after ten days of training. Percent of fat utilized significantly increased (P = 0.0039) at the 15 Watt workload following training in the lean (42.359 ± 5.594 vs. 52.638 ± 4.900) and obese (45.871 ± 6.004 vs. 60.768 ± 5.891) groups. Also, at 65% VO2peak, percent of fat utilized significantly increased (P = 0.0400) in the lean (2.694 ± 5.269 vs. 7.201 ± 6.213) and obese (10.625 ± 5.454 vs. 23.649 ± 7.133) groups following ten days of training.

coNcLusIoNs: These results indicate that ten days of vigorous intensity enduranceoriented exercise training can increase fat oxidation to a similar extent in both lean and obese women.

## Metabolic

# Reduced Fatty-Acid Transporters, Diacylglycerol and Ceramide with Metformin and Exercise in Diabetic Female ZDF Rats

Angela C. Smith1, Kerry L. Mullen², Kathryn A. Junkin², Adrian Chabowski², Arend Bonen1, David J. Dyck². 1University of Guelph, Guelph, ON, Canada. 2Medical University of Bialystok, Bialystok, Poland.

Email: asmith09@uoguelph.ca

Derangements in fatty acid (FA) metabolism that relate to insulin resistance in obesity are poorly understood, but appear to involve decreased oxidation and increased accumulation. Both exercise (Ex) and metformin (Met) activate AMPk in skeletal muscle, which may increase FA oxidation and reduce reactive lipid species (ceramide and diacylglycerol (DAG)).

PuRPosE: We investigated whether Met and/or Ex would prevent derangements in glucose homeostasis in the female Zucker diabetic fatty (ZDF) rat, a high-fat diet-induced model of diabetes, and whether improvements would be related to changes in muscle FA metabolism.

METHoDS: Female ZDF lean and ZDF fatty rats were fed a control diet (C, nondiabetogenic), or high-fat diet (HF, 48kcal% fat, diabetogenic) on its own or in combination with Met (500mg/kg, HF-Met), treadmill Ex (HF-Ex), or both Ex and Met (HF-E+M) for 8 wk

RESuLTS: HF rats developed overt hyperglycemia (24.4±2.1mM, P < 0.01) and exhibited a significant decrease in skeletal muscle insulin-stimulated (ins-stim) glucose uptake, increases in the putative FA transporter, FAT/CD36, and total ceramide and DAG content The progression of hyperglycemia was prevented in HF-Met (-30%, P < 0.05), HF-Ex (- 55%, P < 0.05) and HF-E+M (-40%, P < 0.05), but with improvements in ins-stim glucose uptake (+15-30%, P < 0.05) and increased GLUT4 transporters (+25-35%, P < 0.05) seen only with Ex treatments, but not with Met on its own. All ZDF groups had decreased muscle FA oxidation (-24-43%, P < 0.01) and increased triacylglycerol (TAG) incorporation (+47- 51%, P < 0.01) vs lean rats, a proposed factor in the development of insulin resistance anc diabetes. Only modest increases in oxidative enzymes (+12-35%, HF-Ex and HF-E+M, P < 0.05), AMPK protein content (+15-30%, P < 0.05) and PGC-1a (+20-25%, P = 0.01) were observed with training. Importantly, significant reductions in FAT/CD36 (-15-33%, P < 0.05). and total ceramide (-68-225%. P < 0.001) and DAG content (-55-130%. P < 0.001) were observed with all three treatments and may be mechanisms alleviating the FAinduced insulin resistance and diabetes in female ZDF rats.

coNcLusIoNs: Our data suggest that improvements in FA oxidation may not be critical for the prevention of diabetes in this model.

## Associations of Visceral Adiposity with C-Reactive Protein, Insulin Resistance, and Endothelial Dysfunction in Korean dults

Ki Jin Kim, Yoon Jung Shin, Chang Bae Hong, Sang Hyun Kim, Na Young Ahn, Kyung Min Gong. Keimyung University, Daequ, Republic of Korea Email: kik744@kmu.ac.kr

puRPosE: The aim of the current study was to examine the associations between hsCRP insulin resistance, body fatness, abdominal adiposity, and endothelial dysfunction in Korean adults selected from the general population.

METHoDS: Using a cross-sectional approach, we studied 160 Korean adults (aged 41.3±13.0 yrs n=38 males and n=122 females) who volunteered in a health promotion program. Subjects were divided into 2 groups based upon spontaneous exercise participation, We measured anthropometric factors (BMl, total body percent fat. WHR. and abdominal fat area by CT scanning), BP, blood levels of glucose, lipids, fibrinogen, hsCRP. leptin, HbA1c, HOMA, and intima thickness of left carotid artery (LCA ; via ultrasonography), Associations among the variables were assessed by Pearson's partial correlation and linear regression, controlling for age. Independent t-tests were used to assess differences between exercise participants and non participants. Significance was accepted at p<0.05.

REsULTS: As expected, the measures of adiposity (BMI, percent fat, WHR, abdominal fat area) were highly correlated with each other (r=,49-86, p<0.01). Blood levels of hsCRP. leptin, and HOMÁ were significantly correlated with all measures of adiposity. Visceral fat area was the most important predictor of hsCRP, explaining 11.3% of the variance in stepwise linear reqression analysis (p<0.01). As visceral fat area tertiles increased from low to high, a significant stepwise increment in blood levels of hsCRP (p=0.043) and HOMA (p=0.0o9) were observed. However, hsCRP and HOMA were not significantly different when compared across whole body fat tertiles. SBP, DBP, and LCA intimal thickness were significantly correlated with WHR and visceral fat area (p<0.05), but SBP and DBP were also correlated with BMI and percent body fat (p<0.o5), so the relative importance of central adiposity as opposed to total body fatness in endothelial dysfunction is unclear. Compared with the non-exercise group, exercise participants had significantly lower (p<0.05) WHR, visceral fat area, ratio of visceral fat area to subcutaneous area, hsCRP, and HoMA with no significant differences in BMI, total body percent fat, and physical fitnss.

coNcLusIoN: Central obesity with high visceral fat is strongly associated with blood level of hsCRP, insulin resistance, and endothelial dysfunction-related factors in healthy Korean adults. Additionally, exercise participation, even in the absence of difference in physical fitness, can be protective against development of central obesity and insulin resistance in this understudied Korean population.

## Metabolic

## Is hypertriglyceridemia during physical inactivity a component of endothelial dysfunction?

Perminder Gulani, Marc T. Hamilton. University of Missouri-Columbia, Columbia, MO Email: pg424@mizzou.edu

Lipoprotein lipase (LPL) is an enzyme present on the vascular endothelium which hydrolyzes triglyceride rich plasma lipoproteins. The interesting feature of this protein is that while it is synthesized in muscle fibers, it is functional when bound to the luminal surface of the endothelium. A major question that has not been answered as of yet is whether LPL binding to the microvascular endothelium of muscle is a key regulatory step for determining muscle LPL activity, especially in response to physical inactivity, the most powerful suppressor of microvascular endothelial bound LPL activity in skeletal muscle.

PUrposE: To determine if physical inactivity has a significant effect on the LPL binding ability of microvascular endothelium in skeletal muscle, We tested the hypothesis that the ability of the microvascular endothelium in skeletal muscle to bind LPL would be lower after physical inactivity.

METHoDS: Tyrosine residues of the LPL were iodinated. Enzymatically active dimeric LPL was purified by heparin sepharose chromatography. The5I-labeled LPL was injected intravenously into the jugular vein of anaesthetized rats after acutely reducing contractile activity locally in the hindlimbs (< 24 h) or after ambulation.

REsuLTS: The dimeric 1251-labeled LPL rapidly bound to the skeletal muscle vasculature (>go% complete in 10 min), A subset of experiments indicated that the tracer was behaving similar to endogenous LPL because there was a striking relationship between endogenous endothelial bound LPL activity in muscles and the ability of 175I-labeled LPL to bind to the endothelium (R² =0.86, P<0.0001). Most interestingly, the fraction of 1251-LPL that bound to muscles after phvsical inactivity was sianificantly lower than that after ambulation e.g. the fraction that bound to red oxidative muscle (soleus) was \~ 50% (P=0.03) lower after physical inactivity than after ambulation, 0.11±0.01% compared with 0.21±0.03% of injected dose. Furthermore, reduction in binding was specific to the muscles whose contractile activity was decreased and not a systemic effect because several other tissues (heart, adipose, aorta) known to bind LPL were not affected by reduced contractile activity in hindlimbs.

cONcLusIoN: These studies indicate that the binding of exogenous LPL to vascular endothelium accounts for 86% of the variance in rat skeletal muscle LPL activity and physical inactivity causes a change in microvascular endothelium in skeletal muscle such that its ability to bind LPL decreases

# The Instigation of Multiple, Divergent Metabolic Pathways by a Single Bout Exercise Protocol in Adults

Vincent J. Bocchicchio, Robert F. Foster, John W. Bass, Michael B. Foster. Sports Conditioning Clinic, Phoenix, AZ. Email: drbenbo@hotmail.com

The purpose of this study was to measure the efficacy of a new model of exercise. Historically, the literature has established mechanical models that correlate to specific metabolic responses. The data presented here challenge some aspects of those models Methods: 100 healthy, adult males and females (18 to 72) were randomly selected and placed into 2 groups for a 5 week study.

The (NM) group performed a supervised series of 7, slow speed, resistance exercises (taken to failure) 2X weekly for an average of 15 minutes per session. The (C) group performed a variety of cardiovascular (target range, 60% - 80% Max h.r.) exercises, recorded daily for an average of 3.5 hours weekly.

A one -way Analysis of Variance (ANOvA) was conducted to assess differences between the New Model (NM) and Cardio (C) participants on pretreatment scores and a series of Paired-Sample T-Tests were were conducted for examination of outcomes for both groups.

ANCOVA were used to compare group results.

Nutritional information was provided to all subjects.

RESULTS: ANCOVA revealed that the (NM) group significantly exceeded the (C) group in measurements of: Improved body composition, cardio respiratory endurance, upper body and lower body strength, trunk flexibility, decreased resting blood pressure and heart rate (All: p <.001).

DIscussIoN: Perhaps the most significant hypothesis proposed by this study is that multiple metabolic pathways (aerobic to anaerobic), previously considered to be inhibitory, can, in fact, be instigated simultaneously and perhaps synergistically. It is hypothesized that one. specific protocol (NM) performed twice weekly for 15 minutes miaht lead to enhanced exercise adherence in adult populations.

## Pulmonary

## Asthma and SCUBA Diving: A Relative Contraindication?

Clayton A. Everline. Seton Hall University GME, Short Hills, NJ

INTRoDucTIoN: More than 7% of the population has been diagnosed with asthma, which is similar to the percentage of divers admitting they have asthma, Numerous concerns exist regarding medically contraindicating subjects with asthma from ScuBA diving. This article examines the currently available literature to allow for a more informed decision regarding the possible risks associated with diving and asthma. A new marketeting campaign for a submersible metered dose albuterol inhaler may give asthmatics the wrong impression that uncontrolled asthma is not a contraindication to ScuBA

METHoDs: PubMed and Google were searched for papers between 2002-2006. Keywords used for the search were 'asthma', 'respiratory atopy', 'SCUBA', and 'diving'. Additional references were reviewed from the bibliographies of received articles. Product literature for the MediDive reaulator (with submersible metered-dose albuterol inhaler) was also reviewed.

REsuLTS: The data showed a high prevalence of asthma among recreational SCUBA divers, similar to the prevalence of asthma among the general population. There was some minimal evidence for an increase in rates of decompression illness among divers with asthma. In non-asthmatic participants, wet hyperbaric chamber and open-water diving led to a decrease in forced vital capacity, forced expired volume over 1.0 second and midexpiratory flow rates. In participants with asymptomatic respiratory atopy, diving was shown to cause a decrease in airway conductivity

DIscussIoN: Additional data are needed to define accurately risks of diving in subjects with different forms of asthma, howeyer, the available data suggest asthmatic patients with normal airway function at rest, and with little airway reactivity in response to exercise or cold air inhalation, have a risk of pulmonary barotrauma similar to that of normal subjects. No studies have shown benefit or harm from use of a submersible metered-dose albuterol inhaler. However, the current literature suggests that asthma requiring use of a metered dose albuterol inhaler within 48 hours of diving is a relative contraindication tc ScuBA. The decision as to whether an asthmatic patient should be allowed to dive rests on the individual's airway function and insight into the consequences of a poorly managed respiratory condition.

57

## Pulmonary

# Ozone-Induced Alterations in Regional Airway Function During Exercise in Smokers Versus Non-Smokers

Melissa Lowe Bates, Timothy Brenza, Abdellaziz Ben-Jebria, James Ultman. The Pennsylvania State University, University Park, PA. Email: mal361@psu.edu

PuRposE: The acute inhalation of ozone (O3) by healthy non-smokers compromises lung function during exercise as measured by forced expiratory volume in one second (FEV1) Paradoxically, cigarette smokers have exhibited little to no decrement in FEV under similar conditions. We hypothesize that smoking-induced changes in the epithelial lining layer, such as increased thickness or lower antioxidant capacity, may allow O to penetrate deeper into the lungs of smokers versus non-smokers, thereby reducing the airway responses that contribute to O3-induced decrements in FEV1. Thus, smoking may alter markers of distal respiratory airway function, notably the normalized slope (NS) of the CO; expirogram.

METHoDS: We recruited 13 smokers (10M, 3F, 24±4 years, 3.7±2.3 pack-years, 3.6±2.0 packs/wk) and 11 non-smokers (6M, 5F, 27±6 years) with normal lung function, who were not obese and had no history of respiratory or cardiovascular disease. Subjects exercised for one hour on a cycle ergometer while breathing 0.3 ppm O3 at a rate equal to 15 liters per minute times body surface area. Before and after O exposure subjects completed lung function tests and a series of breaths from which the CO expirograms were obtained REsuLTS: Non-smokers demonstrated a decrease in FEV, (-9.2% ± 1.7. p = 0.03). Smokers demonstrated a similar decrease in FEV1 (-11.0% ± 2.9, p<0.01) compared to non-smokers. While non-smokers failed to demonstrate a change in NS (-0.7% ± 4.7, p = 0.89), smokers did demonstrate an increase in NS (14.8% ± 6.1, p = 0.03) that was correlated with pack-year smoking history (r2 = 0.45, p = 0.01). There was no relationship between changes in FEV and pack-vear smoking history (r² = 0.03, p = 0.53)

coNcLusIoN: These results suggest that smokers are responsive to O both in the conducting and respiratory regions of the lung whereas non-smokers are primarily responsive in the conducting airways. Additionally, smokers with a higher pack-year history are more susceptible to changes in the respiratory region than smokers with a lower packyear history or non-smokers. This may have an important impact on gas exchange and, therefore, affect the ability of smokers to exercise in the presence of O3

58

# The Self-Contained Breathing Apparatus (SCBA) Influences Pulmonary Function and Respiratory Muscle Performance during Exercise

Stewart R. Petersen, Scott J. Butcher, Jon R. Mayne, Tim C. Hartley, Richard L. Jones. University of Alberta, Edmonton, AB, Canada. Email; stewart.petersen@ualberta.ca

PuRposE: Previous work in our lab has shown that the increased external expiratory resistance of the ScBA regulator increases lung volumes and respiratory muscle work during heavy exercise, causing a ventilatory limitation and the potential for respiratory muscle fatigue. The purpose of the present study was to further examine the impact of the SCBA-imposed respiratory load on work of breathing, respiratory muscle function, and pulmonary function.

METHoDs: Twelve men (31 ± 8.4 yr) completed one graded step test in firefighting gear and breathing from the SCBA, then two randomized exercise sessions on separate days, each consisting of three 10 minute bouts of stepping exercise at 80% of maximal stepping cadence separated by 5 minutes recovery. Subjects wore protective gear including the SCBA for both sessions. The sessions consisted of breathing from (1) the SCBA regulator (BA) and (2) a low resistance breathing valve (RV). Spirometry was performed at baseline and in both the BA and RV conditions. Maximal inspiratory (MIP) and expiratory (MEP mouth pressures were recorded before and within 5 minutes after exercise. During exercise, heart rate, ventilation, esophageal pressure, lung volume, and work of breathing

REsuLTS: The protective gear including the SCBA decreased FVC, FEV and peak expiratory flow (PEFR) compared to baseline (p<0.001) in both conditions; however, the BA decreased FEVi (p<0.05) and PEFR (p<0.01) to a greater degree than the RV.

<table><tr><td>Condition</td><td>FVC (L)</td><td>FEV: (L)</td><td>PEFR (L/sec)</td></tr><tr><td>Baseline</td><td>5.69</td><td>4.32</td><td>12.10</td></tr><tr><td>BA</td><td>5.52</td><td>4.02</td><td>9.65</td></tr><tr><td>RV</td><td>5.50</td><td>4.17</td><td>11.32</td></tr></table>

There were no differences in heart rate or ventilation during exercise. After 30 minutes of stepping exercise, the BA resulted in a decreased inspiratory capacity (3.16 vs. 3.39, p<0.01) and an increased total (2129 vs.1427 cmH-O·L·min-1, p<0.001), expiratory resistive (240 vs. 117 cmH2O·L·min1, p<0.001), and inspiratory elastic (1286 vs. 81e cmH2O-L-min1, p<0.001) work of breathing compared with the RV. Post exercise MEP and MIP were reduced with the BA (by 14.0 % and 12.3 %, respectively, p<0.001), but not the RV (5.5 % and -0.01 %, respectively).

coNcLusIoNs: Firefighting protective gear including the SCBA reduces resting pulmonary function, and increases exercising lung volumes, work of breathing, and respiratory muscle fatigue during stepping exercise. The results of this study suggest that a significant impairment of respiratory muscle function is likely present during heavy firefighting work and might lead to a reduction in respiratory muscle performance.
